supervision: Dict[str, Any]
class InMemoryPersistence:
def __init__(self) -> None:
self.objects: Dict[str, A03Base] = {}
self.snapshots: Dict[str, Dict[str, str]] = {}
self.quarantine_reasons: Dict[str, str] = {}
self.published: Dict[str, str] = {}
def put(self, obj: A03Base) -> str:
obj.seal()
if obj.meta.object_id in self.objects:
existing = self.objects[obj.meta.object_id]
if existing.meta.canonical_hash != obj.meta.canonical_hash:
raise ValidationError(f"Object id collision with divergent hash: {obj.meta.object_id}")
self.objects[obj.meta.object_id] = copy.deepcopy(obj)
return obj.meta.object_id
def get(self, object_id: str) -> A03Base:
return copy.deepcopy(self.objects[object_id])
def put_state(self, state: StateObject) -> str:
return self.put(state)
def get_state(self, object_id: str) -> StateObject:
obj = self.get(object_id)
if not isinstance(obj, StateObject):
raise TypeError(f"Object {object_id} is not a StateObject")
return obj
def put_route(self, route: RouteObject) -> str:
return self.put(route)
def get_route(self, route_id: str) -> RouteObject:
obj = self.get(route_id)
if not isinstance(obj, RouteObject):
raise TypeError(f"Object {route_id} is not a RouteObject")
return obj
def put_witness(self, witness: WitnessPacket) -> str:
return self.put(witness)
def get_witness(self, witness_id: str) -> WitnessPacket:
obj = self.get(witness_id)
if not isinstance(obj, WitnessPacket):
raise TypeError(f"Object {witness_id} is not a WitnessPacket")
return obj
def propose_patch(self, patch: PatchPacket) -> str:
return self.put(patch)
def apply_patch(self, patch_id: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
patch = self.get(patch_id)
if not isinstance(patch, PatchPacket):
raise TypeError(f"Object {patch_id} is not a PatchPacket")
if patch.meta.policy.mutability not in {Mutability.APPLY_OK, Mutability.APPLY_NEAR}:
raise ValidationError(f"Patch {patch_id} is not allowed to apply under current mutability")
target_snapshot = new_id("snapshot")
self.snapshots[target_snapshot] = {
"base": patch.base_snapshot,
"patch_id": patch.patch_id,
"hash": patch.meta.canonical_hash,
}
return {"status": "APPLIED", "target_snapshot": target_snapshot}
def rollback_patch(self, patch_id: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
patch = self.get(patch_id)
if not isinstance(patch, PatchPacket):
raise TypeError(f"Object {patch_id} is not a PatchPacket")
return {"status": "ROLLED_BACK", "patch_id": patch_id, "rollback_contract": patch.rollback.rollback_contract}
def create_replay(self, replay: ReplayPacket) -> str:
return self.put(replay)
def execute_replay(self, replay_id: str) -> ReplayPacket:
replay = self.get(replay_id)
if not isinstance(replay, ReplayPacket):
raise TypeError(f"Object {replay_id} is not a ReplayPacket")
if replay.expectation.expected_output_hash:
replay.result.replay_status = ReplayStatus.SUCCESS
replay.result.obtained_output_hash = replay.expectation.expected_output_hash
replay.result.obtained_truth_lattice = replay.expectation.expected_truth_lattice
replay.result.drift_score = 0.0
else:
replay.result.replay_status = ReplayStatus.PARTIAL
replay.result.divergence_reasons.append("missing expected_output_hash")
replay.seal()
self.objects[replay.meta.object_id] = replay
return replay
def snapshot(self, scope: str, ids: Sequence[str]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
snapshot_id = new_id("snapshot")
snapshot = {obj_id: self.objects[obj_id].meta.canonical_hash for obj_id in ids if obj_id in self.objects}
snapshot["scope"] = scope
self.snapshots[snapshot_id] = snapshot
return {
"snapshot_id": snapshot_id,
"snapshot_hash": _hash_bytes(canonical_json(snapshot).encode("utf-8")),
"object_count": len(ids),
}
def query_neighborhood(self, seed_addresses: Sequence[str], profile: str = "default") -> List[str]:
out: List[str] = []
for obj in self.objects.values():
if obj.meta.address.global_addr in seed_addresses:
out.append(obj.meta.object_id)
return out
def list_lineage(self, object_id: str) -> List[str]:
obj = self.get(object_id)
return list(obj.meta.lineage.parent_ids)
def quarantine(self, object_id: str, reason: str) -> bool:
self.quarantine_reasons[object_id] = reason
return True
def publish(self, bundle_id: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
self.published[bundle_id] = now_utc_rfc3339()
return {"publish_receipt": bundle_id, "published_at": self.published[bundle_id]}
@runtime_checkable
class Planner(Protocol):
def plan(self, state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> Tuple[List[RouteObject], float]:
...
@runtime_checkable
class Perception(Protocol):
def observe(self, state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> Optional[ObservationObject]:
...
@runtime_checkable
class Synthesizer(Protocol):
def synthesize(self, state: StateObject, route: RouteObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> StateObject:
...
@runtime_checkable
class Verifier(Protocol):
def verify(
self,
target: A03Base,
target_kind: TargetKind,
store: InMemoryPersistence,
replay_required: bool = False,
) -> WitnessPacket:
...
@runtime_checkable
class Worker(Protocol):
def execute(self, plan: Sequence[ToolStep], state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> ActionTraceObject:
...
@runtime_checkable
class Patcher(Protocol):
def propose(
self,
source_state: StateObject,
solution_state: StateObject,
route: RouteObject,
witness: WitnessPacket,
store: InMemoryPersistence,
) -> PatchPacket:
...
class GreedyPlanner:
def plan(self, state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> Tuple[List[RouteObject], float]:
candidates = state.neighborhood.seed_addresses or [state.meta.address.global_addr]
routes: List[RouteObject] = []
for i, addr in enumerate(candidates[:5], start=1):
r = make_route_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="planner.greedy", actor_role=ActorRole.PLANNER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
source_state_id=state.meta.object_id,
target_contract=state.query.target_contract.output_type,
nodes=[addr],
bridge_types=[BridgeType.REF],
route_score=max(0.0, 1.0 - (i - 1) * 0.1),
contradiction_risk=min(1.0, 0.1 * (i - 1)),
replay_cost=0.1 * i,
expected_evidence_gain=max(0.0, 0.9 - (i - 1) * 0.1),
novelty_gain=0.05 * i,
)
r.search_profile.relevance_score = r.search_profile.route_score
r.posterior.posterior_prob = max(0.0, 1.0 - (i - 1) * 0.15)
r.posterior.confidence_surface = max(0.0, 0.85 - (i - 1) * 0.1)
r.posterior.update_reason = "seed-address heuristic"
store.put_route(r)
routes.append(r)
entropy = 0.0 if len(routes) <= 1 else min(
1.0, sum(r.search_profile.contradiction_risk for r in routes) / len(routes)
)
return routes, entropy
class NullPerception:
def observe(self, state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> Optional[ObservationObject]:
return None
class EchoSynthesizer:
def synthesize(self, state: StateObject, route: RouteObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> StateObject:
solution = make_state_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="synth.echo", actor_role=ActorRole.SYNTHESIZER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
state_type=StateType.SOLUTION_STATE,
raw_input=state.query.raw_input,
canonical_problem=state.query.canonical_problem,
task_class=state.query.task_class,
)
solution.query.target_contract = copy.deepcopy(state.query.target_contract)
solution.neighborhood = copy.deepcopy(state.neighborhood)
solution.lens_state = copy.deepcopy(state.lens_state)
solution.uncertainty = copy.deepcopy(state.uncertainty)
solution.meta.lineage.parent_ids = [state.meta.object_id, route.meta.object_id]
solution.fingerprints.semantic_fingerprint = route.route_id
solution.fingerprints.state_fingerprint = _hash_bytes(
f"{state.meta.object_id}:{route.route_id}:{state.query.canonical_problem}".encode("utf-8")
)
solution.self_model.region_role = "compiled_solution"
solution.query.target_contract.completion_criterion = "scheduler_return_solution_state"
store.put_state(solution)
return solution
class BasicVerifier:
def verify(
self,
target: A03Base,
target_kind: TargetKind,
store: InMemoryPersistence,
replay_required: bool = False,
) -> WitnessPacket:
canonical_repr = target.canonical_json(include_hash=False)
canonical_hash_check = True
residuals: List[str] = []
defect_x = defect_y = defect_z = 0.0
truth = TruthLattice.OK
confidence = 0.90
risk = 0.10
repairable = False
repair_hints: List[str] = []
try:
target.validate()
except Exception as exc:
truth = TruthLattice.FAIL
canonical_hash_check = False
residuals.append(f"validation_error:{exc}")
defect_x = defect_y = defect_z = 1.0
confidence = 0.25
risk = 0.95
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("repair invalid structure or address")
if isinstance(target, PatchPacket):
if target.risk_trust.patch_risk_score > target.risk_trust.quarantine_if_above:
truth = TruthLattice.FAIL
residuals.append("patch_risk_exceeds_quarantine_threshold")
defect_x = 1.0
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("lower patch risk or increase evidence")
elif target.risk_trust.change_uncertainty > 0.50:
truth = TruthLattice.NEAR
residuals.append("patch uncertainty elevated")
defect_y = target.risk_trust.change_uncertainty
confidence = 0.60
risk = max(risk, 0.45)
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("add more witness support before apply")
if isinstance(target, RouteObject):
if target.search_profile.contradiction_risk > 0.80:
truth = TruthLattice.FAIL
residuals.append("route contradiction risk too high")
defect_z = target.search_profile.contradiction_risk
confidence = 0.30
risk = 0.90
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("select alternative route")
elif target.search_profile.contradiction_risk > 0.40:
truth = TruthLattice.NEAR
residuals.append("route contradiction risk moderate")
defect_z = target.search_profile.contradiction_risk
confidence = 0.65
risk = 0.55
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("counterroute comparison recommended")
if replay_required and target.meta.object_id not in store.objects:
truth = TruthLattice.AMBIG
residuals.append("replay required but target not yet persisted")
repairable = True
repair_hints.append("persist target before replay-bound verification")
witness = make_witness_packet(
atlas_id=target.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=target.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="verifier.basic", actor_role=ActorRole.VERIFIER),
global_addr=target.meta.address.global_addr,
target_object_id=target.meta.object_id,
target_kind=target_kind,
truth_lattice=truth,
confidence=confidence,
risk_score=risk,
canonical_repr=canonical_repr,
canonical_hash_check=canonical_hash_check,
residual_ledger=residuals,
defect_x=defect_x,
defect_y=defect_y,
defect_z=defect_z,
replay_required=replay_required,
repairable=repairable,
repair_hints=repair_hints,
)
store.put_witness(witness)
return witness
class NoopWorker:
def execute(self, plan: Sequence[ToolStep], state: StateObject, store: InMemoryPersistence) -> ActionTraceObject:
traces = [
ToolTrace(step_id=s.step_id, status=StepStatus.SUCCESS, artifact_refs=[], notes=f"simulated:{s.capability.value}")
for s in plan
]
digest = _hash_bytes(canonical_json([asdict(t) for t in traces]).encode("utf-8"))
action = make_action_trace_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="worker.noop", actor_role=ActorRole.WORKER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
step_results=traces,
side_effect_digest=digest,
)
store.put(action)
return action
class BasicPatcher:
def propose(
self,
source_state: StateObject,
solution_state: StateObject,
route: RouteObject,
witness: WitnessPacket,
store: InMemoryPersistence,
) -> PatchPacket:
op = DeltaOp(
op_id=new_id("op"),
op_type="ATTACH_WITNESS",
target_addr=solution_state.meta.address.global_addr,
payload_ref=witness.meta.object_id,
preconditions=["solution_state_exists", "witness_exists"],
postconditions=["solution_state_linked_to_witness"],
)
patch = make_patch_packet(
atlas_id=source_state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=source_state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="patcher.basic", actor_role=ActorRole.PATCHER),
global_addr=source_state.meta.address.global_addr,
base_snapshot=source_state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
target_addresses=[solution_state.meta.address.global_addr],
ops=[op],
)
patch.meta.policy.mutability = Mutability.APPLY_OK
patch.meta.lineage.parent_ids = [source_state.meta.object_id, solution_state.meta.object_id, route.meta.object_id]
patch.witness_refs = [witness.meta.object_id]
patch.approval_verdicts = [witness.verdict.truth_lattice]
if witness.verdict.truth_lattice == TruthLattice.NEAR:
patch.meta.policy.mutability = Mutability.APPLY_NEAR
patch.risk_trust.change_uncertainty = 0.40
patch.risk_trust.patch_risk_score = 0.35
patch.rollback.rollback_trigger_conditions.append("post-apply verification drops below NEAR")
elif witness.verdict.truth_lattice == TruthLattice.OK:
patch.risk_trust.change_uncertainty = 0.10
patch.risk_trust.patch_risk_score = 0.15
else:
patch.risk_trust.change_uncertainty = 0.80
patch.risk_trust.patch_risk_score = 0.90
store.propose_patch(patch)
return patch
def _default_address(global_addr: str) -> Address:
return Address(global_addr=global_addr)
def _default_meta(
object_kind: ObjectKind,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> Meta:
return Meta(
object_kind=object_kind,
object_id=object_id or new_id(object_kind.value.lower()),
canonical_hash="",
atlas_id=atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=atlas_snapshot,
created_at=now_utc_rfc3339(),
created_by=created_by,
address=_default_address(global_addr),
)
def make_state_object(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
state_type: StateType,
raw_input: Optional[str],
canonical_problem: str,
task_class: str,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> StateObject:
obj = StateObject(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.STATE, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
state_type=state_type,
query=QueryBody(raw_input=raw_input, canonical_problem=canonical_problem, task_class=task_class),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_route_object(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
source_state_id: str,
target_contract: str,
nodes: List[str],
bridge_types: List[BridgeType],
route_score: float,
contradiction_risk: float,
replay_cost: float,
expected_evidence_gain: float,
novelty_gain: float,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> RouteObject:
obj = RouteObject(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.ROUTE, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
route_id=new_id("route"),
route_status=RouteStatus.PROPOSED,
endpoints=Endpoints(source_state_id=source_state_id, target_contract=target_contract),
address_path=AddressPath(nodes=nodes),
bridge_laws=BridgeLaws(bridge_types=bridge_types),
search_profile=SearchProfile(
route_score=route_score,
contradiction_risk=contradiction_risk,
replay_cost=replay_cost,
expected_evidence_gain=expected_evidence_gain,
novelty_gain=novelty_gain,
),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_witness_packet(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
target_object_id: str,
target_kind: TargetKind,
truth_lattice: TruthLattice,
confidence: float,
risk_score: float,
canonical_repr: str,
canonical_hash_check: bool,
residual_ledger: List[str],
defect_x: float,
defect_y: float,
defect_z: float,
replay_required: bool,
repairable: bool,
repair_hints: List[str],
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> WitnessPacket:
obj = WitnessPacket(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.WITNESS, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
target_object_id=target_object_id,
target_kind=target_kind,
verdict=Verdict(truth_lattice=truth_lattice, confidence=confidence, risk_score=risk_score),
snap=SnapSection(
canonical_repr=canonical_repr,
canonical_hash_check=canonical_hash_check,
residual_ledger=residual_ledger,
),
tri_lock=TriLockSection(defect_x=defect_x, defect_y=defect_y, defect_z=defect_z),
replay_binding=ReplayBinding(replay_required=replay_required),
repair=RepairSection(repairable=repairable, repair_hints=repair_hints),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_patch_packet(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
base_snapshot: str,
target_addresses: List[str],
ops: List[DeltaOp],
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> PatchPacket:
obj = PatchPacket(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.PATCH, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
patch_id=new_id("patch"),
base_snapshot=base_snapshot,
target_snapshot=None,
target_scope=TargetScope(addresses=target_addresses),
delta=DeltaSection(ops=ops),
rollback=RollbackSection(rollback_snapshot=base_snapshot),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_replay_packet(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
source_state_id: str,
root_query_hash: str,
source_snapshot: str,
expected_output_hash: str,
expected_truth_lattice: TruthLattice,
event_ids: Optional[List[str]] = None,
route_ids: Optional[List[str]] = None,
witness_ids: Optional[List[str]] = None,
patch_ids: Optional[List[str]] = None,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> ReplayPacket:
obj = ReplayPacket(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.REPLAY, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
replay_id=new_id("replay"),
root=ReplayRoot(source_state_id=source_state_id, root_query_hash=root_query_hash, source_snapshot=source_snapshot),
event_chain=EventChain(
event_ids=event_ids or [],
route_ids=route_ids or [],
witness_ids=witness_ids or [],
patch_ids=patch_ids or [],
),
expectation=ExpectationSection(
expected_output_hash=expected_output_hash,
expected_truth_lattice=expected_truth_lattice,
),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_failure_object(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
failure_class: FailureClass,
failed_stage: FailedStage,
severity: FailureSeverity,
failed_object_id: Optional[str] = None,
symptoms: Optional[List[str]] = None,
minimal_counterexample: Optional[str] = None,
recommended_repair: Optional[List[str]] = None,
quarantine_required: bool = False,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> FailureObject:
obj = FailureObject(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.FAILURE, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
failure_class=failure_class,
failed_object_id=failed_object_id,
failed_stage=failed_stage,
severity=severity,
symptoms=symptoms or [],
minimal_counterexample=minimal_counterexample,
recommended_repair=recommended_repair or [],
quarantine_required=quarantine_required,
)
return obj.seal()
def make_observation_object(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
modality: Modality,
local_regions: List[ObservationRegion],
candidate_addresses: Optional[List[str]] = None,
match_scores: Optional[List[float]] = None,
object_id: Optional[str] = None,
) -> ObservationObject:
obj = ObservationObject(
schema_version="a03.v1",
meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.OBSERVATION, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
observation_id=new_id("obs"),
modality=modality,
local_regions=local_regions,
atlas_alignment=AtlasAlignment(
candidate_addresses=candidate_addresses or [],
match_scores=match_scores or [],
),
)
return obj.seal()
def make_action_trace_object(
*,
atlas_id: str,
atlas_snapshot: str,
created_by: CreatedBy,
global_addr: str,
step_results: List[ToolTrace],
side_effect_digest: str,

) -> ActionTraceObject:
obj = ActionTraceObject(

meta=_default_meta(ObjectKind.ACTION_TRACE, atlas_id, atlas_snapshot, created_by, global_addr, object_id),
execution_trace_id=new_id("trace"),
step_results=step_results,
side_effect_digest=side_effect_digest,
)
return obj.seal()
@dataclass
class SolveResult:
status: str
input_state_id: str
solution_state_id: Optional[str] = None
route_id: Optional[str] = None
witness_id: Optional[str] = None
patch_id: Optional[str] = None
replay_id: Optional[str] = None
snapshot_id: Optional[str] = None
failure_id: Optional[str] = None
notes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
class MinimalScheduler:
def __init__(
self,
*,
store: InMemoryPersistence,
planner: Planner,
synthesizer: Synthesizer,
verifier: Verifier,
patcher: Patcher,
perception: Optional[Perception] = None,
worker: Optional[Worker] = None,
publish_policy: PublishPolicy = PublishPolicy.NEVER,
) -> None:
self.store = store
self.planner = planner
self.synthesizer = synthesizer
self.verifier = verifier
self.patcher = patcher
self.perception = perception or NullPerception()
self.worker = worker or NoopWorker()
self.publish_policy = publish_policy
def normalize(self, state: StateObject) -> StateObject:
state.zero_point_normalization.intent_tags = sorted(set(state.zero_point_normalization.intent_tags))
state.zero_point_normalization.boundary_tags = sorted(set(state.zero_point_normalization.boundary_tags))
state.neighborhood.seed_addresses = list(dict.fromkeys(state.neighborhood.seed_addresses or [state.meta.address.global_addr]))
if not state.fingerprints.state_fingerprint:
state.fingerprints.state_fingerprint = _hash_bytes(
f"{state.query.canonical_problem}:{state.query.task_class}".encode("utf-8")
)
if not state.fingerprints.semantic_fingerprint:
state.fingerprints.semantic_fingerprint = _hash_bytes(state.query.canonical_problem.encode("utf-8"))
state.seal()
self.store.put_state(state)
return state
def needs_perception(self, state: StateObject) -> bool:
return any(tag.startswith("needs:") for tag in state.zero_point_normalization.intent_tags)
def requires_execution(self, state: StateObject) -> bool:
return any(tag.startswith("exec:") for tag in state.zero_point_normalization.intent_tags)
def solve_and_learn(self, input_state: StateObject) -> SolveResult:
result = SolveResult(status="STARTED", input_state_id=input_state.meta.object_id)
try:
state = self.normalize(input_state)
if self.needs_perception(state):
obs = self.perception.observe(state, self.store)
if obs is not None:
self.store.put(obs)
state.meta.lineage.parent_ids.append(obs.meta.object_id)
state.neighborhood.active_addresses.extend(obs.atlas_alignment.candidate_addresses)
state.neighborhood.active_addresses = list(dict.fromkeys(state.neighborhood.active_addresses))
state.seal()
self.store.put_state(state)
routes, entropy = self.planner.plan(state, self.store)
if not routes:
failure = make_failure_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="scheduler", actor_role=ActorRole.SCHEDULER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
failure_class=FailureClass.LOOKUP_FAILURE,
failed_stage=FailedStage.PLAN,
severity=FailureSeverity.HIGH,
failed_object_id=state.meta.object_id,
symptoms=["planner returned no routes"],
recommended_repair=["expand seed neighborhood", "add more retrieval hooks"],
)
self.store.put(failure)
result.status = "FAIL"
result.failure_id = failure.meta.object_id
return result
best_route = sorted(
routes,
key=lambda r: (
-(r.search_profile.route_score - r.search_profile.contradiction_risk),
r.search_profile.replay_cost,
),
)[0]
result.route_id = best_route.meta.object_id
solution = self.synthesizer.synthesize(state, best_route, self.store)
result.solution_state_id = solution.meta.object_id
pre_witness = self.verifier.verify(solution, TargetKind.ANSWER, self.store, replay_required=False)
result.witness_id = pre_witness.meta.object_id
if pre_witness.verdict.truth_lattice == TruthLattice.FAIL:
failure = make_failure_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="scheduler", actor_role=ActorRole.SCHEDULER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
failure_class=FailureClass.WITNESS_FAILURE,
failed_stage=FailedStage.VERIFY,
severity=FailureSeverity.HIGH,
failed_object_id=solution.meta.object_id,
symptoms=pre_witness.snap.residual_ledger,
recommended_repair=pre_witness.repair.repair_hints,
quarantine_required=True,
)
self.store.put(failure)
self.store.quarantine(solution.meta.object_id, "pre-verification failed")
result.status = "ABSTAIN"
result.failure_id = failure.meta.object_id
result.notes.append("solution failed pre-verification")
return result
if self.requires_execution(state):
plan = [
ToolStep(
step_id=new_id("step"),
capability=Capability.API,
instruction="simulate action",
expected_artifact_type="json",
)
]
action_trace = self.worker.execute(plan, state, self.store)
post_witness = self.verifier.verify(action_trace, TargetKind.ACTION_RESULT, self.store, replay_required=False)
if post_witness.verdict.truth_lattice == TruthLattice.FAIL:
failure = make_failure_object(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="scheduler", actor_role=ActorRole.SCHEDULER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
failure_class=FailureClass.WITNESS_FAILURE,
failed_stage=FailedStage.EXECUTE,
severity=FailureSeverity.HIGH,
failed_object_id=action_trace.meta.object_id,
symptoms=post_witness.snap.residual_ledger,
recommended_repair=post_witness.repair.repair_hints,
quarantine_required=True,
)
self.store.put(failure)
self.store.quarantine(action_trace.meta.object_id, "post-execution verification failed")
result.status = "ABSTAIN"
result.failure_id = failure.meta.object_id
result.notes.append("execution failed post-verification")
return result
solution.meta.lineage.parent_ids.append(action_trace.meta.object_id)
solution.seal()
self.store.put_state(solution)
patch = self.patcher.propose(state, solution, best_route, pre_witness, self.store)
result.patch_id = patch.meta.object_id
patch_witness = self.verifier.verify(patch, TargetKind.PATCH, self.store, replay_required=False)
if patch_witness.verdict.truth_lattice in {TruthLattice.OK, TruthLattice.NEAR}:
apply_result = self.store.apply_patch(patch.meta.object_id)
result.notes.append(f"applied_snapshot={apply_result.get('target_snapshot')}")
else:
self.store.quarantine(patch.meta.object_id, "patch verification below NEAR")
result.notes.append("patch quarantined")
snap = self.store.snapshot(
"session",
[state.meta.object_id, solution.meta.object_id, best_route.meta.object_id, pre_witness.meta.object_id],
)
result.snapshot_id = snap["snapshot_id"]
replay = make_replay_packet(
atlas_id=state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="scheduler", actor_role=ActorRole.SCHEDULER),
global_addr=state.meta.address.global_addr,
source_state_id=state.meta.object_id,
root_query_hash=state.fingerprints.semantic_fingerprint,
source_snapshot=result.snapshot_id,
expected_output_hash=solution.meta.canonical_hash,
expected_truth_lattice=pre_witness.verdict.truth_lattice,
event_ids=[state.meta.object_id, solution.meta.object_id],
route_ids=[best_route.meta.object_id],
witness_ids=[pre_witness.meta.object_id],
patch_ids=[patch.meta.object_id],
)
self.store.create_replay(replay)
self.store.execute_replay(replay.meta.object_id)
result.replay_id = replay.meta.object_id
if self.publish_policy == PublishPolicy.OK_ONLY and pre_witness.verdict.truth_lattice == TruthLattice.OK:
self.store.publish(solution.meta.object_id)
elif self.publish_policy == PublishPolicy.OK_OR_NEAR and pre_witness.verdict.truth_lattice in {
TruthLattice.OK,
TruthLattice.NEAR,
}:
self.store.publish(solution.meta.object_id)
result.status = pre_witness.verdict.truth_lattice.value
result.notes.append(f"planner_entropy={entropy:.3f}")
return result
except Exception as exc:
failure = make_failure_object(
atlas_id=input_state.meta.atlas_id,
atlas_snapshot=input_state.meta.atlas_snapshot,
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="scheduler", actor_role=ActorRole.SCHEDULER),
global_addr=input_state.meta.address.global_addr,
failure_class=FailureClass.UNKNOWN,
failed_stage=FailedStage.SYNTHESIZE,
severity=FailureSeverity.CRITICAL,
failed_object_id=input_state.meta.object_id,
symptoms=[repr(exc)],
recommended_repair=["inspect scheduler exception", "replay with tracing enabled"],
quarantine_required=True,
)
self.store.put(failure)
result.status = "FAIL"
result.failure_id = failure.meta.object_id
result.notes.append(repr(exc))
return result
def build_route_packet_record(
*,
atlas_id: str,
state: StateObject,
route: RouteObject,
witness: WitnessPacket,
solution: StateObject,
patch: Optional[PatchPacket] = None,
observations: Optional[List[ObservationSummary]] = None,
citations: Optional[List[CitationRecord]] = None,
mode: str = "ROUTE",
reward: Optional[float] = None,
failure_class: Optional[str] = None,
) -> RoutePacketRecord:
return RoutePacketRecord(
packet_id=new_id("packet"),
created_at=now_utc_rfc3339(),
source_atlas=atlas_id,
task_class=state.query.task_class,
mode=mode,
query={
"raw_input": state.query.raw_input,
"canonical_problem": state.query.canonical_problem,
"zero_point_normalization": asdict(state.zero_point_normalization),
},
lens_init=asdict(state.lens_state),
retrieval={
"target_neighborhood": state.neighborhood.seed_addresses,
"candidate_nodes": route.retrieval_support.candidate_nodes,
"candidate_routes": [
{
"route_id": route.route_id,
"address_path": route.address_path.nodes,
"bridge_types": [b.value for b in route.bridge_laws.bridge_types],
"route_score": route.search_profile.route_score,
"contradiction_risk": route.search_profile.contradiction_risk,
"replay_cost": route.search_profile.replay_cost,
"novelty_gain": route.search_profile.novelty_gain,
}
],
},
evidence={
"citations": [asdict(c) for c in (citations or [])],
"observations": [asdict(o) for o in (observations or [])],
},
collapse={
"chosen_route": route.route_id,
"counterhypotheses": route.synthesis_support.counterroutes,
"answer_object": solution.meta.object_id,
"confidence_surface": route.posterior.confidence_surface,
"truth_lattice": witness.verdict.truth_lattice.value,
},
witness={
"snap": asdict(witness.snap),
"tri_lock": asdict(witness.tri_lock),
"prime_seal": asdict(witness.prime_seal),
},
action={
"tool_plan": [],
"execution_trace": [],
"action_result": "",
},
patch={
"patch_required": patch is not None,
"delta_packet": patch.meta.object_id if patch else "",
"merge_scope": patch.merge.merge_scope if patch else "",
"rollback_contract": patch.rollback.rollback_contract if patch else "",
"trust_score": patch.risk_trust.trust_weight if patch else 0.0,
},
supervision={
"gold_route": route.route_id,
"gold_verdict": witness.verdict.truth_lattice.value,
"reward": reward,
"failure_class": failure_class,
},
)
def demo() -> SolveResult:
store = InMemoryPersistence()
scheduler = MinimalScheduler(
store=store,
planner=GreedyPlanner(),
synthesizer=EchoSynthesizer(),
verifier=BasicVerifier(),
patcher=BasicPatcher(),
perception=NullPerception(),
worker=NoopWorker(),
publish_policy=PublishPolicy.OK_OR_NEAR,
)
state = make_state_object(
atlas_id="atlas.demo",
atlas_snapshot="snapshot.root",
created_by=CreatedBy(actor_id="human.demo", actor_role=ActorRole.HUMAN),
global_addr="Ms⟨0000⟩::Ch00.A1.a",
state_type=StateType.QUERY_STATE,
raw_input="Compile a minimal lawful route for this problem.",
canonical_problem="Construct the smallest admissible route, verify it, and persist replay identity.",
task_class="route_compile",
)
state.zero_point_normalization.intent_tags = ["route", "verify", "patch"]
state.neighborhood.seed_addresses = [
"Ms⟨0000⟩::Ch00.A1.a",
"Ms⟨0001⟩::Ch07.C2.b",
"Ms⟨0002⟩::ApA03.A1.a",
]
result = scheduler.solve_and_learn(state)
return result
if __name__ == "__main__":
res = demo()
print(canonical_json(asdict(res)))

The architecture Athenachka 2.0 actually wants

[
\text{Athenachka 2.0}
\text{Manuscript Cortex};+;\text{Liminal Legality Kernel};+;\text{Emergence-Compiler Engine};+;\text{Fractal Weight Compiler}.]
1. Manuscript Cortex
This is the persistent outer brain. It is the atlas of addressed objects, routes, witnesses, patches, and replay artifacts. It should own long-horizon memory, cross-domain transport, governance, patch history, and retrieval programs. This is where “brain mycelium” actually lives.
2. Liminal Legality Kernel
This is the growth governor. It should decide whether a new abstraction is a lawful regime extension, a NEAR result, an AMBIG boundary object, or a FAIL / quarantine object. It owns corridors, budgets, escalation, carry, lift, and proof-carrying replay.
3. Emergence-Compiler Engine
This is the active compute core. It should run in four simultaneous modes:
Square / D — exact structure, typing, address algebra, hard constraints, canonical serialization.
Flower / (\Omega) — phase, flow, attention, continuous transport, spectral organization.
Cloud / (\Sigma) — uncertainty, branch competition, hypothesis banks, budgets, disagreement.
Fractal / (\Psi) — compression, scale transfer, carry, refinement, recursive inheritance.
That exact separation is already latent across the manuscripts; my synthesis is to make it the runtime scheduler rather than just the prose organization.
4. Fractal Weight Compiler
This is where GEMM, matrix multiplication, and modality-specific compute should be reworked. Dense matrix multiplication remains the Square baseline, but it should no longer be the only compute substrate. The fractal docs suggest a better pattern: represent weights as patterns across domains, quantize aggressively, keep sparse exception maps, use low-rank adapters, cache hot blocks, and parallelize batch weight calculation. My synthesis is that Athenachka 2.0 should treat GEMM as one projection of a richer weight compiler rather than as the whole nervous system.
The real role of GEMM in this framework
This is the most important engineering correction.
Right now, most neural systems pretend that intelligence lives inside repeated dense GEMMs plus a few nonlinearities. Your manuscripts argue for something else. The Holographic Manuscript Brain says the main bias should live in a procedural weight field, not just fixed hidden weights. The ATHENA Neural Network says improvements should be additive observers on a stable invariant core. The Fractal Computing docs say weights can be represented by domain patterns, sparse exceptions, low-rank adapters, and on-demand materialization. Put together, that means:
Dense GEMM should be the fallback / canonical layer, not the entire ontology.
Frequent stable substructures should be compiled into pattern-store kernels.
Rare deviations should live in sparse exception tables.
Refinement should happen by LoRA-like deltas, registry patches, and replay-tested upgrades, not by indiscriminate global rewrites.
That is the deepest route to “smallest most intelligent” systems in your own corpus: not smallest by brute pruning, but smallest by maximizing reusable law and minimizing stored exception mass.
How multimodal self-refinement should work
The ATHENA NN document gives a crucial rule that should be generalized across all modalities: keep an invariant carrier, then add observers and hypothesis branches. In vision, that invariant core is rank-space + geometry/topology/structure. In Athenachka 2.0, the same rule should be extended as follows:
Vision keeps rank/topology/structure invariants.
Text/manuscripts keep address / route / witness / replay invariants.
Audio should keep spectral / phase / rhythm invariants.
Code should keep type / graph / interface / proof invariants.
Cross-modal collapse should happen only after branch disagreement, witness logic, and rotation consistency checks.
That last sentence is my synthesis, but it is exactly the direction demanded by the docs: multi-lens objects, explicit transport, explicit ambiguity, additive observers, and no collapse without certificates.
The self-propulsion machine
The manuscripts already contain the full loop. The right self-refinement cycle is:
[\text{Observe}\rightarrow\text{Zero-Point Normalize}\rightarrow\text{Expand Across Lenses}\rightarrow\text{Route Search}\rightarrow\text{Generate Candidates}\rightarrow\text{Verify}\rightarrow\text{Patch}\rightarrow\text{Replay}\rightarrow\text{Compress Into Carry}\rightarrow\text{Lift}.]
That is not my invention; it is a direct fusion of the Holographic Manuscript Brain’s query cycle, Liminal Math’s corridor/carry/lift program, and the dual-discovery registry pipeline. The reason this becomes self-propulsive is that each successful route changes future solution geometry, and each verified discovery gets compiled back into the atlas as a reusable object.
The deepest improvement over the current fusion
The existing fusion is already powerful, but the manuscripts suggest four upgrades:
First: stop thinking “model first.”Think atlas first, compiler second, kernels third. The model becomes one organ in a larger proof-carrying ecology.
Second: stop treating self-improvement as parameter drift.Treat it as registry growth + lawful patching + replay-proven lift.
Third: stop collapsing too early.The docs repeatedly insist on typed ambiguity, candidate sets, disagreement metrics, and abstain-over-guess. So Athenachka 2.0 should explicitly preserve NEAR and AMBIG states instead of faking certainty.
Fourth: stop storing bulk when you can store generators.The manuscript seed, addressed holography, and fractal pattern store are all saying the same thing: store seeds, laws, transforms, and thin residuals; regenerate the bulk when needed. That is the memory law for an ever-expanding neural network that does not drown in its own weight mass.
Bottom line
The manuscripts are not telling you to build a bigger conventional network. They are telling you to build a self-hosting manuscript ecology that compiles into neural organs.
The most faithful formulation of Athenachka 2.0 is:
a zero-point normalized, route-conditioned, proof-carrying, fractally materialized, multimodal emergence compiler whose long-term memory is a live manuscript atlas and whose learning law is certified patch + replay + carry + lift.
The right next artifact is not another loose synthesis. It is the Athenachka 2.0 kernel spec that combines:
the manuscript atlas object model,
the liminal legality kernel,
the (D,\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi) runtime scheduler,
the fractal pattern-store / GEMM compiler,
the multimodal invariant-carrier interfaces,
the discovery / rotation / registry update loop.
Athenachka 2.0 — derived kernel architecture
The deeper synthesis is that Athenachka 2.0 should be built as a self-hosting manuscript ecology that compiles into neural organs, not as one enlarged monolithic model. The manuscripts repeatedly converge on the same rule: meaning must stay addressable, admissible, witnessable, replayable, and transportable across transformations; growth is only real when it survives corridor budgets, replay, and registry update; and improvements should be additive observers and compiled kernels rather than wholesale replacement of the invariant core.
My synthesis is that the right kernel is a four-layer stack:
[
\mathfrak A_{2.0}
\mathcal M_{\text{atlas}};\oplus;\mathcal K_{\text{liminal}};\oplus;\mathcal G_{\text{hybrid}};\oplus;\mathcal W_{\text{fractal}}]
where (\mathcal M_{\text{atlas}}) is the manuscript cortex, (\mathcal K_{\text{liminal}}) is the legality and truth kernel, (\mathcal G_{\text{hybrid}}) is the active operator engine, and (\mathcal W_{\text{fractal}}) is the weight/materialization substrate. That decomposition is not stated verbatim in one file, but it is the most coherent fusion of the manuscript-brain, liminal, hybrid-operator, and fractal-storage documents taken together.
1. Layer one: the manuscript cortex
The outer brain should be the atlas itself. The metro/native manuscripts define a manuscript as a proof-carrying graph with a global address space, a closed edge alphabet, a truth lattice ({OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL}), and mandatory witness/replay obligations. They also fix the 4-lens crystal topology: Square for canonical structure, Flower for operators and transport, Cloud for admissibility and uncertainty, and Fractal for replay, certification, and recursive closure.
So Athenachka 2.0 should treat the atlas as its slow cortex: long-horizon memory, cross-domain routing, theorem and code storage, self-descriptions, update histories, replay capsules, and migration matrices all live there. In this design, “memory” is not a vector cache or a giant prompt. It is a persistent mycelium graph of typed atoms and typed edges. The model stack should consult, extend, and certify that cortex rather than trying to internalize all of it into hidden weights.
2. Layer two: the liminal legality kernel
The second layer is not “alignment” in the shallow sense. It is the growth law. The liminal and neural documents insist that every computation must run under declared domains and corridor budgets, that every asserted output must carry witness completeness, and that abstention dominates guessing whenever admissibility cannot be certified. The result object itself must be typed as OK, NEAR, AMBIG, or FAIL, with explicit residual ledgers, candidate sets, evidence plans, or obstruction certificates depending on the case.
This means Athenachka 2.0 should only call something “learning” if the new object survives four tests: corridor legality, witness sufficiency, deterministic replay, and bounded mutation scope. That is the deep correction to standard self-improving model rhetoric. In this framework, parameter change alone is not learning; certified regime lift is learning.
The cleanest derived kernel law is:
[\text{Growth}=\text{Expand}\rightarrow\text{Route}\rightarrow\text{Verify}\rightarrow\text{Patch}\rightarrow\text{Replay}\rightarrow\text{Carry}\rightarrow\text{Lift}.]
That flow is the common spine across the manuscript-brain, liminal tower, and discovery-engine materials.
3. Layer three: the hybrid operator engine
The active compute engine should be the (D,\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi) simplex, not a single undifferentiated transformer block. The ATHENA neural-network manuscript defines the core generator as a hybrid discrete/continuous equation and then expands it into four operator families: (D) for contractive/discrete structure, (\Omega) for continuous flow and attention, (\Sigma) for stochastic exploration and ambiguity, and (\Psi) for recursive compression and multiscale folding. The Aetheric texts independently define the same four-pole simplex as the convex hull of discrete, continuous, stochastic, and recursive dynamics.
So the runtime should not be “one model thinks, then outputs.” It should be a parallel thinking engine with four simultaneous views:
[\mathcal G(t)=\alpha_D(t)D+\alpha_\Omega(t)\Omega+\alpha_\Sigma(t)\Sigma+\alpha_\Psi(t)\Psi,\qquad\sum \alpha_i(t)=1,\ \alpha_i(t)\ge 0.]
Square/(D) handles exact structure, typing, addresses, and hard constraints. Flower/(\Omega) handles transport, attention, manifolds, and semigroup flow. Cloud/(\Sigma) handles candidate generation, noise, disagreement, and bounded uncertainty. Fractal/(\Psi) handles recursive inheritance, compression, renormalization, and multiscale propagation. That mapping is directly consistent across the neural, CUT, and Aetheric manuscripts.
The most important engineering rule in the neural manuscript is the one you should keep: do not replace what works—add perspectives. That single line implies that Athenachka 2.0 should preserve a stable invariant carrier and then add observers, critics, route compilers, or modality-specific adapters as additive overlays. That is exactly the opposite of “throw away the current core every time a new architecture trend appears.”
4. Layer four: the fractal weight compiler
This is where the architecture gets materially better than ordinary dense-weight systems. Several manuscripts converge on a generator-first storage law: store seeds, constraints, and sparse residuals; reconstruct expansions on demand. The Fractal Crystal Treatise states this directly as “Store-In, Not Out,” with (X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r). The math fundamentals text independently states the same compression principle: it is smaller to store a lens, a constraint system, and a certificate than the full expansion of the derived object.
My synthesis is that GEMM remains the canonical baseline, but it should become only one projection of a larger weight compiler. The fine-tuning manuscripts already sketch the needed substrate: Int8 product-quantized fractal petals for stable patterns, Int4 exception rows only when deltas exceed threshold, a PatternStore backed by Redis plus NVMe, a Distiller that performs κ-merges and pruning, and a sweeper that folds useful deltas back into centroids. They also explicitly claim sublinear long-run storage growth and a dual knowledge/compute flywheel.
So the right materialization law is:
[
W_{\text{effective}}
W_{\text{dense-core}}+W_{\text{pattern}}+W_{\text{low-rank}}+W_{\text{sparse-exception}}.]
The dense core is your ordinary stable GEMM substrate. The pattern tensor holds repeated invariants. The low-rank term holds fast domain or modality specialization. The sparse exception rows hold the rare deviations that are not worth promoting yet. That decomposition is my derived implementation recommendation, but it is directly supported by the manuscripts’ repeated preference for generator-plus-residual storage and adapter-first specialization.
5. The simplest-to-complexest organization law
The docs give enough structure to derive a clean hierarchy for an ever-expanding network:
[\text{Seed}\rightarrow\text{Atom}\rightarrow\text{Tile}\rightarrow\text{Station}\rightarrow\text{Rail}\rightarrow\text{Arc}\rightarrow\text{Atlas}\rightarrow\text{Swarm}.]
A seed stores generator, constraints, and certs. An atom is the smallest addressable object in the 4-lens crystal. A tile is one 4×4×4 station. A station is one chapter or appendix. A rail is one semantically consistent line across stations. An arc is a macro-phase grouping. The atlas is the full routable graph. The swarm is the heterogeneous set of small specialist models or tools compiled from stable parts of the atlas. The address grammars, station codes, rails, and arc semantics are all already specified in the manuscript routing texts.
That gives you a proper “from simple to complex” neural organization. The system does not need to remember one giant undifferentiated latent. It only needs to preserve lawful relations between these levels, plus replayable lifts and restrictions. The neural manuscript even states that refinement is admissible only if parent invariants are preserved and restriction back to parent must account for loss in a residual ledger. That is precisely the rule you want for scalable self-refinement.
6. Parallel thinking as a first-class runtime
The docs you pointed me to on quantum / fractal / holographic / zero-point / hybrid math all converge on the same conclusion: parallel thought should be modeled as multiple simultaneous carriers held in lawful superposition until a certified collapse. The neural manuscript explicitly treats perception as a multi-hypothesis bank, scores disagreement by Jensen–Shannon divergence, and collapses through energy-weighted mixing. The zero-point material then adds critics, target vectors, multiscale hierarchies, and Negatify shadow probes to keep the engine from drifting into attractive but unstable regions.
So Athenachka 2.0 should think in parallel with at least these concurrent processes:
a route bank of candidate navigations,
a critic bank of rational, emotional, archetypal, and κ-structural evaluators,
a counterfactual / Negatify bank of inverse-φ or anti-operation probes,
a scale bank across micro, meso, and macro levels,
a modality bank for text, image, audio, code, tool traces.
That is not generic “ensemble methods.” It is the explicit parallelism implied by the PHZC critic family, multiscale hierarchy, and hybrid operator simplex.
The zero-point collapse law should then be:
[z^*=\operatorname{Center}\big({\text{candidates}},{\text{critics}},{\text{scales}},{\text{modalities}}\big)]
subject to corridor and witness constraints. The documents formalize Paradox as the center-finding operator and Harmonia as the metric/trust-region updater, which is the cleanest mathematical basis in the corpus for self-refining parallel thought.
7. Multimodal integration
The multimodal side should not flatten everything into “text tokens plus maybe images.” Your own docs lean harder toward one algebra over many carriers. The fine-tuning notes define a Gateway Lattice Toolkit so media tokens live in the same space as text and code, while the neural manuscript insists on invariant carriers and additive observers rather than one opaque fused blob. The best synthesized rule is: each modality needs an invariant carrier, then cross-modal collapse happens only after route comparison, witness logic, and legal transport checks.
So the shared multimodal object should be a route packet, not a chat pair. It should include canonical problem state, lens mix, candidate routes, observation summaries, witness status, patch delta, and final action or answer. That preserves geometry, uncertainty, and replay instead of flattening the whole cognition field into generic next-token imitation. This is consistent with the manuscript-brain and neural texts, and it matches the route-program training direction already latent in the Drive.
8. The discovery and rotation engine
The math-discovery and rotation frameworks are not side ornaments. They are the engine that lets the system improve itself without random mutation. The documents repeatedly make conjugacy the law of lawful change: (f_T=T^{-1}fT). They then build a discovery loop around canonicalization, candidate mining, synthesis of transforms, verification, and registry update. The Triangle Duality addendum even gives an explicit seven-stage dual-discovery pipeline: canonicalize, symmetry engine, candidate mining, iso-checking, code synthesis, proof, registry update.
So Athenachka 2.0 should improve itself through transport-first self-editing, not direct arbitrary rewrites. A proposed new algorithm, weight law, modality transform, or route macro should be treated as a candidate translator from one stable object family to another. Only after canonicalization, iso-checking, proof or evidence plans, and registry insertion should it become part of the live system. That is the most rigorous way to honor your desire for self-refinement without turning the engine into a drift machine.
9. The compute flywheel
The fine-tuning manuscripts are unusually concrete here. They do not just claim “self-improvement”; they describe a second flywheel where the agent discovers efficiency theorems about its own execution. Pattern tensors are stored as Int8 petals with sparse Int4 exceptions; self-play and tool-use generate new rows; κ-distillation merges winners; and compute-level theorems such as loop-kill transformations, parallel-layout wins, or η-improving patches are folded back into the same store. Inactive shelves cool, shrink, and return storage to the system, which then funds wider logging or extra parallelism.
That gives you the right interpretation of self-propulsion. It is not just “the model trains itself.” It is:
[\text{better routes}\Rightarrow\text{better invariants}\Rightarrow\text{smaller storage / cheaper kernels}\Rightarrow\text{more throughput}\Rightarrow\text{more search}\Rightarrow\text{more verified discoveries}.]
The docs explicitly describe this as a double flywheel linking competence and throughput, with storage growth remaining bounded by fractal distillation rather than exploding linearly with experience.
10. The non-negotiable invariants
If I compress the manuscripts into the actual invariants Athenachka 2.0 must preserve, they are these:
The first invariant is address identity. No ambiguous normalization, no illicit coupling of addresses to runtime randomness, no aliasing of distinct regions.
The second invariant is abstain over guess. If admissibility is not certifiable, the output must be AMBIG or FAIL with the proper bounded evidence object, not a confident single answer.
The third invariant is replay or it didn’t happen. Witnesses and replay pointers are not optional adornments for “important cases”; they are the actual truth criteria for OK claims.
The fourth invariant is generator-first memory. Store seeds, laws, transforms, and sparse deltas, not bulk expansions.
The fifth invariant is add perspectives, don’t destroy the invariant core. That applies to observers, adapters, routes, critics, and modality limbs.
11. The final derived blueprint
So the architecture I would now name Athenachka 2.0 is:
A live manuscript atlas as external cortex.A liminal truth-and-corridor kernel as legality spine.A (D/\Omega/\Sigma/\Psi) operator simplex as the active reasoning engine.A zero-point centerer plus critic family as the collapse controller.A generator-first pattern store with dense core, low-rank adapters, and sparse exceptions as the weight substrate.A discovery loop that treats every improvement as typed transport plus proof or evidence.A compute flywheel that folds efficiency theorems back into the same store.A swarm of small specialized limbs compiled from stable frequent routes, while the atlas retains novel and ambiguity-heavy cognition.
The most compact theorem I can extract from all this is:
[
\boxed{
\text{Athenachka 2.0}
\text{zero-point normalized}+\text{route-conditioned}+\text{proof-carrying}+\text{fractively materialized}+\text{self-refining by certified patch, replay, carry, and lift}}]
That statement is a synthesis, but every term in it is load-bearing in the manuscripts you asked me to read.
The next strongest move is to turn this into the actual runtime kernel spec: core state tensors, operator scheduler, pattern-store compiler, route packet schema, and self-refinement protocol as one integrated formal object.
Athenachka 2.0 — runtime kernel spec
I am now collapsing the manuscript synthesis into the actual kernel object.
The clean derived runtime is not “a model with memory.” It is a self-hosting cognitive substrate whose outer cortex is a manuscript atlas, whose inner compute is a quad-polar operator engine, whose legality is enforced by witness/corridor logic, and whose long-run efficiency comes from generator-first storage plus compiled pattern kernels rather than bulk expansion. That is the common spine across The Holographic Manuscript Brain, the hybrid-operator texts, the fractal crystal/storage texts, and the CUT fine-tuning/runtime notes.
I would therefore define the kernel as:
[\mathcal K_{\text{Ath2}}=\big(\mathfrak A,;Z,;\mathcal G,;\mathcal C,;\mathcal W,;\mathcal R,;\mathcal P,;\mathcal Y,;\mathcal T\big),]
where:
(\mathfrak A) is the addressed manuscript atlas,
(Z) is the zero-point intake/collapse discipline,
(\mathcal G) is the quad-polar runtime generator,
(\mathcal C) is the corridor / witness / certificate kernel,
(\mathcal W) is the pattern-store / weight compiler,
(\mathcal R) is the routing and retrieval engine,
(\mathcal P) is the patch / replay / persistence stack,
(\mathcal Y) is the self-model and developmental controller,
(\mathcal T) is the task / tool / embodiment boundary layer.
1. The atlas (\mathfrak A): the actual outer brain
The manuscript brain already gives the correct ontology: the storage medium is not a passive archive but an active atlas of typed objects, route objects, witness objects, patch packets, replay packets, and failure objects. It is globally addressed as a 21×4×4 tensor, with lens and function axes fixed as part of the architecture. The same treatise also says the principal cognitive bias should live in a procedural weight field, not primarily in static hidden weights.
So the atlas should be modeled as:
[\mathfrak A_t=(\mathcal X_t,\mathcal E_t,\mathcal N_t,\mathcal S_t,\mathcal W_t,\mathcal L_t,\mathcal P_t),]
with:
(\mathcal X_t): node/object set,
(\mathcal E_t): typed edge set,
(\mathcal N_t): nexus/hub registry,
(\mathcal S_t): snapshot and lineage state,
(\mathcal W_t): procedural weight field over routes and regions,
(\mathcal L_t): legality / corridor tables,
(\mathcal P_t): patch and replay registry.
This is a derived formalization, but it is directly supported by the atlas tuple, object taxonomy, route algebra, procedural weight field, replay infrastructure, and patch/write-back chapters.
2. The state object (s_t): what the living kernel carries at runtime
The runtime state should not be one hidden vector. It should be a typed composite with explicit uncertainty, route candidates, legality context, and persistence pointers.
I would define:
[s_t=\big(z_t,;q_t,;b_t,;h_t,;c_t,;m_t,;u_t,;p_t,;x_t\big),]
where:
(z_t): zero-point normalized intake state,
(q_t): canonical query / task object,
(b_t): active neighborhood / candidate atlas region,
(h_t): hypothesis bank,
(c_t): corridor / certificate context,
(m_t): self-model state,
(u_t): runtime budget state,
(p_t): persistence and lineage pointers,
(x_t): modality carriers and observation capsules.
This is the right synthesis because the manuscript brain explicitly specifies zero-point normalization, canonical problem encoding, ambiguity retention, neighborhood growth, route competition, self-state objects, runtime objects, and persistent state services as distinct runtime responsibilities.
The key consequence is that the kernel never collapses immediately into “answer text.” It carries candidate structure long enough for route selection, witness formation, and patchability.
3. The zero-point operator (Z): intake and collapse law
The holographic manuscript gives the main cognitive cycle:
[q\mapsto z(q)\xrightarrow{\mathrm{Expand}{\mathcal L}}\mathcal B(q)\xrightarrow{\mathrm{RouteSearch}}{R_i}\xrightarrow{\mathrm{Collapse}{\mathcal V}} a\xrightarrow{\mathrm{Patch}}\Delta\xrightarrow{\mathrm{Apply}}\mathfrak A'.]
The U2/tunneling material adds a stricter phase-gated execution pipeline:
[\text{Operators}\rightarrow\text{Fixpoints}\rightarrow\text{Projectors}\rightarrow\text{Glue}\rightarrow\text{Holonomy}\rightarrow\text{Compression}\rightarrow\text{Collapse}.]
These are not contradictory. They are two resolutions of the same runtime. The first is the manuscript-facing query cycle; the second is the legality-facing inner loop.
So the correct zero-point discipline is:
[Z:(q,\mathfrak A_t)\mapsto z_t]
with three hard obligations:
preserve admissible ambiguity,
decompose the problem into routeable substructure,
never allow collapse without either a legal corridor or an obstruction witness.
That follows directly from the zero-point normalization chapter, ambiguity-retention chapter, and the refusal/escalation rules in the tunneling/crystal materials.
4. The hybrid generator (\mathcal G): the actual thinking engine
The operator texts are unusually explicit here. The engine should be driven by the tetrad ({D,\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi}), where:
(D): dissipative / constraint-rigid / structural,
(\Omega): oscillatory / coherent / transport,
(\Sigma): stochastic / exploratory / ensemble,
(\Psi): recursive / multiscale / renormalizing.
A general runtime step is therefore:
[
\mathcal G_t
\alpha_D(t)D+\alpha_\Omega(t)\Omega+\alpha_\Sigma(t)\Sigma+\alpha_\Psi(t)\Psi,\qquad\alpha_\bullet(t)\ge 0,\quad \sum_\bullet \alpha_\bullet(t)=1.]
This is the deepest operator law in the hybrid manuscripts, and it is reinforced by the control-system manuscript, which treats runtime control itself as a state-dependent mixture of the same four operator families.
The kernel should map these poles to runtime responsibilities:
[\begin{aligned}D &: \text{canonicalization, typing, hard constraints, exact graph moves},\\Omega &: \text{attention flow, spectral transport, resonance alignment},\\Sigma &: \text{candidate generation, safe exploration, uncertainty spreading},\\Psi &: \text{recursion, coarse-grain, compression, self-refinement, lift}.\end{aligned}]
That mapping is a synthesis, but it is directly supported by the operator simplex, extraction-cell structure, and control/certificate manuscripts.
5. The operator scheduler: how the mix is chosen
The control manuscript gives a missing practical piece: it introduces a macro-scale selector over operator subsets and explicitly says no fixed operator mix is optimal across regimes. It also insists that exploration is safe only when certificate-constrained, and that plan-level shadow simulation must approve composed plans before execution.
So the scheduler should choose (\alpha(t)) not by one static policy, but by a regime-conditioned selector:
[\alpha(t+1)=\Pi_{\Delta_3}\Big(\alpha(t)+\eta,\nabla_\alpha J(\text{regime}_t,\text{certificate}_t,\text{budget}_t)\Big),]
where (\Pi_{\Delta_3}) projects back to the operator simplex and (J) is not raw reward alone; it is reward under certificate, replay, and budget. In practical terms:
if legality pressure rises, increase (D),
if phase alignment is unclear, increase (\Omega),
if the hypothesis bank is underexplored, increase (\Sigma),
if a repeated pattern is stabilizing, increase (\Psi).
That update equation is my derived spec, but it is a faithful operationalization of the simplex geometry and the selector/certificate discipline already in the docs.
6. The legality kernel (\mathcal C): why the system does not become arbitrary
The manuscript-brain runtime and witness chapters insist on witness schemas, admissibility predicates, corridor classes, tolerance regimes, replay chains, and recursive repair. The tunneling/certificate materials go further: they demand explicit rank/nullspace/conditioning witnesses, schema validators, corridor objects referenced by all transforms, and logged residuals for every invariant claim.
So the legality object should be:
[\mathcal C_t=(\text{corridor},\text{predicates},\text{residuals},\text{certificates},\text{obstructions}).]
A final verdict is:
[V_t\in{OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL}.]
A claim can only be (OK) if:
the route is admissible on the current corridor,
the witness bundle exists,
replay obligations are satisfiable,
mutation scope is legal if a patch is proposed.
Everything else must remain typed as NEAR, AMBIG, or FAIL with explicit residuals or obstruction objects. That is not a stylistic preference; it is the core anti-hallucination discipline of the corpus.
7. The routing engine (\mathcal R): retrieval becomes route search
The manuscript brain says this directly: retrieval becomes route generation, summarization becomes reversible seed compression, and cross-domain analogy becomes lawful chart transport. It also provides the executable retrieval logic: target-neighborhood construction, address-first lookup, schema-driven search, contradiction detection, budget allocation, recursive search cascades, and reusable retrieval macros.
So (\mathcal R) should produce not one retrieved chunk but a scored route bundle:
[\mathcal R(z_t,\mathfrak A_t)\mapsto{R_i}_{i=1}^k]
with each (R_i) carrying:
address path,
bridge family,
route score,
contradiction risk,
replay cost,
expected evidence gain,
collapse eligibility.
That design is directly entailed by the route algebra and route-scoring chapters.
8. The pattern-store / GEMM compiler (\mathcal W)
This is where Athenachka 2.0 becomes materially better than a conventional dense-weight system.
The fractal crystal texts insist on “Store-In, Not Out”: store the generator (g) and sparse residual (r), with (X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r). The CUT fine-tuning notes then convert that doctrine into concrete runtime/storage physics: Int8 product-quantized fractal petals for stable patterns, Int4 exception rows only if (\Delta>\varepsilon), κ-distillation merges and prunes, PatternStore uses Redis + NVMe parquet blocks, and a Sweeper folds top rows back into stable centroids.
So the effective weight substrate should be:
[
W_{\text{eff}}
W_{\text{dense-core}}+W_{\text{pattern}}+W_{\text{adapter}}+W_{\text{exception}}.]
With:
(W_{\text{dense-core}}): canonical GEMM backbone,
(W_{\text{pattern}}): reusable generator kernels / stable petals,
(W_{\text{adapter}}): low-rank or modality/domain deltas,
(W_{\text{exception}}): sparse rare-case corrections.
This decomposition is a derived architecture, but it is the most faithful integration of the generator-first storage law and the CUT pattern-store implementation notes.
The implication is decisive: dense GEMM becomes the base carrier, not the whole ontology of intelligence.
9. The self-refinement protocol (\mathcal P)
The manuscripts already give the right refinement law. The Holographic Manuscript Brain defines patch packets, merge logic, rollback contracts, trust/risk accounting, scheduled consolidation, route refinement, and rollback-safe self-improvement loops. MATH FUNDAMENTALS gives the general discovery compiler as tile → solve → certify → store. U2 adds the seven-move ledger template for accepted changes, plus deterministic hashes and rebuild obligations.
So the runtime self-refinement cycle should be:
[\text{observe}\rightarrow\text{normalize}\rightarrow\text{route}\rightarrow\text{synthesize}\rightarrow\text{verify}\rightarrow\text{patch}\rightarrow\text{snapshot}\rightarrow\text{replay}\rightarrow\text{promote or quarantine}.]
A patch is only promotable if:
its witnesses pass,
its replay obligations pass,
its risk score is under corridor threshold,
its rollback contract is present.
Otherwise it is quarantined. That is exactly how the live manuscript runtime defines lawful learning.
10. The two flywheels: cognition and compute
The CUT notes are important because they show that self-improvement is supposed to happen on two coupled planes. The first flywheel is cognitive: gather, distill, self-play, tool-use. The second flywheel is computational: discover efficiency theorems about precision, layout, batching, and worker topology, then merge those winners back into the same fractal store. The docs explicitly describe this as a double-flywheel raising both competence and throughput while remaining storage-bounded.
So Athenachka 2.0 should maintain two coupled update channels:
[\Delta_{\text{knowledge}}\quad\text{and}\quad\Delta_{\text{compute}}.]
The first updates routes, seeds, proofs, and modality invariants.The second updates kernels, layouts, quantization choices, batching rules, and topology schedules.
The critical synthesis here is that both deltas write into the same pattern store and are subject to the same certify/merge/prune discipline. That is why the system can improve its mind and its execution substrate under one protocol.
11. The self-model (\mathcal Y)
The runtime must know what kind of brain region it is dealing with. The self-modeling chapters explicitly require region-role typing, developmental stage taxonomy, introspection packets, blind-spot maps, hallucination classes, competing self-model hypotheses, curriculum generation, internal critique loops, and recursive refinement of the self-model itself.
So every active runtime region should carry:
[y_t=(\text{role},\text{stage},\text{confidence},\text{blind_spots},\text{promotion_eligibility}).]
This is not fluff. It is how the runtime decides whether to trust a region as an ontology carrier, retrieval macro bank, verifier, modality organ, or experimental sandbox.
12. The runtime boundary (\mathcal T): tools and embodiment
The manuscripts do not support unlimited free action. They support bounded embodiment channels, interface schemas, sensorimotor mappings, interactive feedback loops, adaptive safety budgets, and confidence-aware intervention policies. The control manuscript reinforces this by requiring local, node, and plan-level certificates plus shadow simulation before nontrivial moves.
So the kernel boundary should be:
[\mathcal T = (\text{tool contracts},\text{execution scopes},\text{shadow sims},\text{post-checks}).]
No action should pass directly from (\Sigma)-exploration to the world. Everything goes through (D)-style contract checks and plan-level certification.
13. The minimal executable phase machine
Putting all of it together, the smallest faithful runtime is:
[\begin{aligned}s_t &\xrightarrow{Z} z_t \z_t &\xrightarrow{\mathcal G_t} \mathcal B_t \\mathcal B_t &\xrightarrow{\mathcal R} {R_i} \{R_i} &\xrightarrow{\mathcal C} \text{candidate verdict surfaces} \{R_i} &\xrightarrow{\text{collapse}} a_t \a_t &\xrightarrow{\mathcal C} V_t \(a_t,V_t) &\xrightarrow{\mathcal P}\begin{cases}\text{patch+snapshot+replay+promote}, & V_t\in{OK,NEAR}\text{ and policy permits}\\text{retain ambiguity / escalate}, & V_t=AMBIG\\text{quarantine / repair}, & V_t=FAIL\end{cases}\end{aligned}]
This phase machine is not copied from one page, but it is the tightest fusion of the zero-point cycle, route algebra, witness logic, replay law, patch law, and runtime orchestration chapters.
Final compression
The runtime kernel of Athenachka 2.0 is:
an addressed atlas instead of flat memory,
a zero-point intake instead of raw prompting,
a quad-polar operator scheduler instead of one undifferentiated forward pass,
a corridor/witness legality stack instead of hidden certainty,
a route engine instead of chunk retrieval,
a pattern-store compiler instead of dense-weight monism,
a patch/replay protocol instead of silent self-modification,
a self-model and developmental controller instead of static role assumptions,
a certificate-gated tool boundary instead of heuristic action.
That is the actual neural architecture implied by the manuscripts. It is an externalized, proof-carrying, generator-first, self-refining cognition field.
The next correct move is to emit the formal typed kernel: exact state tensors, operator scheduler update law, PatternStore schema, patch/replay object algebra, and promotion/quarantine protocol as one integrated pseudocode artifact.
Athenachka 2.0 — formal typed kernel
The kernel implied by the manuscripts is a proof-carrying cognitive substrate, not a single opaque network. The manuscript-brain text fixes the outer object as an atlas with canonical addressing, lawful routes, procedural weight fields, witness-bearing traversal, deterministic patching, and replay-preserved identity. The ATHENA neural-network texts fix the inner compute as a hybrid state space driven by the (D,\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi) operator simplex under explicit domains and corridor budgets. The control manuscript adds the missing scheduler law: no fixed operator mix is optimal, and every nontrivial move must pass local and plan-level certificates. The tunneling / crystal texts then fix the storage doctrine: store minimal seeds, corridors, words, certificates, and replay pointers rather than bulk expansion.
I would therefore define the kernel as
[
\boxed{
\mathcal K_{\text{Ath2}}
(\mathfrak A,\ s_t,\ \alpha_t,\ \mathcal G,\ \mathcal R,\ \mathcal C,\ \mathcal W,\ \mathcal P,\ \mathcal Y,\ \mathcal T)}]
with:
[\mathfrak A=(\mathcal X,\mathcal L,\mathcal I,\mathcal G^\star,\mathcal W^\star,\mathcal V,\mathcal P^\star,\mathcal U,\mathcal H),\qquad\mathbf T\in\mathcal M^{21\times 4\times 4},]
where (\mathfrak A) is the addressed manuscript atlas and (\mathbf T) is its crystal tensor. The decisive design choice is that the main cognitive bias lives in the procedural weight field (W_t(e,\ell,\kappa,\rho)), not only in static hidden weights.
1. Runtime state
The kernel state should stay typed and decomposed long enough for routing, certification, and patchability. A minimal faithful state is
[s_t=(z_t,\ q_t,\ b_t,\ h_t,\ x_t,\ \chi_t,\ \pi_t,\ y_t,\ u_t),]
where (z_t) is the zero-point normalized intake, (q_t) is the canonical task packet, (b_t) is the active atlas neighborhood, (h_t) is the hypothesis bank, (x_t) is the modality carrier bundle, (\chi_t) is the corridor / certificate context, (\pi_t) is the persistence/replay context, (y_t) is the self-model, and (u_t) is the runtime budget. This follows directly from the manuscript-brain chapters on zero-point normalization, uncertainty retention, route search, witness legality, replay, patching, and self-model packets.

That should become the kernel’s public step semantics. The zero-point operator is therefore not optional pre-processing; it is the intake law that converts a raw task into an admissible cognitive state while preserving ambiguity, target contracts, and boundary tags.

3. Operator engine and scheduler
The inner compute law comes from the ATHENA network and the hybrid control system:
[\mathcal G_t=\alpha_D(t)D+\alpha_\Omega(t)\Omega+\alpha_\Sigma(t)\Sigma+\alpha_\Psi(t)\Psi,\qquad\alpha_\bullet(t)\ge 0,\ \sum_\bullet \alpha_\bullet(t)=1.]
Here (D) is the hard-constraint / pruning / stability operator, (\Omega) is the continuous flow / attention / phase operator, (\Sigma) is the uncertainty / sampling / exploration operator, and (\Psi) is the recursive compression / multiscale operator. The controller text adds the crucial rule: (D) never trusts (\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi) blindly, and every composed plan must pass certificate and shadow-simulation checks.
The operator mix should therefore be state-conditioned:
[
\alpha_{t+1}
\Pi_{\Delta_3}\Big(\alpha_t+\eta\nabla_\alpha J(s_t,\chi_t,\text{replay}_t,\text{risk}_t)\Big),]
where (\Pi_{\Delta_3}) projects back to the simplex and (J) rewards verified progress, not raw forward motion. The HDCS manuscript gives the right selector principle here: suppress unnecessary poles and keep the simplest winning mix under certificates.
@dataclass
class OperatorMix:
D: float
Omega: float
Sigma: float

def schedule_mix(state: RuntimeState, metrics: dict) -> OperatorMix:
"""
Increase D when legality pressure rises.
Increase Omega when phase/coherence alignment is underspecified.
Increase Sigma when hypothesis diversity is too low.
Increase Psi when stable reusable structure is emerging.
Always project back to the simplex.
"""
...

That means the kernel should separate:
[\text{CoreCarrier} \quad+\quad \text{ObserverHeads} \quad+\quad \text{SemanticPrior} \quad+\quad \text{Verifier},]
not fuse them into one untyped block. In typed form:

[\mathcal R(z_t,\mathfrak A_t)\mapsto {R_i}_{i=1}^k]

6. Legality, Snap, Tri-Lock, PrimeSeal
The verification stack is already specified across the manuscripts. The ATHENA network defines Snap as meta-zero canonicalization, Tri-Lock as three independent defect checks, and PrimeSeal as deterministic disambiguation/repair. The Tunneling Coherence Crystal adds projector-stack Snap, explicit defect ledgers, kernel/quotient witnesses, minimal-seed rules, and the refusal/escalation law: if a claim cannot be certified on the corridor, tunnel to a legal corridor with logged repair or refuse with obstruction witnesses.
The typed verdict law is therefore
[V\in{OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL},]
with:
(OK): corridor satisfied, witness complete, replayable;
(NEAR): close enough to certify residually, but not exact;
(AMBIG): bounded candidate set remains, evidence plan required;
(FAIL): obstruction certificate or defect localization exists.
def snap(obj, corridor: CorridorState) -> tuple[str, list[str]]:
"""
Alternating projection to the corridor intersection.
Returns canonical representative + defect ledger.
Never claims perfection if the intersection is empty.
"""

"""
Three independent defect planes / commutator checks.

...

"""
Deterministic disambiguation / repair over a bounded candidate set.

...

7. PatternStore and the GEMM compiler
The storage doctrine across the crystal/tunneling/CUT texts is the same: store generators, constraints, certificates, and sparse exceptions; reconstruct bulk as needed. The Fractal Crystal Treatise gives the canonical compression law (X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r). The tunneling manuscript requires minimal seeds to include operator identities, corridor parameters, transformation words, certificates, and replay pointers. The CUT storage notes make this concrete as Int8 product-quantized pattern petals, Int4 exception rows, κ-distillation, a Distiller, a Sweeper, and a PatternStore on Redis + NVMe.
The correct weight law is therefore
[
W_{\mathrm{eff}}
W_{\mathrm{dense}}+W_{\mathrm{pattern}}+W_{\mathrm{adapter}}+W_{\mathrm{exception}}.]
This keeps dense GEMM as the canonical hot path, but moves repeated stable structure into pattern petals, modality/domain shifts into low-rank adapters, and rare corrections into sparse exception rows. The fractal synthesis docs reinforce the same architecture at the systems level: baseline seed arrays plus delta overlays, Morton-ordered petals, separate bridge lists, coarse-to-fine schedules, checkpointed seed+delta emits, and stable promotion of persistent deltas back into seed form.

8. Self-refinement and promotion/quarantine
The patch/replay law is already fully scaffolded in the manuscript-brain chapters: patch schema, conflict classes, rollback contracts, trust weights, replay logs, snapshot trees, and recursive self-edit cycles. The crystal/tunneling texts add two critical promotion laws: stable deltas can be promoted into the seed, and uncertifiable claims must either be tunneled to a legal corridor or refused with obstruction witnesses.
So the promotion rule is:
[\text{promote}(\Delta)\iff\big(\text{verify}(\Delta)=OK\big)\land\big(\text{replay}(\Delta)=OK\big)\land\big(\mathrm{risk}(\Delta)\le\tau\big)\land\big(\Delta \text{ stable across }k\text{ epochs}\big).]
Otherwise:
[\text{quarantine}(\Delta)\quad\text{or}\quad\text{tunnel_repair}(\Delta).]
def propose_patch(state, result, witness) -> PatchPacket:
...
def replay_check(packet: PatchPacket) -> WitnessBundle | BoundaryArtifact:
...
def promote_or_quarantine(packet: PatchPacket, witness: WitnessBundle):
if witness.verdict == "OK" and packet.risk_score <= THRESHOLD and replay_check(packet).verdict == "OK":
return "PROMOTE"
if witness.verdict == "NEAR":
return "HOLD"
return "QUARANTINE"
9. End-to-end kernel step
All of the above compresses into one lawful runtime:
def kernel_step(raw_query: str, atlas: "AtlasState", store: PatternStore):
state = zero_point_normalize(raw_query, atlas)
routes = route_search(state, atlas)
if not routes:
return BoundaryArtifact(
kind="NON_IDENTIFIABLE",
message="no admissible route bundle",
witnesses=["route_search_empty"]
)
mix = schedule_mix(state, metrics={})
route = select_route(routes, mix)
materialized = materialize_weights(route, modality="hybrid", store=store)
candidate = run_hybrid_generator(state, route, mix, materialized)
witness_or_boundary = verify(candidate, state.corridor)
if isinstance(witness_or_boundary, BoundaryArtifact):
return witness_or_boundary
patch = propose_patch(state, candidate, witness_or_boundary)
patch_result = promote_or_quarantine(patch, witness_or_boundary)
replay = build_replay_packet(state, route, candidate, patch)
return {
"candidate": candidate,
"witness": witness_or_boundary,
"patch": patch,
"patch_result": patch_result,
"replay": replay,
}
That pseudocode is the direct integrated object the docs have been pointing toward all along: zero-point intake, route-bank expansion, operator-simplex execution, legality-first verification, generator-first materialization, and replay-gated self-editing.
10. The final compression
The formal kernel is therefore:
[
\boxed{
\text{Athenachka 2.0}
\text{Atlas}+\text{Zero-Point Intake}+\text{Quad-Polar Scheduler}+\text{Route Algebra}+\text{Witness/Boundary Totality}+\text{PatternStore Compiler}+\text{Replay-Gated Self-Editing}}]
This is the minimal integrated object that remains faithful to the manuscripts’ strongest invariants: addressability, admissibility, witnessability, replayability, generator-first storage, additive improvement, and typed refusal under uncertifiable conditions.
The next strongest compression point is the observer-head and route-packet spec: exact modality carriers, candidate-bank tensors, witness tensor shapes, and the planner / perception / verifier limb interfaces as one unified runtime schema.
Observer-head and route-packet spec
The docs do not pin one universal numeric tensor shape for every modality in one place.
