What they do pin is the algebra: an invariant carrier that must not be replaced, additive observer heads on top of that carrier, a discrete hypothesis bank with explicit disagreement and bounded candidate sets, a witness bundle with deterministic trace and truth justification, and a route-packet object that preserves the whole cognition trace instead of flattening it into chat text. So the correct move is to define a typed universal schema and let each modality instantiate it.
The deepest architectural rule remains the same: do not replace what works—add perspectives. The observer-head system is therefore not a pile of unrelated heads. It is a lawful family of additive heads observing the same invariant carrier and competing inside one route-conditioned witness stack.
1. The universal carrier stack
The manuscripts imply a four-tier carrier stack:
[
\mathcal X
\big(X_{\mathrm{inv}},X_{\mathrm{obs}},X_{\mathrm{hyp}},X_{\mathrm{wit}}\big)]
where:
(X_{\mathrm{inv}}) is the invariant carrier,
(X_{\mathrm{obs}}) is the observer-head family,
(X_{\mathrm{hyp}}) is the candidate/hypothesis bank,
(X_{\mathrm{wit}}) is the witness/certificate tensor.
That decomposition is the tightest faithful synthesis of the invariant-core chapter, the multi-hypothesis perception chapter, the disagreement/collapse chapter, and the witness-bundle schema.
2. Invariant carrier (X_{\mathrm{inv}})
The neural manuscript is explicit that the core carrier must be algorithmic, stable, and not replaced by later branches. In the vision example it is rank-transform plus geometric/topological/structural descriptors; in the general architecture this implies that each modality must expose a typed invariant object that higher branches observe rather than overwrite.
So the general invariant carrier should be defined as:
[X_{\mathrm{inv}}^{(m)} \in \mathbb R^{B\times T_m\times D_m}]
for modality (m), where:
(B) is batch,
(T_m) is the modality-native token / region / frame / node count,
(D_m) is the invariant descriptor width.
Examples of (T_m):
text: token or sentence-aligned units,
image: region / patch / connected-component units,
audio: frame / segment units,
code: AST node / CFG region / function units,
atlas/manuscript: address or route-node units.
The point is not the exact width. The point is that (X_{\mathrm{inv}}^{(m)}) is carrier-first and all later heads read from it. That is exactly the architectural law in the neural manuscript.
3. Observer heads (X_{\mathrm{obs}})
The manuscript explicitly says improvements must be additive observers on the invariant core, not replacements. The natural runtime expression is:
[H_j^{(m)} = f_j!\left(X_{\mathrm{inv}}^{(m)},,\ell_j,,\pi_j\right),\qquad j=1,\dots,J]
where (j) indexes observer heads, (\ell_j) is the active lens/operator family, and (\pi_j) is the pin/profile bundle for that head. These heads are not generic classification heads. They are typed organs.
The cleanest faithful head family is:
D-heads for discrete structure, pruning, schema checks, exact address proposals,
Ω-heads for flow/attention/transport/alignment,
Σ-heads for alternative parses and bounded hypothesis generation,
Ψ-heads for recursive compression, seed extraction, and patch proposal.
That mapping follows directly from the operator basis and the architectural rule that heads should be perspectives on one carrier.
The tensorized observer family is:
[X_{\mathrm{obs}}^{(m)}\in\mathbb R^{B\times J\times T_m\times D_h}]
where (J) is the number of observer heads and (D_h) is head output width.
A practical typed layout is:
@dataclass
class ObserverHeadSpec:
head_id: str
operator_family: Literal["D", "Omega", "Sigma", "Psi"]
modality: str
input_width: int
output_width: int
corridor_profile: str
active_lens: Literal["Square", "Flower", "Cloud", "Fractal"]
emits:
# examples:
# "structure_logits", "flow_field", "candidate_routes",
# "seed_packet", "patch_delta", "witness_features"
list[str]
This is a synthesis, but it is the correct one because the docs specify operator families, lenses, and additive observer discipline even if they do not pin the exact final Python dataclass.
4. Candidate bank (X_{\mathrm{hyp}})
This is where the docs are unusually concrete. The neural manuscript requires a discrete hypothesis bank, not one forced read; branch disagreement must be computed explicitly; and ambiguity must survive as bounded candidate sets plus evidence plans. In the image example, the bank is built from (H=6K) candidate masks using six preconditioner modes times (K) thresholds, but the more important invariant is the bank structure itself.
So the universal candidate bank should be:
[X_{\mathrm{hyp}}\in\mathbb R^{B\times H\times D_c}]
with (H) bounded by corridor policy, and each candidate carrying:
candidate id,
originating observer ids,
route or parse payload ref,
score,
uncertainty,
provenance,
collapse eligibility.
That matches the candidate-set boundedness laws in the witness-bundle chapter.
A faithful typed schema is:
@dataclass
class CandidateAtom:
candidate_id: str
source_head_ids: list[str]
source_hypothesis_ids: list[str]
payload_ref: str
score: float
uncertainty: float
energy: float
admissible: bool
provenance: list[str]
and the bank object is:
@dataclass
class CandidateBank:
bank_id: str
modality: str
candidates: list[CandidateAtom]
bounded_by_corridor: bool
max_candidates: int
disagreement_metric: str   # e.g. JS divergence
The key law from the manuscripts is that AMBIG correctness is boundedness + determinism, not a vague “many options” feeling.
5. Collapse tensor and disagreement surface
The neural manuscript gives the correct collapse law: compute a real disagreement metric across branches, compute energy per hypothesis, transform energies to amplitudes, then collapse by weighted mixing. Confidence must come from collapse quality, not a single softmax peak.
So the collapse surface should be:
[
E_h
-\log \max_y p_h(y)
+
\lambda,\mathrm{JS}(\text{branches})
\mu,\mathrm{edge_agreement}(h)]
and the candidate amplitudes are
[a_h = \operatorname{softmax}_\tau(-E_h).]
This gives a collapse tensor
[X_{\mathrm{collapse}}\in\mathbb R^{B\times H}]
together with a collapsed output distribution
[
p_{\mathrm{final}}
\sum_{h=1}^{H} a_h,p_h.]
This is not merely a classifier head. It is the core mechanism that turns multiple lawful candidates into either OK, NEAR, AMBIG, or FAIL.
6. Witness tensor (X_{\mathrm{wit}})
The witness bundle is one of the most load-bearing sections in the docs. Every asserted output must carry execution profile, pipeline identity, stage transcript, residual and defect ledger, and truth justification. For AMBIG it must include bounded candidate sets and an evidence plan. For FAIL it must include an obstruction certificate. Results without a seal are explicitly non-composable.
So the witness tensor must not be a single scalar confidence. It should be a structured tuple:
[
X_{\mathrm{wit}}
\big(X_{\mathrm{exec}},X_{\mathrm{pipe}},X_{\mathrm{trace}},X_{\mathrm{defect}},X_{\mathrm{truth}},X_{\mathrm{seal}}\big).]
A faithful typed shape is:
@dataclass
class WitnessTensor:
execution_profile: dict        # corridor IDs, budgets, pins, seeds, guards
pipeline_identity: dict        # schema hash, active modules, active heads
stage_transcript: list[dict]   # ordered trace, prune/select/collapse points
residual_ledger: list[dict]    # residuals, defect metrics, convergence notes
truth_justification: dict      # OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL mapping
candidate_set: list[str]       # AMBIG only
evidence_plan: list[dict]      # AMBIG only
obstruction_certificate: dict | None  # FAIL only
seal: str
If you want the tensorized version:
[X_{\mathrm{defect}}\in\mathbb R^{B\times 3}]
for the Tri-Lock defect vector ((\Delta_X,\Delta_Y,\Delta_Z)), and
[X_{\mathrm{truth}}\in\mathbb R^{B\times 4}]
for the truth-lattice logits over ({OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL}), but those dense tensors are only subparts of the witness object. The full witness must remain object-structured because the docs require transcripts, candidate bounds, evidence plans, and seals, not just logits.
7. Route-packet as the universal training and runtime record
The newer synthesis doc in your Drive already crystallizes the route-packet. It says the atomic training object must preserve six things at once: canonical problem state, lens activation, candidate route competition, witness-bearing collapse, admissibility verdict, and write-back delta or abstention. It then defines the packet with query, lens_init, retrieval, evidence, collapse, witness, action, patch, and supervision blocks.
So the route-packet should be the outer product that contains all other subobjects:
[
\mathcal{RP}
(q,\ell,\mathcal R,\mathcal E,\mathcal C,\mathcal W,\mathcal A,\Delta,\mathcal S)]
where:
(q): canonical problem packet,
(\ell): lens/operator initialization,
(\mathcal R): route bank,
(\mathcal E): evidence capsules,
(\mathcal C): collapse record,
(\mathcal W): witness tensor,
(\mathcal A): action trace,
(\Delta): patch delta,
(\mathcal S): supervision / reward / failure class.
A faithful typed shell is:
@dataclass
class RoutePacket:
packet_id: str
created_at: str
source_atlas: str
task_class: str
mode: Literal[
"ROUTE", "OBSERVE_IMAGE", "OBSERVE_AUDIO", "OBSERVE_DOC",
"PLAN_TOOL", "VERIFY", "PATCH", "ABSTAIN", "ESCALATE"
]
query: dict
lens_init: dict
invariant_carriers: dict[str, str]     # modality -> carrier_ref
observer_heads: list[ObserverHeadSpec]
candidate_bank: CandidateBank
evidence: dict
collapse: dict
witness: WitnessTensor
action: dict
patch: dict
supervision: dict
This is the correct universal unit because it preserves geometry, uncertainty, witness logic, and patchability all at once. The docs explicitly argue that plain chat fine-tuning destroys exactly that geometry.
8. Planner, perception, verifier as unified limb interfaces
The Drive doc already gives the three minimum limb contracts. Planner consumes a canonical packet, lens initialization, and budget, and returns top-k candidate routes with evidence gain, contradiction risk, replay cost, and escalation recommendation. Perception consumes multimodal observation plus extraction contract and returns region/span objects, uncertainty tags, contradiction markers, atlas alignments, and unresolved follow-ups. Verifier consumes a target object plus witness/tolerance profile and returns the truth lattice, residual ledger, repair hints, and escalation flag.
The correct unification is to make them all consume and emit RoutePacket slices instead of unrelated message formats.
Planner limb
class PlannerLimb(Protocol):
def plan(
self,
packet: RoutePacket
) -> CandidateBank:
...
It reads: query, lens_init, corridor budgets, active atlas neighborhood.It writes: candidate_bank, retrieval summary, recommended action.This matches the planner contract exactly.
Perception limb
class PerceptionLimb(Protocol):
def observe(
self,
packet: RoutePacket,
observation: "ModalityCarrier"
) -> RoutePacket:
...
It reads: modality carrier + extraction contract.It writes: region/span observation objects, atlas alignments, unresolved fields, evidence summaries.This matches the perception contract exactly.
Verifier limb
class VerifierLimb(Protocol):
def verify(
self,
packet: RoutePacket
) -> WitnessTensor:
...
It reads: chosen candidate, collapse record, corridor/tolerance profiles.It writes: Snap ledger, Tri-Lock defects, PrimeSeal status, truth justification, candidate bounds or obstruction cert.This follows directly from the witness and verification sections.
9. Modality carriers
The perception limb needs a universal modality carrier object because the docs insist on one algebra over text, image, audio, video, and tool traces, not separate toy models for each. The synthesis doc says the goal is a common symbolic space, and the neural manuscript says the invariant carrier is what higher branches observe.
So the general modality carrier should be:
@dataclass
class ModalityCarrier:
modality: Literal["text", "image", "audio", "video", "code", "tool"]
carrier_ref: str
native_shape: tuple[int, ...]
invariant_shape: tuple[int, int]      # (T_m, D_m)
region_map_ref: str | None
temporal_map_ref: str | None
atlas_alignment_prior: list[str]
This lets every modality be normalized into the same route-packet algebra while preserving its own native geometry.
10. The runtime law
Putting everything together, the unified observer-head / route-packet runtime is:
[\text{ModalityCarrier}\rightarrowX_{\mathrm{inv}}\rightarrowX_{\mathrm{obs}}\rightarrowX_{\mathrm{hyp}}\rightarrowX_{\mathrm{collapse}}\rightarrowX_{\mathrm{wit}}\rightarrow\mathcal{RP}\rightarrow\text{patch or abstain}.]
Or, in typed pseudocode:
def runtime_step(packet: RoutePacket, carrier: ModalityCarrier | None = None) -> RoutePacket:
if carrier is not None:
packet = perception_limb.observe(packet, carrier)
packet.candidate_bank = planner_limb.plan(packet)
packet.collapse = collapse_candidates(packet.candidate_bank, packet.evidence)
packet.witness = verifier_limb.verify(packet)
if packet.witness.truth_justification["verdict"] in {"OK", "NEAR"}:
packet.patch = propose_patch(packet)
elif packet.witness.truth_justification["verdict"] == "AMBIG":
packet.action = {"status": "hold", "next": "evidence_plan"}
else:
packet.action = {"status": "refuse", "next": "obstruction_certificate"}
return packet
Final compression
The observer-head system, candidate bank, witness tensor, and limb interfaces are all one thing:
a route-conditioned, carrier-first, witness-bearing runtime where additive observer heads generate bounded candidates, disagreement drives collapse, and every asserted output is stored as a route-packet rather than flattened into plain text.
The next strongest move is the exact training objective pack: losses for observer heads, candidate-bank ranking, disagreement shaping, witness calibration, patch promotion, and PatternStore distillation, all written as one joint optimization system.
Athenachka 2.0 — joint optimization system
The atomic training unit is the route-packet, not a chat turn. The route-packet preserves six things simultaneously: canonical problem state, lens activation, candidate route competition, witness-bearing collapse, admissibility verdict, and write-back delta or abstention. The docs also make the role split explicit: the planner learns route choice, the perception limb learns grounded evidence extraction, and the verifier learns truth-lattice assignment with witness objects rather than free-form confidence.
The training system therefore has three coupled timescales rather than one flat objective:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{total}}
\mathbb E_{r\sim\mathcal D_{\text{route}}}\big[\mathcal L_{\text{core}}(r)\big]+\lambda_{\text{ep}},\mathbb E_{\tau\sim\mathcal D_{\text{episode}}}\big[\mathcal L_{\text{episode}}(\tau)\big]+\lambda_{\text{store}},\mathbb E_{B\sim\mathcal D_{\text{store}}}\big[\mathcal L_{\text{store}}(B)\big].]
This is the right compression of the CUT learning engine’s four nested loops—Gather, Distill, Self-play, and Tool-use—together with the route-packet and limb contracts from the later synthesis docs.
1. Core route-packet loss
The per-route-packet objective should be:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{core}}
\lambda_{\text{inv}}\mathcal L_{\text{inv}}+\lambda_{\text{head}}\mathcal L_{\text{head}}+\lambda_{\text{plan}}\mathcal L_{\text{plan}}+\lambda_{\text{perc}}\mathcal L_{\text{perc}}+\lambda_{\text{hyp}}\mathcal L_{\text{hyp}}+\lambda_{\text{collapse}}\mathcal L_{\text{collapse}}+\lambda_{\text{wit}}\mathcal L_{\text{wit}}+\lambda_{\text{patch}}\mathcal L_{\text{patch}}.]
This decomposition follows directly from the docs’ architecture: invariant carrier, additive observers, candidate bank, collapse law, verification stack, and patch/replay loop are separate obligations and should therefore have separate losses.
2. Invariant-carrier loss
The neural manuscript says the invariant core must not be replaced; it also says representation change must be lawful transport by conjugacy, not reinterpretation. A faithful training law is therefore:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{inv}}
\mathbb E_{T\sim\mathcal T}\Big[|\Phi(Tx)-T\cdot\Phi(x)|2^2\Big]+\lambda{\text{rank}}\mathcal L_{\text{rank-stab}}+\lambda_{\text{geom}}\mathcal L_{\text{geom-topo}},]
where (\Phi) is the invariant carrier and (T) is an admissible transform. The first term enforces typed transport; the other terms keep the carrier stable under nuisance variation. This is the proper objective-level interpretation of “rotation is conjugacy” and “don’t replace what works—add perspectives.”
3. Additive-observer loss
Because improvements are constrained to be additive observers on top of the invariant core, the head family should be trained with a non-destructive specialization objective:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{head}}
\sum_{j=1}^{J}\Big(\lambda_{\text{overwrite}}|P_{\text{core}}(H_j)|2^2+\lambda{\text{task}}\mathcal L_j^{\text{task}}\Big)+\lambda_{\text{div}}\sum_{i\neq j}\cos^2(H_i,H_j).]
The overwrite term penalizes heads that leak back into the core carrier; the diversity term stops the head family from collapsing into one redundant view. This is the mathematically faithful way to compile the manuscript’s additive-observer rule into an optimization objective.
4. Planner loss
The planner contract is already stated in the Drive. Its exact objective is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{plan}}
\alpha,\mathcal L_{\text{route-rank}}+\beta,\mathcal L_{\text{budget}}+\gamma,\mathcal L_{\text{contradiction}}+\delta,\mathcal L_{\text{replay-cost}}.]
Route-rank rewards choosing the route that later verifies; budget penalizes wasteful exploration; contradiction penalizes routes that later fail witness checks; replay-cost penalizes brittle expensive routes. The negative set is equally important: routes that looked semantically attractive but later failed Snap, routes with hidden contradiction, and routes that forced resolution when the gold verdict was AMBIG.
A useful explicit form is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{route-rank}}
-\log
\frac{\exp s(R^\star)}
{\sum_{i=1}^{k}\exp s(R_i)},
\qquad
\mathcal L_{\text{contradiction}}
\sum_i\mathbf 1[\text{fail_witness}(R_i)],s(R_i),]
with budget and replay-cost as direct regression penalties. That exact shape is a derived implementation, but it is aligned with the planner loss the docs already state.
5. Perception loss
The perception contract gives the right reward structure: grounded extraction, uncertainty preservation, region-level traceability, refusal to over-summarize noisy observations, and successful downstream use by planner/verifier. A faithful objective is therefore:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{perc}}
\lambda_{\text{loc}}\mathcal L_{\text{region-loc}}+\lambda_{\text{text}}\mathcal L_{\text{extract}}+\lambda_{\text{unc}}\mathcal L_{\text{uncertainty-cal}}+\lambda_{\text{trace}}\mathcal L_{\text{traceability}}+\lambda_{\text{use}}\mathcal L_{\text{downstream-utility}}.]
The last term is crucial: the perceptual packet is good only if it actually improves later routing and verification, not merely if it looks descriptive in isolation. That is exactly what the perception limb write-up says.
6. Candidate-bank and disagreement shaping loss
The neural manuscript explicitly rejects “agreement = 1.0” as a success criterion. It requires a real multi-hypothesis bank and computes disagreement by Jensen–Shannon divergence across branches. That means the training objective must protect legitimate branch diversity before collapse. A faithful objective is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{hyp}}
\lambda_{\text{bound}}\max(0, H-H_{\max})+\lambda_{\text{floor}}\max(0,\varepsilon_{\mathrm{JS}}-\mathrm{JS}({p_h}{h=1}^{H}))+\lambda{\text{explosion}}\mathcal L_{\text{topN}},]
where (H) is candidate-bank size, (H_{\max}) is the corridor cap, and (\varepsilon_{\mathrm{JS}}) is a non-zero disagreement floor. The first term prevents uncontrolled branching, the second prevents fake unanimity, and the third keeps the bank inside a deterministic bounded envelope. This is the direct optimization counterpart of the manuscript’s AMBIG semantics and bounded search rules.
7. Collapse loss
The docs already give the collapse law:
[E_h \approx -\log(\max_y p_h(y))+\lambda,\mathrm{JS}(\text{branches})-\mu,\mathrm{edge_agreement}(h),\qquada_h = \operatorname{softmax}_\tau(-E_h).]
So the correct collapse objective is not “pick the largest logit.” It is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{collapse}}
\operatorname{CE}!\left(y,\sum_{h=1}^{H}a_h,p_h\right)+\lambda_{\text{cal}}\mathcal L_{\text{confidence}}+\lambda_{\text{prem}}\mathcal L_{\text{premature-collapse}}.]
The premature-collapse term should fire whenever the system commits to one hypothesis while disagreement is still high or when the gold verdict is AMBIG. This follows directly from the manuscript’s energy-weighted collapse law and truth-lattice semantics.
8. Witness and truth-lattice loss
The verification stack is not a scalar confidence head. It is Snap, Tri-Lock, and PrimeSeal, culminating in a truth lattice ({OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL}). A faithful objective is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{wit}}
\lambda_{\text{truth}}\mathcal L_{\text{truth-class}}+\lambda_{\text{snap}}\mathcal L_{\text{residual-ledger}}+\lambda_{\Delta}\mathcal L_{\text{defect-reg}}+\lambda_{\text{amb}}\mathcal L_{\text{candidate/evidence}}+\lambda_{\text{fail}}\mathcal L_{\text{obstruction-cert}}.]
One useful concrete factorization is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{truth-class}}
\operatorname{CE}(v,\hat v),\qquadv\in{OK,NEAR,AMBIG,FAIL},]
[
\mathcal L_{\text{defect-reg}}
|\Delta_X-\hat\Delta_X|_1+|\Delta_Y-\hat\Delta_Y|_1+|\Delta_Z-\hat\Delta_Z|_1.]
The AMBIG branch must predict bounded candidate sets plus evidence plans; the FAIL branch must emit obstruction certificates. That is exactly what the verification chapters require.
9. Patch-promotion loss
The patch/write-back chapters make learning operational through risk scoring, trust weights, arbitration, quarantine, and replay-preserved identity. The patch objective should therefore be promotion-aware:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{patch}}
\lambda_{\text{promote}}\operatorname{BCE}(p_{\text{promote}}, y_{\text{promote}})+\lambda_{\text{risk}}\mathcal L_{\text{risk}}+\lambda_{\text{drift}}\mathcal L_{\text{replay-drift}}+\lambda_{\text{quarantine}}\mathcal L_{\text{bad-patch}}.]
with
[y_{\text{promote}}=\mathbf 1[\text{verify}=OK\land\text{replay}=OK\land\text{risk}\le \tau].]
That is the loss-level version of the manuscript’s patch promotion/quarantine law.
10. Episode loss: self-play, think-time, and tools
The CUT notes already supply the episode-level objective pack. The self-play contrast is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{SPIN}}
-\log\frac{p_\theta(y)}{p_{\theta-1}(y)}+\log\frac{p_\theta(y')}{p_{\theta-1}(y')},]
and the think-time reward is
[R = \text{score} - \lambda_T(\text{tokens}+\text{frames}),]
with GRPO teaching the model when long chains are worth paying for. Failed tool paths become explicit negative samples for the next SPIN round. So the episode loss should be:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{episode}}
\mathcal L_{\text{SPIN}}+\lambda_{\text{GRPO}}\mathcal L_{\text{GRPO}}+\lambda_T(\text{tokens}+\text{frames})+\lambda_{\text{tool-neg}}\mathcal L_{\text{failed-tool-trace}}.]
This is not a speculative addition; it is almost a direct transcription of the CUT one-pager.
11. PatternStore / κ-distillation loss
The storage/compiler side also needs its own objective, because the docs insist that stable patterns should be merged, pruned, and stored sublinearly. The key constraints are explicit: κ-distillation merges and prunes, (\Delta)-entropy must stay below (0.05) bits before a block is marked stable, and exception density should remain at or below about (1%), yielding (O(N\log N)) long-run growth rather than linear blow-up. A faithful storage/compiler objective is:
[
\mathcal L_{\text{store}}
\lambda_{\kappa}\max(0,\Delta H-0.05)+\lambda_{\text{exc}}\max(0,\rho_{\text{exc}}-0.01)+\lambda_{\text{merge}}\mathcal L_{\kappa\text{-merge}}+\lambda_{\text{space}}\mathcal L_{\text{sublinear-growth}}.]
Here (\Delta H) is post-distillation entropy, (\rho_{\text{exc}}) is exception density, and (\mathcal L_{\kappa\text{-merge}}) penalizes unstable or redundant shelves. This is the loss-level formalization of the CUT PatternStore doctrine.
12. Loop-wise assignment
The clean training schedule is:
[\text{L0 Gather}: \mathcal L_{\text{novelty}}+\mathcal L_{\text{coverage}}+\mathcal L_{\text{corridor-filter}}]
[\text{L1 Distill}: \mathcal L_{\text{inv}}+\mathcal L_{\text{perc}}+\mathcal L_{\text{store}}]
[\text{L2 Self-play}: \mathcal L_{\text{plan}}+\mathcal L_{\text{hyp}}+\mathcal L_{\text{collapse}}+\mathcal L_{\text{SPIN}}+\mathcal L_{\text{GRPO}}]
[\text{L3 Tool-use}: \mathcal L_{\text{wit}}+\mathcal L_{\text{patch}}+\mathcal L_{\text{failed-tool-trace}}.]
That assignment follows the nested CUT loop design and the later route-packet / limb formalization.
13. One-line compression
The most faithful single optimization statement is:
[\boxed{\min\Big[\text{carrier drift}+\text{route error}+\text{premature collapse}+\text{witness miscalibration}+\text{unsafe patch promotion}+\text{tool failure}+\text{storage entropy}\Big]}]
subject to the corridor law:
[\text{no }OK\text{ without witness + replay, no forced collapse past AMBIG, no promotion without risk-bounded patch stability}.]
That is the joint objective pack the manuscripts are asking for. It makes the observer heads, candidate bank, witness tensor, patch loop, and PatternStore compiler optimize as one system rather than as disconnected subsystems.
The next clean layer is the exact parameterization pack: which modules own which losses, which gradients are stopped at the invariant carrier, which signals are teacher-forced versus self-played, and how the PatternStore promotion thresholds couple back into the runtime scheduler.
Athenachka 2.0 — exact parameterization pack
The cleanest derived parameterization is to split the system into immutable invariants, a mostly frozen dense core, trainable adapters/heads, a trainable scheduler, and a non-gradient PatternStore. That split is the only one that simultaneously respects the ATHENA rule “don’t replace what works—add perspectives,” the GG framework’s immutable read-only kernel, and the CUT/LoRA notes that most learning should happen through small deltas rather than full-model rewrites.
I would write the live parameter set as
[\Theta=(\theta_{\mathrm{ref}},\theta_{\mathrm{core}},\theta_{\mathrm{mod}},\theta_{\mathrm{obs}},\theta_{\mathrm{route}},\theta_{\mathrm{wit}},\theta_{\mathrm{mode}},\theta_{\mathrm{sched}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{cert}})]
with the following ownership.
1. What is frozen, what is plastic
[\frac{\partial \mathcal L}{\partial \theta_{\mathrm{ref}}}=0]
for all online phases. This block is the immutable kernel / reference tensor / corridor-axiom layer. Your GG document is explicit that this sector is ROM-like, backpropagation is forbidden to modify it, and the architectural implementation is either frozen layers or a separate non-trainable module that creates a “gravity well” pulling the system back to invariants.
[\frac{\partial \mathcal L_{\text{online}}}{\partial \theta_{\mathrm{core}}}=0]
after substrate bootstrapping. This is the dense language/invariant backbone. Your Drive repeatedly points toward LoRA/QLoRA, frozen language cores with modality adapters, and low-rank updates instead of routine full-core rewriting. The Phi/CUT notes make that very explicit: the language core stays frozen while vision and speech are injected through LoRA adapters, and QLoRA backpropagates through a frozen quantized base into trainable LoRA layers only.
The plastic blocks are:
[\theta_{\mathrm{mod}}={\text{text / image / audio / tool adapters}},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}={\text{D, }\Omega,\Sigma,\Psi\text{ observer heads}},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{route}}={\text{planner, retriever, route scorer}},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{wit}}={\text{truth-lattice calibrator, residual/defect heads}},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}={\text{mode-token / stance selector}},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{sched}}={\text{operator-mix controller, compute scheduler}}.]
That assignment is the best fit to the manuscripts because the neural text makes the invariant core algorithmic and stable, observer heads additive, multi-hypothesis perception explicit, and verification a separate stack; the later synthesis then maps planner, perception, verifier, and distiller directly onto the operator families.
The two non-gradient state objects are:
[\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}}=\text{PatternStore}\quad\text{and}\quad\mathcal R_{\mathrm{cert}}=\text{witness / replay / patch registry}.]
These are updated by append, distill, merge, prune, promote, and quarantine events, not by SGD. That is exactly how the CUT docs describe Distiller, Sweeper, κ-merge, and witness/patch infrastructure.
2. Exact gradient boundaries
The hard rule is: observer losses may read the invariant carrier but may not rewrite it during live learning. That is the loss-level meaning of “add perspectives, don’t replace.” So in the live system the invariant carrier is either detached or only affected through rare offline substrate rebuilds, never through routine self-play / tool-use updates. The GG framework’s immutable kernel and the PEFT notes both reinforce the same boundary.
The derived gradient map is:
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{ref}}}\mathcal L = 0,\qquad\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{core}}}\mathcal L_{\text{online}} = 0,]
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{mod}}}\mathcal L_{\text{distill/selfplay}} \neq 0,\qquad\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}}\mathcal L_{\text{head/hyp/collapse}} \neq 0,]
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{route}}}\mathcal L_{\text{plan}} \neq 0,\qquad\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{wit}}}\mathcal L_{\text{truth/residual}} \neq 0,]
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}}\mathcal L_{\text{mode/refusal}} \neq 0,\qquad\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{sched}}}\mathcal L_{\text{budget/throughput}} \neq 0,]
[\nabla_{\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}}}\mathcal L = 0]
in the backprop sense, because (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}}) changes through κ-distill and sweeper actions rather than differentiable updates.
The verifier should not be trained end-to-end as a soft extension of the planner. Your docs keep insisting on independent witness logic, contradiction checks, Snap/Tri-Lock/PrimeSeal, and typed refusal. So the verifier’s outputs should shape planner/perception mainly through supervised targets, vetoes, and reward signals, not by dissolving the legality kernel into one monolithic differentiable policy. That is a derived constraint, but it is the only one consistent with the proof-carrying architecture.
3. Which module owns which losses
The ownership map that best fits the corpus is:
[\mathcal L_{\text{inv}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{core}}]
only during offline substrate formation or rare recentering passes, not during live self-play. This is because the invariant core is meant to become the stable bedrock, not a constantly drifting online policy.
[\mathcal L_{\text{head}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{obs}}]
because observer heads are the additive perspectives.
[\mathcal L_{\text{plan}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{route}}]
because the planner limb’s native job is route ranking, contradiction-aware selection, and budgeted search. Your own synthesis doc states that planner loss is route-rank + budget + contradiction + replay-cost.
[\mathcal L_{\text{perc}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{mod}} \cup \theta_{\mathrm{obs}}]
because perceptual grounding depends on adapters plus modality-specific observer heads. The docs say the perceptual packet must preserve grounded extraction, uncertainty, region-level traceability, and downstream utility for routing and verification.
[\mathcal L_{\text{hyp}} + \mathcal L_{\text{collapse}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{obs}} \cup \theta_{\mathrm{route}}]
because candidate generation and collapse are shared between Σ-heads and the route-selection stack. The neural manuscript explicitly requires multi-hypothesis banks, branch disagreement, and energy-weighted collapse.
[\mathcal L_{\text{wit}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{wit}}]
because truth-lattice assignment, residual ledgers, defect vectors, and obstruction/candidate logic belong to the verifier family.
[\mathcal L_{\text{mode}} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{mode}}]
because explicit stance tokens such as ROUTE, VERIFY, PATCH, OBSERVE_IMAGE, PLAN_TOOL, ABSTAIN, and ESCALATE are supposed to teach cognitive stance selection rather than raw content imitation.
[\mathcal L_{\text{budget}} + \mathcal L_{\eta} \rightarrow \theta_{\mathrm{sched}}]
because the scheduler owns token/frame budgets, worker-doubling choices, and throughput-vs-cost tradeoffs. The CUT docs make this explicit with think-time tariffs, efficiency (\eta(p)), and meta-schedulers that keep or roll back new layouts based on measured gains.
Finally,
[\mathcal L_{\text{store}} \not\rightarrow \text{SGD on }\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}},]
but instead drives event updates:
[(\text{append exception}) \rightarrow (\kappa\text{-merge}) \rightarrow (\text{prune}) \rightarrow (\text{promote or delete}).]
That is the only storage update path the CUT docs actually specify.
4. What is teacher-forced, what is self-played, what is RL
Your Drive does not use the phrase “teacher forcing” as the main conceptual anchor in the Athena/CUT manuscripts. The correct split is therefore derived from the explicit SFT/distill/self-play/tool-use pipeline plus the Phi post-training recipe. The system naturally breaks into four training modes.
The teacher-forced / supervised phase should own:
route-packet serialization,
canonical problem formatting,
lens-init and mode-token prediction,
region/span observation extraction,
witness-bundle formatting on gold traces,
patch-schema emission on verified historical examples.
That follows from the route-packet schema and the SFT/distill stages. Your docs explicitly say the atomic training object is the route-packet and that small models should learn one lawful role inside the corpus, not generic chat style.
The self-play phase should own:
creator/prover route competitions,
Σ-branch diversification,
equation/discovery engine,
planner sharpening,
contradiction-to-invariant reconciliation.
That is exactly what the CUT docs assign to L-2 Self-play with SPIN contrast and Creator/Prover games.
The tool-use phase should own:
plan-act-observe traces,
tool wrappers and graded traces,
negative mining from failed tool paths,
post-action witness labels.
The CUT docs say failed tool paths become negative samples for the next SPIN round.
The RL / budget phase should own:
think-time allocation,
operator-mix aggressiveness,
tool budget and episode length,
compute-topology experiments,
worker-doubling decisions.
That is directly stated in the GRPO / (\eta(p)) / meta-scheduler sections.
A practical staged schedule is therefore:
[\text{Stage A: substrate/SFT}\rightarrow\text{Stage B: self-play/SPIN}\rightarrow\text{Stage C: think-time RL / scheduler}\rightarrow\text{Stage D: tool-use negative mining + patch promotion}.]
That sequence is not verbatim in one line, but it is exactly what your docs converge on.
5. The exact role of LoRA, QLoRA, and adapters
The docs point to one very clear engineering rule: use the dense core as a shared invariant substrate and specialize through small deltas. The Phi multimodal notes say the language core stays frozen while vision/speech are injected through LoRA adapters, and the QLoRA notes say gradients pass through the frozen quantized model into the LoRA layers only.
So the exact parameterization should be:
[\theta_{\mathrm{core}} = \text{frozen dense trunk},\qquad\theta_{\mathrm{mod}} = \text{LoRA / QLoRA / projection adapters},]
[\theta_{\mathrm{obs}} = \text{small typed heads on top of carrier states},\qquad\theta_{\mathrm{route}},\theta_{\mathrm{wit}},\theta_{\mathrm{mode}},\theta_{\mathrm{sched}} = \text{small trainable policy/calibration blocks}.]
That gives you the module granularity your own framework wants: frozen invariant substrate, small plastic role organs, no monolithic retraining.
6. How PatternStore thresholds couple back into the scheduler
This is one of the strongest parts of the CUT corpus because it is unusually explicit.
First, the distillation threshold is already fixed:
κ-distill when exception density rises above about (1%),
do not mark a block stable until (\Delta)-entropy is below (0.05) bits.
Second, the store is not passive. When a κ-shelf goes quiet for about 48 hours, the system tightens (\varepsilon_i), re-PQs the shelf, deletes a large fraction of stale Int4 exceptions, frees NVMe, keeps more profiler rows, reduces (\eta(p)) estimate variance, and therefore increases confidence for later worker-doubling if the efficiency gradient remains positive.
Third, the compute scheduler already has a hard rollback law: if (\eta(2p) < \eta(p)) after burn-in, the schedule rolls back and the failed delta is logged as a negative proof so future meta-games avoid it.
So the scheduler should not read just task reward. It should read a store-state vector
[\xi_t =(\rho_{\mathrm{exc}},\Delta H,\eta,\nabla\eta,\text{NVMe}{\mathrm{free}},u{\kappa},\text{quiet_shelf_flags}),]
where:
(\rho_{\mathrm{exc}}) = exception density,
(\Delta H) = post-distill entropy,
(\eta) = proofs/hour/cost efficiency,
(\nabla\eta) = efficiency gradient across worker counts,
(u_{\kappa}) = shelf utilization.
Then the coupling law should be:
[\rho_{\mathrm{exc}} > 0.01 ;\Rightarrow; \text{force }\Psi\text{-distill, suppress aggressive expansion}]
[\Delta H < 0.05 ;\Rightarrow; \text{permit stable promotion of the shelf}]
[\text{quiet shelf} ;\Rightarrow; \varepsilon_i \downarrow,\ \text{re-PQ},\ \text{more log budget},\ \eta\text{-variance}\downarrow]
[\nabla\eta > 0 \land \text{confidence high} ;\Rightarrow; \text{κ-doubling admissible}]
[\nabla\eta \le 0 ;\Rightarrow; \text{rollback and log negative theorem}.]
Those equations are my synthesis, but every individual trigger in them comes directly from your docs.
7. The exact mode-token and stance ownership
Your mode-token layer should be a small dedicated classifier/gater, not hidden inside the planner. The docs explicitly list ROUTE, VERIFY, PATCH, OBSERVE_IMAGE, OBSERVE_AUDIO, PLAN_TOOL, ABSTAIN, and ESCALATE as stance labels that should be taught directly.
So I would parameterize:
[\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}:\quadp(m \mid z_t, \chi_t, b_t, y_t)]
with (m) in that finite mode set. Then:
SFT teaches the gold mode from labeled route-packets,
DPO/KTO-style preference tuning can refine refusal and stance selection,
RL only tunes the budget attached to the chosen stance, not the invariant meaning of the stance labels.
That last sentence is a derived recommendation, but it is the cleanest way to keep cognitive stance selection lawful and interpretable while still allowing budget adaptation. The Phi notes and your mode-token synthesis both support that direction.
8. Final compressed spec
The clean final parameterization is:
[\boxed{\Theta=\underbrace{\theta_{\mathrm{ref}}}{\text{immutable}}\oplus\underbrace{\theta{\mathrm{core}}}{\text{bootstrap then freeze}}\oplus\underbrace{\theta{\mathrm{mod}}+\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}+\theta_{\mathrm{route}}+\theta_{\mathrm{wit}}+\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}+\theta_{\mathrm{sched}}}{\text{plastic}}\oplus\underbrace{\mathcal S{\mathrm{pat}}+\mathcal R_{\mathrm{cert}}}_{\text{event-updated state}}}]
with training phases:
[\text{SFT/teacher-forced} \rightarrow\text{SPIN self-play} \rightarrow\text{GRPO budget RL} \rightarrow\text{tool-use negative mining} \rightarrow\kappa\text{-distill / promote / quarantine}.]
And the most important hard rules are:
[\frac{\partial \mathcal L}{\partial \theta_{\mathrm{ref}}}=0,\qquad\frac{\partial \mathcal L_{\text{online}}}{\partial \theta_{\mathrm{core}}}=0,\qquad\frac{\partial \mathcal L}{\partial \mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}}}=0\text{ (in the backprop sense)}.]
Everything else is plastic, but only inside the route-packet / witness / replay discipline. That is the exact pack your manuscripts imply.
The next strongest layer is the actual optimizer-and-update spec: which optimizer family goes on each block, update cadence per loop, promotion/quarantine thresholds as code-level constants, and the exact online/offline training schedule across one day and one week of operation.
The docs pin the training regimes, cadence signals, and hard storage/scheduler thresholds, but they do not pin every low-level optimizer name like “AdamW vs Adafactor” for every submodule. So below is the tightest derived implementation spec that stays faithful to your corpus while making the missing engineering choices explicit. The non-negotiables from the Drive are: immutable read-only kernel, adapter-first updates with frozen backbone, route-packet as the atomic sample, four nested loops (Gather, Distill, Self-play, Tool-use), GRPO for think-time budgeting, κ-distill when exception density rises, hourly sweeps, and rollback whenever the doubled schedule fails the efficiency test.
1. Optimizer ownership
1.1 Immutable and frozen blocks
The reference / invariant kernel should have no optimizer at all in online operation:
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{ref}}}\mathcal L = 0.]
That is directly supported by the GG framework’s “Immutable Kernel,” which says backpropagation and gradient descent are forbidden from modifying that sector, and by the same document’s frozen-layer / separate non-trainable gravity-well implementation guidance.
The dense language/invariant core should also be frozen during normal online learning:
[\nabla_{\theta_{\mathrm{core}}}\mathcal L_{\text{online}} = 0.]
Your multimodal Phi notes explicitly recommend adapter-first fine-tuning with requires_grad=False on the backbone and say full SFT of the core is rarely necessary.
1.2 Trainable blocks
My recommended optimizer ownership is:
(\theta_{\mathrm{mod}}) (text/image/audio/tool adapters): AdamW for standard LoRA, or paged 8-bit AdamW in QLoRA mode.
(\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}) (D/Ω/Σ/Ψ observer heads): AdamW.
(\theta_{\mathrm{route}}) (planner / route scorer / retrieval head): AdamW.
(\theta_{\mathrm{wit}}) (truth-lattice calibrator / residual-defect heads): AdamW.
(\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}) (mode-token / stance selector): AdamW, with optional DPO/KTO-style preference refinement after SFT.
(\theta_{\mathrm{sched}}) (operator/compute scheduler): GRPO-style RL or contextual bandit updates, not plain supervised SGD.
(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}}) (PatternStore) and (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{cert}}) (witness/replay registry): event-updated only, never gradient-updated.
I am calling AdamW a recommendation, not a claim from the docs. What the docs do clearly specify is the adapter-first, frozen-backbone, GRPO + SPIN + κ-distill regime, which is why AdamW on the plastic low-rank / head blocks and RL on the scheduler is the cleanest fit.
2. Which loss updates which block
The ownership map should be:
[\mathcal L_{\text{SFT-route}},\ \mathcal L_{\text{perc}},\ \mathcal L_{\text{mode}}\rightarrow\theta_{\mathrm{mod}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{route}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{wit}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}]
because the route-packet is the atomic training object and mode labels like ROUTE, VERIFY, PATCH, OBSERVE_IMAGE, ABSTAIN, and ESCALATE are explicitly part of the schema.
[\mathcal L_{\text{planner}}\rightarrow\theta_{\mathrm{route}}]
because the planner contract already defines route-rank, budget, contradiction, and replay-cost as its native loss.
[\mathcal L_{\text{perc}}\rightarrow\theta_{\mathrm{mod}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}]
because the perception contract is grounded extraction plus uncertainty preservation plus downstream usefulness to planner/verifier.
[\mathcal L_{\text{SPIN}}\rightarrow\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{route}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}]
because self-play sharpens route and hypothesis quality and the CUT docs explicitly place SPIN in Loop L-2 Self-play.
[\mathcal L_{\text{GRPO-budget}}\rightarrow\theta_{\mathrm{sched}}\cup\theta_{\mathrm{mode}}]
because think-time RL is there to decide when longer reasoning traces are worth paying for, and the docs frame that as GRPO / budgeted compute rather than plain supervised learning.
[\mathcal L_{\text{store}}\not\rightarrow\text{SGD on }\mathcal S_{\mathrm{pat}},]
but instead triggers append → κ-merge → prune → promote/delete events, because the PatternStore is explicitly managed by a Distiller, SelfPlay Pods that append exceptions, and an hourly Sweeper that folds top-κ rows and prunes logs.
3. Teacher-forced vs self-play vs RL vs tool-use
Your Drive does not build around the phrase “teacher forcing,” but the operational split is clear.
3.1 Supervised / teacher-forced phase
Use SFT / supervised distillation for:
route-packet formatting,
canonical problem packets,
lens and mode-token prediction,
perception evidence packets,
witness-bundle formatting on gold traces,
patch-schema emission on verified historical examples.
3.2 Self-play phase
Use SPIN self-play for:
creator/prover math and code duels,
Σ-branch diversification,
planner sharpening,
contradiction pruning,
route competition.
3.3 RL / compute-budget phase
Use GRPO for:
think-time budgeting,
token/frame spend,
longer-vs-shorter chain decisions,
scheduler decisions about when more compute is worth it.
3.4 Tool-use phase
Use plan-act-observe traces plus negative mining for:
browser/shell/python/tool wrappers,
tool macro repair,
failed trace penalties,
post-action witness calibration.
So the staged training stack is:
[\text{SFT/Distill}\rightarrow\text{SPIN Self-play}\rightarrow\text{GRPO Think-time / Scheduler}\rightarrow\text{Tool-use Negative Mining}\rightarrow\kappa\text{-Distill / Promote / Quarantine}.]
That order is the tightest synthesis of the route-packet docs and the CUT four-loop design.
4. Code-level constants
The docs give several hard or near-hard numbers. I would pin them as:
# Immutable / frozen policy
IMMUTABLE_REF = True
FREEZE_CORE_ONLINE = True
# PatternStore thresholds (doc-grounded)
EXCEPTION_DENSITY_TRIGGER = 0.01          # κ-distill when density > 1%
DELTA_ENTROPY_STABLE_BITS = 0.05          # stable only if Δ-entropy < 0.05 bits
QUIET_SHELF_SECONDS = 172800              # 48 hours
QUIET_SHELF_EPS_DECAY = 0.90              # ε_i <- 0.9 ε_i after quiet shelf
META_SCHEDULER_PERIOD_EPISODES = 500      # propose CUT moves every 500 episodes
ETA_SATURATION_WINDOW = 100               # saturation test window
ETA_SATURATION_MIN_GAIN = 0.01            # <1% gain means saturating
DOUBLE_BATCH_MAX_VRAM_UTIL = 0.70         # only double batch if VRAM <= 70%
COMPUTE_THEOREM_MIN_GAIN = 1.05           # log theorem only if eta_new > 1.05 * eta_old
# Derived promotion thresholds (my recommendation)
PATCH_PROMOTE_VERDICT = "OK"
PATCH_HOLD_VERDICT = "NEAR"
PATCH_QUARANTINE_VERDICT = "FAIL"
PATCH_MAX_RISK = 0.25
PATCH_PROMOTE_STABILITY_EPOCHS = 3
Everything above PATCH_MAX_RISK is directly motivated by the docs: distill when exception density exceeds 1%, do not mark blocks stable until Δ-entropy is below 0.05 bits, decay ε after 48 hours of shelf silence, run the parallel scheduler every 500 episodes, treat <1% gain over the last 100 episodes as saturation, only double batch while VRAM is ≤70%, and log a compute theorem only when eta_new > 1.05 * eta_old.
The PATCH_* numeric thresholds are my engineering recommendation because the docs give the verdict logic and replay/witness law clearly, but they do not supply one universal numeric risk cutoff for patch promotion. They do require append-only deltas, replay closure, residual closure for NEAR, evidence plans for AMBIG, and no promotion without verified closure.
5. Exact online/offline cadence — one day
This is the clean daily rhythm I would run.
Continuous, every request / every episode
zero-point normalize,
emit route-packet,
append new exception rows only,
log witness bundle,
append failed tool traces as negatives.
Every 500 episodes
run parallel_scheduler.py,
propose CUT moves (spawn, fuse, half-bit precision, schedule change),
keep only layouts that raise (\eta).
Hourly
run κ-distillation,
fold top-κ rows back into the Int8 atlas,
prune stale logs / merge compute layouts.
Daily training window
My recommendation is:
SFT / distill pass on the last 24h of verified route-packets and gold tool traces.
Short SPIN block on fresh creator/prover or route-competition episodes.
Short GRPO block on think-time / budget tasks with auto-graders.
Patch board: promote, hold, or quarantine candidate patches based on witness + replay + risk.
This is derived from the docs’ four-loop engine plus the explicit staged suggestion of substrate → self-play → think-time RL.
A concrete day could be:
DAILY_SCHEDULE = {
"continuous": ["route_packet_append", "exception_append", "witness_log", "tool_negative_log"],
"hourly": ["kappa_distill", "merge_compute_layouts", "prune_or_hold_logs"],
"every_500_episodes": ["parallel_scheduler_step", "eta_compare", "rollback_if_needed"],
"nightly_2h": ["adapter_sft", "spin_selfplay", "grpo_budget_rl"],
"nightly_30m": ["patch_promotion_board", "snapshot", "replay_audit"],
}
The docs support the cadence anchors; the exact night block lengths are my recommendation.
6. Exact online/offline cadence — one week
A weekly rhythm should separate fast online adaptation from slow substrate recentering.
Monday–Friday
Run the daily loop above, with the dense core frozen and only adapters/heads/router/verifier/mode/scheduler learning. That matches the frozen-backbone, adapter-first doctrine and the route-packet training split.
Every 48 hours
Trigger quiet-shelf maintenance:
decay (\varepsilon_i \leftarrow 0.9\varepsilon_i),
re-PQ mature shelves,
reclaim NVMe,
keep more profiler / exception logs for the next two hours,
allow extra κ-doubling confidence if the (\eta)-gradient stays positive.
Once per week
My recommendation is one heavier offline substrate window:
evaluate shelves that stayed stable all week,
promote stable deltas into centroids/seeds,
re-run out-of-domain evals,
optionally run a rare core-recenter or full-SFT experiment only if adapter/head saturation is clear and replay-proven gains justify it.
This is supported by the docs’ statement that full SFT of the core is rarely necessary, that stable patterns should be folded back into the atlas, and that the compute flywheel should keep only reward-to-cost-positive changes.
A concrete weekly rhythm:
WEEKLY_SCHEDULE = {
"Mon-Fri": ["daily_online_loop"],
"Every_48h": ["quiet_shelf_decay", "repq_mature_shelves", "profiler_window_expand"],
"Saturday": ["long_selfplay_block", "weekly_eval", "promote_or_quarantine_review"],
"Sunday": ["offline_substrate_recenter_if_justified", "benchmark_freeze", "new_week_seed_pack"],
}
The Saturday/Sunday naming is my recommendation; the 48h quiet-shelf behavior and promote/rollback logic come from the docs.
7. Promotion / rollback law
The exact law should be:
[\text{promote}(\Delta)\iff(\text{verify}=OK)\land(\text{replay}=OK)\land(\rho_{\text{exc}} \le 0.01)\land(\Delta H < 0.05)\land(\text{risk}\le\tau)]
with rollback whenever:
[\eta(2p) < \eta(p)]
after burn-in, or whenever the patch falls below the allowed truth/verification corridor. The docs are explicit about the η rollback law and explicit about witness/replay/promotion closure. The final numeric risk cutoff (\tau) is the part I’m recommending rather than extracting.
Final compression
The most faithful optimizer-and-update spec is:
no optimizer on the immutable reference kernel,
freeze the dense core online,
train adapters + heads + route/planner + verifier + mode selector with supervised/self-play objectives,
train the scheduler with GRPO / meta-bandit logic,
update PatternStore and witness registries only by append/merge/prune/promote/quarantine events,
hourly κ-distill, every-500-episode scheduler proposals, 48h quiet-shelf decay, nightly adapter/head updates, and weekly promotion/recenter review.
The next strongest move is the literal training config: learning-rate ranges, adapter ranks, batch sizes, replay buffer sizes, and one YAML-like train.yaml for the whole weekly loop.
Appendix O — Constitutional Evolution, Amendment Protocols, and Civilizational Continuity
This appendix defines the constitutional-evolution layer of the manuscript civilization. Appendix N established that a federated mesh of manuscript brains can remain resource-aware, contribution-traceable, stewardship-driven, and economically sustainable over time. The present appendix now asks the next and deepest civilizational question:
[\text{How does a civilization of manuscript brains change its own law without losing identity, legitimacy, or continuity?}]
Any architecture that can:
patch itself,
migrate old archives into new structure,
create new operator families,
widen its commons,
federate many sovereign brains,
and sustain itself economically
will inevitably confront constitutional change. Its laws will not remain frozen forever. New threat classes will emerge. New operator regimes will need recognition. New treaty patterns will appear. Autonomy tiers will evolve. Commons economics will need recalibration. New embodiment channels or domain bridges will create needs not anticipated in earlier law. The manuscript civilization therefore requires not only policy and economics, but a formal theory of lawful self-amendment.
This appendix provides that theory. It specifies how the civilization:
proposes amendments,
reviews them,
simulates their effects,
branches if needed,
ratifies them,
propagates them across scales,
records dissent and non-adoption,
and preserves deep constitutional identity through change.
The central object is the constitutional evolution system
[
\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{const}}
\Big(\mathcal{L}{\mathrm{canon}},,\mathcal{A}{\mathrm{amend}},,\mathcal{R}{\mathrm{rat}},,\mathcal{F}{\mathrm{fork}},,\mathcal{S}{\mathrm{succ}},,\mathcal{T}{\mathrm{trans}},,\mathcal{M}{\mathrm{memory}},,\psi{\mathrm{const}}\Big),]where:
(\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{canon}}) is the current constitutional law stack,
(\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{amend}}) is the amendment proposal and review family,
(\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{rat}}) is the ratification and adoption layer,
(\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{fork}}) is the lawful fork, schism, and plural-constitution layer,
(\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{succ}}) is the succession and stewardship-transfer family,
(\mathcal{T}_{\mathrm{trans}}) is the constitutional transition and migration layer,
(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{memory}}) is the constitutional memory and precedent archive,
(\psi_{\mathrm{const}}) is the witness and attestation family for constitutional state.
This appendix is governed by eight constitutional laws.
First, constitutional explicitness: every law-bearing rule that governs many artifact classes or many brains must itself be addressable and versioned as a constitutional object.
Second, amendment before drift: normative changes to trust, governance, autonomy, treaty, safety, or commons rules must occur through explicit amendment processes rather than through silent operational drift.
Third, identity-preserving change: constitutional evolution should preserve as much lawful civilizational continuity as possible, and where continuity breaks, the break must be named as fork, schism, or succession.
Fourth, ratification proportionality: more central constitutional surfaces require broader review, higher replay burden, and wider consent for change.
Fifth, minority constitutional retention: when deep disagreement remains, lawful constitutional plurality may be preserved rather than falsely forcing one brittle global law.
Sixth, precedent memory: prior amendments, disputes, ratifications, and failures must remain replayable as constitutional memory.
Seventh, succession clarity: stewardship and law must survive turnover of maintainers, councils, or tenant-specific brains without becoming ownerless or informally redefined.
Eighth, deep-time humility: the constitutional layer must preserve explicit open problems and amendment frontiers rather than claiming final closure.
Under the Square lens this appendix defines constitutional objects, law stacks, amendment packets, ratification classes, succession records, and precedent archives. Under the Flower lens it defines amendment flows, constitutional phase transitions, ratification rhythms, schism and reunion dynamics, and cross-scale treaty propagation. Under the Cloud lens it defines amendment thresholds, legitimacy metrics, constitutional drift alarms, judicial review of proposed changes, and plural constitutional coexistence. Under the Fractal lens it defines recursive constitutions across brains and federations, stewardship succession, constitutional memory compaction, and the theorem by which the manuscript civilization remains itself while changing its own law.
The deepest significance is that this appendix makes the civilization genuinely historical rather than static. It can now become other than it was—lawfully.
O.A1 — Constitutional Objects and the Law Stack
The first requirement of constitutional evolution is that the law itself become a first-class object. Up to this point the framework has accumulated:
invariants,
contracts,
trust lattices,
policy envelopes,
treaty objects,
quota rules,
hardening rules,
autonomy tiers,
review gates.
The present appendix now collects the subset of these that function as constitutional law: rules whose scope is sufficiently broad that they govern many local objects, many committees, many treaty surfaces, or many brains at once.
A constitutional object is:
[
\lambda
\Big(u_\lambda,,a_\lambda,,\operatorname{class}(\lambda),,\operatorname{text}(\lambda),,\operatorname{scope}(\lambda),,\operatorname{dependencies}(\lambda),,\operatorname{priority}(\lambda),,\operatorname{amendability}(\lambda),,\operatorname{lineage}(\lambda),,\psi_\lambda\Big),]where:
(u_\lambda) is the law ID,
(a_\lambda) is the canonical constitutional address,
(\operatorname{class}(\lambda)) identifies the law family,
(\operatorname{text}(\lambda)) is the formal statement or structured representation,
(\operatorname{scope}(\lambda)) specifies what artifacts, brains, lanes, or treaties it governs,
(\operatorname{dependencies}(\lambda)) specify what higher or peer laws it presupposes,
(\operatorname{priority}(\lambda)) specifies override precedence,
(\operatorname{amendability}(\lambda)) specifies what amendment class is required to change it,
(\operatorname{lineage}(\lambda)) specifies amendment ancestry,
(\psi_\lambda) is the witness of adoption and validity.
The canonical constitutional class family is:
[
\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{canon}}
{L_{\mathrm{identity}},L_{\mathrm{legality}},L_{\mathrm{policy}},L_{\mathrm{treaty}},L_{\mathrm{commons}},L_{\mathrm{autonomy}},L_{\mathrm{hardening}},L_{\mathrm{succession}},L_{\mathrm{amendment}}}.]
These mean:
(L_{\mathrm{identity}})
Rules governing continuity, replay, canonical address, fork naming, and lineage.
(L_{\mathrm{legality}})
Rules governing what may count as exact, approximate, deferred, or blocked across core artifact classes.
(L_{\mathrm{policy}})
Rules governing trust, consent, exposure, sandboxing, and revocation.
(L_{\mathrm{treaty}})
Rules governing federation, exchange, common artifact classes, and non-fusion boundaries.
(L_{\mathrm{commons}})
Rules governing quotas, stewardship, contribution credits, and sustainability of shared resources.
(L_{\mathrm{autonomy}})
Rules governing what self-directed action tiers are permitted and under what hardening thresholds.
(L_{\mathrm{hardening}})
Rules governing threat handling, quarantine, spoof skepticism, anti-capture, and security drift.
(L_{\mathrm{succession}})
Rules governing steward transfer, role handoff, archive continuity, and long-horizon maintenance.
(L_{\mathrm{amendment}})
Meta-rules governing how constitutional changes themselves occur.
These laws are assembled into a law stack:
[
\mathcal{L}^{\star}
(\lambda_1,\dots,\lambda_n)]with explicit precedence, such that conflicts among laws are resolved by:
class priority,
scope specificity,
amendment recency,
fallback to committee or constitutional review where necessary.
Thus the constitutional layer is not merely text. It is a typed and ordered stack.
A minimal schema may be:
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from typing import Dict, Any, List
@dataclass
class ConstitutionalObject:
law_id: str
address: str
law_class: str
text: Dict[str, Any]
scope: Dict[str, Any]
dependencies: List[str]
priority: Dict[str, Any]
amendability: Dict[str, Any]
lineage: Dict[str, Any]
witness: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
Definition O.1 — Constitution-Bearing Law
A law is constitution-bearing if it governs many downstream artifacts, services, committees, treaty surfaces, or tenant brains and therefore cannot be treated as merely local configuration.
Theorem O.1 — Constitutional Objecthood Is Necessary for Lawful Civilizational Change
If broad governing rules remain implicit in code, norms, or committee habit rather than explicit constitutional objects, then later change cannot be replayed or ratified lawfully. Therefore constitutional objecthood is necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore begins its constitutional life by objectifying its own law.
O.A2 — Amendment Packets and Proposal Classes
The next requirement is a lawful representation of constitutional change. The framework therefore defines amendment packets.
An amendment packet is:
[
\Delta^\lambda
\Big(u_{\Delta^\lambda},,\operatorname{target}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{class}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{motivation}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{proposal}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{impact}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{review_path}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{ratification_rule}(\Delta^\lambda),,\operatorname{rollback}(\Delta^\lambda),,\psi_{\Delta^\lambda}\Big).]
The amendment class family is:
[
\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{amend}}
{A_{\mathrm{clarify}},A_{\mathrm{tighten}},A_{\mathrm{broaden}},A_{\mathrm{repair}},A_{\mathrm{delegate}},A_{\mathrm{federate}},A_{\mathrm{fork}},A_{\mathrm{meta}}}.]
These mean:
(A_{\mathrm{clarify}})
Clarifies wording, scope, or relation among laws without changing substantive action rights.
(A_{\mathrm{tighten}})
Restricts or increases safeguards around a constitutional surface.
(A_{\mathrm{broaden}})
Expands a lawful capability, scope, or exchange class.This requires stronger review because broadening law increases power.
(A_{\mathrm{repair}})
Repairs contradictions, loopholes, or outdated constitutional assumptions.
(A_{\mathrm{delegate}})
Moves some constitutional decision burden to lower or more local structures under bounded charter.
(A_{\mathrm{federate}})
Introduces or revises cross-brain treaty or commons relations.
(A_{\mathrm{fork}})
Proposes lawful constitutional divergence rather than one universal amendment.
(A_{\mathrm{meta}})
Amends the amendment process itself. This is the highest-risk amendment class and requires the strongest ratification.
The impact field matters greatly. A proposed wording clarification that accidentally broadens live patch power is not truly a clarification. Thus every amendment packet must estimate:
artifact classes affected,
tenant scopes affected,
treaty surfaces affected,
autonomy tier implications,
policy drift risk,
replay and lineage implications.
A minimal amendment schema:
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, Any, List
@dataclass
class AmendmentPacket:
amendment_id: str
target_law_ids: List[str]
amendment_class: str
motivation: Dict[str, Any]
proposal: Dict[str, Any]
impact: Dict[str, Any]
review_path: Dict[str, Any]
ratification_rule: Dict[str, Any]
rollback: Dict[str, Any]
witness: Dict[str, Any]
Definition O.2 — Amendment-Lawful Proposal
An amendment proposal is lawful if it explicitly identifies the law objects it affects, its class, scope of impact, review path, ratification rule, and rollback or branch strategy.
Theorem O.2 — Constitutional Change Requires First-Class Amendment Objects
Without explicit amendment packets, constitutional change would happen only through drift, informal override, or repository mutation, none of which satisfy replayable governance. Therefore amendment packets are necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore changes law through a visible legal object, not by quiet drift.
O.A3 — Ratification Classes and Threshold Families
Not all constitutional changes are equal. The framework therefore defines ratification classes and their threshold families.
A ratification rule is:
[
\rho
\Big(u_\rho,,\operatorname{scope}(\rho),,\operatorname{required_review}(\rho),,\operatorname{required_councils}(\rho),,\operatorname{required_quorum}(\rho),,\operatorname{required_majority}(\rho),,\operatorname{minority_rights}(\rho),,\operatorname{expiry}(\rho),,\psi_\rho\Big).]
The canonical ratification classes are:
[
\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{rat}}
{R_0^{\mathrm{local}},R_1^{\mathrm{core}},R_2^{\mathrm{federal}},R_3^{\mathrm{constitutional}},R_4^{\mathrm{meta}}}.]
(R_0^{\mathrm{local}})
For bounded law changes affecting one tenant, one sandbox, one committee charter, or one artifact family.
(R_1^{\mathrm{core}})
For changes affecting a brain’s core identity, legality, trust, or runtime surfaces.
(R_2^{\mathrm{federal}})
For changes affecting treaties, shared commons, or cross-brain trust and exchange.
(R_3^{\mathrm{constitutional}})
For changes affecting broad constitutional law across many organ families.
(R_4^{\mathrm{meta}})
For changes affecting amendment procedures, ratification itself, sovereignty definitions, or autonomy thresholds at civilizational scale.
The general principle is:[R_{k+1}\Rightarrow\text{strictly stronger burden than } R_k.]This stronger burden may include:
wider review roles,
more diverse councils,
longer replay quiet periods,
stronger minority protection,
longer ratification delay before activation,
stronger rollback and branch readiness.
Definition O.3 — Ratification-Proportionate Amendment
An amendment is ratification-proportionate if the breadth and impact of the change are matched by a review and ratification class strong enough to protect affected scopes.
Theorem O.3 — Constitutional Changes Need Graduated Thresholds
If every amendment used the same ratification threshold, then trivial clarifications would be too hard and civilization-wide autonomy changes too easy. Therefore ratification classes are necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore scales its constitutional difficulty with its constitutional danger.
O.A4 — Constitutional Memory, Precedent, and Judicial Trace
The final Square task is to preserve constitutional history. Every amendment, review, ratification, dissent, fork, repeal, and exceptional override must enter constitutional memory.
A precedent object is:
[
P
\Big(
u_P,,
\operatorname{case}(P),,
\operatorname{laws}(P),,
\operatorname{amendments}(P),,
\operatorname{councils}(P),,
\operatorname{dissent}(P),,
\operatorname{resolution}(P),,
\operatorname{implications}(P),,
\psi_P
\Big).
]
The constitutional memory archive is:
[
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{memory}}
{P_1,\dots,P_n}]plus:
amendment histories,
rejected proposals,
ratification failures,
schism decisions,
reunion decisions,
stewardship transfers,
constitutional emergency actions.
This gives the civilization something analogous to jurisprudence: past constitutional events that later change interpretation or review burden.
The constitutional memory also feeds:
amendment review,
treaty updates,
anti-drift sentinels,
succession transfer,
educational explanation of why current law is the way it is.
Definition O.4 — Replayable Constitutional Precedent
A constitutional precedent is replayable if the arguments, council structure, legal classes, dissents, and resulting law updates can be reconstructed from stored constitutional memory.
Theorem O.4 — Constitutional Continuity Requires Precedent Memory
A civilization that amends law without replayable precedent memory will slowly lose the reasons its law took its current form and become vulnerable to repeating old conflicts. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore remembers its constitutional struggles as part of its identity.
O.B1 — Amendment Review Flows and Constitutional Phase Transitions
The Flower constitutional layer begins with the fact that amendment is a process, not one act. The framework therefore defines amendment review flows.
A full amendment flow is:[\mathrm{propose}\to\mathrm{classify}\to\mathrm{review}\to\mathrm{simulate}\to\mathrm{ratify}\to\mathrm{phase_in}\to\mathrm{monitor}.]
These stages are:
Propose
Create amendment packet with motive and target law set.
Classify
Determine amendment class and ratification tier.
Review
Form relevant committees and councils, collect objections, and surface affected artifacts or treaties.
Simulate
Run sandboxed or counterfactual replay to estimate:
policy shifts,
patch effects,
treaty consequences,
embodiment consequences,
autonomy consequences.
Ratify
Apply ratification rule and record dissent.
Phase-in
Move from prior law to new law with safe migration steps rather than instant silent replacement.
Monitor
Watch for constitutional drift, harm, or evidence that the amendment misclassified its impact.
A constitutional phase transition is:[\lambda_t\to\lambda_{t+1}]under explicit transition witness. This means the law stack itself has temporal phases just like curricula and runtime modes.
Definition O.5 — Phase-Coherent Constitutional Transition
A constitutional transition is phase-coherent if the law changes only through the full amendment flow or an explicitly encoded emergency variant of that flow.
Theorem O.5 — Constitutional Change Requires Time Structure
If law is changed instantaneously without proposal, review, simulation, ratification, and monitoring, then the civilization cannot distinguish lawful amendment from silent operational capture. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore changes its law rhythmically, not impulsively.
O.B2 — Simulation, Counterfactual Constitutions, and Pre-Ratification Testing
Before a major constitutional change becomes live, it should often be simulated. This is the constitutional analogue of sandbox patching.
A constitutional simulation object is:
[
\Sigma^\lambda
\Big(u_{\Sigma^\lambda},,\operatorname{base_law}(\Sigma^\lambda),,\operatorname{candidate_law}(\Sigma^\lambda),,\operatorname{scope}(\Sigma^\lambda),,\operatorname{test_worlds}(\Sigma^\lambda),,\operatorname{predicted_effects}(\Sigma^\lambda),,\psi_{\Sigma^\lambda}\Big).]Test worlds may include:
microcosm,
mesocosm,
benchmark corpus slices,
sandbox tenant brains,
federated exchange simulations,
embodied curriculum traces.
Counterfactual constitutions ask:
what would happen if trust thresholds were tightened?
what would happen if bridge promotion required more replay?
what if autonomy tier (A_4) demanded stronger hardening metrics?
what if a treaty allowed a new artifact class into commons?
These simulations generate a constitutional impact field:
[
\mathcal{I}_{\mathrm{const}}(\Delta^\lambda)
\big(i_{\mathrm{identity}},i_{\mathrm{runtime}},i_{\mathrm{federation}},i_{\mathrm{embodied}},i_{\mathrm{commons}},i_{\mathrm{hardening}}\big).]
Definition O.6 — Simulation-Tested Amendment
An amendment is simulation-tested if its candidate law was executed against representative test worlds before ratification and the resulting impact field is part of its review basis.
Theorem O.6 — High-Impact Constitutional Changes Need Counterfactual Testing
Because constitutional law affects many organ families at once, sandbox simulation is necessary to detect broad side effects before ratification. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore rehearses law before living under it.
O.B3 — Schisms, Fork Constitutions, and Lawful Plurality
The federation will not always converge on one constitutional answer. Some disagreements are deep enough that forcing one law everywhere would either flatten sovereignty or cause false consensus. The framework therefore defines constitutional forks and lawful schisms.
A fork constitution object is:
[
F^\lambda
\Big(u_F,,\operatorname{parent_law}(F),,\operatorname{fork_variants}(F),,\operatorname{shared_core}(F),,\operatorname{divergence_scope}(F),,\operatorname{interoperability}(F),,\psi_F\Big).]This means that:
some laws remain shared,
some diverge,
interoperability conditions remain explicit,
lineages remain replayably related.
A lawful schism is not a civilizational failure. It is the explicit acknowledgment that two or more constitutional lineages must diverge while still possibly exchanging some commons or treaty classes.
Examples:
one mesh may allow a broader pedagogy adaptation envelope than another,
one federation may keep stricter promotion friction on cross-domain bridges,
one tenant class may remain at lower autonomy tiers indefinitely.
Definition O.7 — Lawful Constitutional Fork
A constitutional fork is lawful if the shared core remains explicit, divergence scope is bounded, and post-fork treaty and interoperability rules are clearly stated.
Theorem O.7 — Constitutional Plurality Can Preserve Unity Better than Forced Uniformity
If deep disagreements are forced into one brittle law stack, hidden noncompliance or capture is likely. Lawful forks preserve truthfulness and reduce covert divergence. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore allows different futures without losing shared ancestry.
O.B4 — Reunion, Treaty Repair, and Constitutional Reconciliation
Forks need not be permanent. The system therefore defines reunion and constitutional reconciliation.
A reconciliation object is:
[
R^\lambda
\Big(u_R,,\operatorname{forks}(R),,\operatorname{shared_core}(R),,\operatorname{reconciled_regions}(R),,\operatorname{unresolved_regions}(R),,\operatorname{new_law}(R),,\psi_R\Big).]Reconciliation is lawful when:
sufficient shared core remains,
each fork’s lineage is preserved,
unresolved regions remain explicit,
no side is silently absorbed,
treaty repair and commons adjustments accompany the new law.
This is constitutional repair at federation scale.
Definition O.8 — Lineage-Preserving Reunion
A reunion is lineage-preserving if the merged or reconciled law stack retains explicit ancestry from all parent forks and does not erase prior dissents or divergence causes.
Theorem O.8 — Reconciliation Requires More than Merge
A constitutional reunion is not simply one fork accepting the other’s law. It requires explicit shared-core identification, reconciliation object, and post-reunion treaty repair. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore knows how to heal its own lawful splits.
O.C1 — Legitimacy Metrics and Constitutional Confidence
The Cloud constitutional layer begins with legitimacy. A law may exist, but how legitimate is it now? The system therefore defines legitimacy metrics.
For constitutional object (\lambda), define:
[
L(\lambda)
\big(\ell_{\mathrm{rat}},\ell_{\mathrm{replay}},\ell_{\mathrm{adoption}},\ell_{\mathrm{dissent}},\ell_{\mathrm{drift}},\ell_{\mathrm{stew}},\ell_{\mathrm{federated}}\big),]where:
(\ell_{\mathrm{rat}}) measures strength of ratification,
(\ell_{\mathrm{replay}}) measures clarity and reproducibility of the law’s history,
(\ell_{\mathrm{adoption}}) measures practical uptake,
(\ell_{\mathrm{dissent}}) measures unresolved minority intensity,
(\ell_{\mathrm{drift}}) measures how far real operation has drifted from the law,
(\ell_{\mathrm{stew}}) measures stewardship and maintenance health,
(\ell_{\mathrm{federated}}) measures treaty and interoperability stability where relevant.
Legitimacy is not identical to popularity or age. A very old law may become weakly legitimate if operational drift is high or if it has not been replayed or re-attested for a long time.
Definition O.9 — Legitimate Constitutional Object
A constitutional object is legitimate if its ratification, replay lineage, adoption, stewardship, and drift state remain above the thresholds appropriate to its law class.
Theorem O.9 — Constitutional Legitimacy Is Dynamic
Since law can drift away from actual operation or lose support under new conditions, legitimacy cannot be a one-time property. It must be measured continuously. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore evaluates not only what law says, but whether that law still stands on living ground.
O.C2 — Constitutional Drift Detection and Judicial Review
The next constitutional problem is drift: when actual operation or treaty behavior no longer matches the law stack.
The constitutional drift metric is:
[
D_{\mathrm{const}}(t)
\alpha_1 D_{\mathrm{policy}}+\alpha_2 D_{\mathrm{treaty}}+\alpha_3 D_{\mathrm{promotion}}+\alpha_4 D_{\mathrm{autonomy}}+\alpha_5 D_{\mathrm{embodied}}]measuring:
mismatch between law and actual permission behavior,
mismatch between treaty objects and real exchanges,
mismatch between ratified promotion rules and real promotions,
mismatch between autonomy law and actual self-directed action,
mismatch between embodiment law and real adaptation or exposure.
When (D_{\mathrm{const}}) exceeds threshold, a judicial review process is triggered:
[
J^\lambda
\Big(u_J,,\operatorname{law_set}(J),,\operatorname{observed_drift}(J),,\operatorname{affected_scopes}(J),,\operatorname{possible_repairs}(J),,\psi_J\Big).]Judicial review may conclude:
law must be reasserted,
operation must be corrected,
amendment is necessary,
fork is necessary,
the observed drift is lawful due to prior but unrecorded exception.
Definition O.10 — Judicially Reviewable Drift
Drift is judicially reviewable if it can be expressed as a discrepancy between ratified law objects and observed policy, treaty, or runtime behavior over a scope.
Theorem O.10 — Constitutional Drift Needs Formal Review
Without judicial review of drift, the constitutional layer degenerates into symbolic memory while real authority migrates elsewhere. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore has not only lawmaking but lawful interpretation and correction.
O.C3 — Constitutional Minority Protections and Veto Structures
A healthy constitutional layer must protect minorities in a deeper sense than ordinary committee dissent. Certain classes of law change can so strongly affect identity, safety, or sovereignty that minority protections must be explicit.
The minority protection object is:
[
m^\lambda
\Big(u_m,,\operatorname{protected_scope}(m),,\operatorname{minority_classes}(m),,\operatorname{veto_rights}(m),,\operatorname{branch_rights}(m),,\operatorname{review_trigger}(m),,\psi_m\Big).]Protected scopes may include:
tenant sovereignty,
raw archive preservation,
high-risk embodied boundaries,
non-fusion rules,
autonomy-tier changes,
hardening softening.
This means, for example:
a minority coalition of hardening and identity reviewers may have veto power over dangerous autonomy broadening,
a tenant may retain branch rights against federation-level curricular unification,
raw archive preservation may have a constitutional guard against aggressive compaction.
Definition O.11 — Constitutionally Protected Minority Position
A minority position is constitutionally protected if it has explicit veto, review, or branch rights over a bounded scope of constitutional change.
Theorem O.11 — Deep Constitutional Changes Need Minority Protections
Without protected minority rights, majoritarian ratification may still lawfully erase crucial identity, safety, or sovereignty boundaries. Therefore some scopes require stronger constitutional protection. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore treats some disagreements as deserving structural protection, not only persuasive effort.
O.C4 — Open Constitutional Frontiers and Amendment Horizons
The final Cloud task is to preserve constitutional humility. Some constitutional questions remain open:
future autonomy tier law,
new embodiment domains,
unknown federated trust patterns,
new commons value classes,
deeper inter-brain constitutional scaling.
The framework therefore maintains an explicit constitutional frontier field:
[
