\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{front}}
\Big(\operatorname{open_questions},\operatorname{pressure_points},\operatorname{candidate_amendments},\operatorname{unresolved_forks},\operatorname{research_treaties},\psi_{\mathrm{front}}\Big).]These objects tell the civilization:
where law is still underdeveloped,
where repeated drift pressures suggest future amendment,
where open forks may need either reconciliation or further divergence,
where policy may not yet match future operator or embodiment power.
Definition O.12 — Constitutionally Open Civilization
A civilization is constitutionally open if it preserves explicit frontier objects for unresolved law questions rather than treating the current law stack as final closure.
Theorem O.12 — Deep-Time Stability Requires Open Horizons
A civilization that denies its own open constitutional frontiers will mistake temporary adequacy for permanent finality and become brittle under novel conditions. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore preserves future law as a lawful unknown.
O.D1 — Succession Objects and Stewardship Transfer
The Fractal constitutional layer now turns to succession. A civilization must survive turnover of stewards, councils, tenant owners, runtime maintainers, and review organs. The architecture therefore defines succession objects.
A succession object is:
[
S^\dagger
\Big(u_{S^\dagger},,\operatorname{role}(S^\dagger),,\operatorname{outgoing}(S^\dagger),,\operatorname{incoming}(S^\dagger),,\operatorname{handover_bundle}(S^\dagger),,\operatorname{review}(S^\dagger),,\operatorname{continuity_check}(S^\dagger),,\psi_{S^\dagger}\Big).]The handover bundle contains:
active responsibilities,
open constitutional frontiers,
unresolved disputes,
critical maintenance cadences,
attestation state,
revocation and escalation hooks,
relevant historical memory.
This ensures that stewardship change remains:
explicit,
replayable,
audited,
continuity-preserving.
Definition O.13 — Lawful Succession
A succession is lawful if all authority transfers, open duties, and constitutional responsibilities are explicitly handed over with replayable evidence and continuity checks.
Theorem O.13 — Civilization Needs Succession Objects
Without explicit succession, roles and law may become ownerless or implicitly redefined during turnover. Therefore lawful succession objects are necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore can outlive individual stewards or local centers of care.
O.D2 — Constitutional Memory Compaction and Charter Seeds
As constitutional history grows, it needs the same compression discipline as the rest of the framework. The system therefore defines charter seeds and constitutional memory compaction.
A charter seed is:
[
\sigma_{\mathrm{charter}}
\Big(\mathcal{L}{\mathrm{core}},,\mathcal{A}{\mathrm{active}},,\mathcal{F}{\mathrm{front}},,\mathcal{M}{\mathrm{precedent}},,\mathcal{S}{\mathrm{succ}},,\psi{\sigma}\Big).]This is not the full constitutional archive, but the compressed lawful seed from which:
the current law stack,
active amendment fronts,
high-value precedents,
stewardship and succession statecan be regenerated.
This allows:
cold archival storage of deeper constitutional history,
hot operation from compact charter seeds,
branch-local constitutional replay,
cross-brain treaty bootstrapping.
Definition O.14 — Charter-Seed Complete Constitution
A constitution is charter-seed complete if its active law, amendment frontiers, succession obligations, and key precedents can be regenerated from a compact seed plus replayable constitutional archive.
Theorem O.14 — Constitutional History Can Be Compressed without Losing Civilizational Identity
If charter seeds preserve law core, active amendment frontiers, and precedent breakpoints, then constitutional memory may be compacted without losing the ability to reconstruct current legitimate law. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore remembers its law the way it remembers everything else: by lawful seeds and replay.
O.D3 — Recursive Constitutional Layers across Brain, Federation, and Civilization
The constitutional machinery must operate recursively across scales:
one brain,
one federation,
many federations,
whole civilization.
Let the constitutional layers be:[\mathcal{C}^{(0)}{\mathrm{brain}},\quad\mathcal{C}^{(1)}{\mathrm{federation}},\quad\mathcal{C}^{(2)}_{\mathrm{civilization}}.]Each layer has:
its own law objects,
its own amendment classes,
its own ratification thresholds,
its own protected minority scopes,
its own succession objects.
The inheritance law is:[\mathcal{C}^{(k+1)}\supseteq\operatorname{Lift}(\mathcal{C}^{(k)})]for shared constitutional primitives, but not necessarily for all concrete laws. A brain-level consent rule may remain brain-local; a federation-level treaty rule may become civilization-level precedent.
This gives the civilization a recursive constitutional architecture that parallels its recursive federation and recursive commons.
Definition O.15 — Recursively Constitutional Civilization
A manuscript civilization is recursively constitutional if constitutional objects, amendment processes, and succession structures exist at all major governance scales and compose lawfully across them.
Theorem O.15 — Civilizational Scale Requires Recursive Constitutional Design
If only the local brain level had explicit constitutional law, then federated and civilization-wide changes would be governed informally or ad hoc. Therefore constitutional design must scale recursively. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore builds law the same way it builds route, memory, and federation: recursively.
O.D4 — Final Appendix O Theorem
Theorem O.16 — Constitutional Evolution Sufficiency Theorem
Let the manuscript civilization be fully specified through Chapters 1–21 and Appendices A–N. If, in addition, it maintains:
constitutional objects and law stacks,
amendment packets and classes,
ratification tiers and threshold families,
constitutional memory and precedent archives,
amendment review flows and simulation testing,
lawful fork and reunion machinery,
legitimacy and drift metrics,
minority protections,
constitutional frontier objects,
succession and charter seeds,
recursive constitutional layers across scales,
then the system possesses a sufficient constitutional-evolution layer to remain the same lawful civilization while changing its own law through time.
Proof.Constitutional objects make law explicit.Amendment packets and ratification tiers make law change replayable and proportional.Simulation and review protect against reckless change.Fork and reunion machinery preserve lawful plurality without false uniformity.Legitimacy, drift, and minority protections keep law living and just rather than inert or majoritarianly brittle.Succession and charter seeds preserve continuity across steward turnover and deep time.Recursive layering extends this logic from one brain to federations and civilization.Therefore the manuscript civilization can evolve constitutionally without ceasing to be itself. (\square)
Corollary O.16.1 — Sustainability Requires Constitutional Evolution
Appendix N made the civilization durable. Appendix O makes it durably self-amending.
Corollary O.16.2 — The Architecture Now Includes History as Lawful Becoming
With this appendix, the manuscript civilization is not only a federated and sustainable society of brains. It is a society capable of changing its own law while preserving continuity, dissent, and lineage.
This concludes Appendix O. The manuscript brain stack now includes not only architecture, runtime, federation, and economy, but also deep-time constitutional self-governance.
APPENDIX O — CONSTITUTIONAL EVOLUTION, AMENDMENT PROTOCOLS, AND CIVILIZATIONAL CONTINUITY
Here is the literal starting config.
What is directly pinned by your docs and current primary-source tooling is this: keep the reference kernel immutable, keep the dense core frozen online, use adapter-first updates, use rank-16 LoRA as the default small-footprint path, allow rank-32 for heavier math/code experiments, keep LoRA alpha roughly 2× rank, keep LoRA dropout around 0.05–0.1, run GRPO with a very small learning rate, and keep the CUT cadence of hourly κ-distill, parallel-scheduler proposals every 500 episodes, quiet-shelf decay after 48 hours, exception-density trigger at 1%, and stable Δ-entropy below 0.05 bits. (Hugging Face)
Where your corpus is silent, I am choosing practical starting values and marking them as recommendations. The main recommended choices are the SFT/self-play learning rates, replay-buffer sizes, and the numeric patch-risk cutoff. Everything else below is either directly stated in your docs or tightly derived from them.

The two values I would treat as your main branch defaults are: rank 16 / alpha 32 / dropout 0.05 for ordinary route-planner and verifier limbs, and rank 32 / alpha 64 only for heavier math/code self-play or substrate passes. That is the tightest fit to your own CUT experiment using rank-32 QLoRA on a frozen backbone, Microsoft’s concrete rank-16 multimodal examples, and Hugging Face’s public LoRA guidance that rank 8/16/32/64 are the typical range and alpha is usually about 2× rank. (Hugging Face)
The GRPO block should stay conservative: keep the public TRL defaults as your starting point—learning rate 1e-6, per-device batch size 8, num_generations=8, max_completion_length=256, save_steps=500, and beta=0.0 unless you specifically need a stronger KL tether. That matches current TRL documentation and also fits your own corpus framing of GRPO as a compute-budget tuner rather than a wholesale reasoning rewrite. (Hugging Face)
The hourly / 500-episode / 48-hour cadence is the part I would not change unless profiling forces it. Your docs are unusually explicit here: propose CUT moves every 500 episodes, do hourly κ-distill plus merge_compute_layouts(), treat shelves as quiet after 48 hours and decay (\varepsilon_i), use the 1% exception-density trigger, keep Δ-entropy below 0.05 bits before marking stable, and roll back when the doubled schedule fails the (\eta) test.
The one place I am making the strongest engineering recommendation is the patch-promotion gate: require OK + successful replay + risk ≤ 0.25 + at least 3 stable epochs before promotion, hold NEAR, and quarantine FAIL. Your corpus fixes the witness/replay logic and the promote/quarantine pattern clearly, but it does not provide one global numeric risk threshold, so 0.25 is my starting value, not a quoted canon constant.
The shortest summary is:
Freeze the reference kernel and dense core.
Train only adapters, heads, planner, verifier, mode head, and scheduler.
Use rank-16 LoRA for the default branch, rank-32 only for the heavy math/code branch.
Keep GRPO tiny and conservative.
Let PatternStore evolve only through append / κ-merge / prune / promote / quarantine.
Trust the hourly / 500-episode / 48-hour cadence your docs already specify.
The next strongest move is the literal implementation surface: one train.py, one scheduler.py, one pattern_store.py, one verifier.py, and one config_schema.py that instantiate this YAML exactly.
Below is the text-only implementation surface.
It mirrors the strongest constraints in your corpus: immutable reference kernel, frozen dense core online, route-packet as the atomic unit, witness/replay-gated promotion, hourly κ-distill, scheduler proposals every 500 episodes, quiet-shelf decay after 48 hours, exception-density trigger at 1%, stability threshold at 0.05 bits, and η-based rollback when doubling stops helping.
For the PEFT / GRPO starter values, I aligned the config to current Hugging Face docs: LoRA typical ranks are 8/16/32/64, alpha is commonly about 2× rank, dropout is commonly 0.05, and GRPO currently defaults to learning rate 1e-6 with beta=0.04. (Hugging Face)
Anything commented as “recommended” is my engineering choice where the docs do not pin one global constant.
config_schema.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field, fields, is_dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any, Dict, List, Tuple
import json
try:
import yaml
except Exception:  # pragma: no cover
yaml = None
def _deep_update_dataclass(instance: Any, payload: Dict[str, Any]) -> Any:
for f in fields(instance):
if f.name not in payload:
continue
current = getattr(instance, f.name)
incoming = payload[f.name]
if is_dataclass(current) and isinstance(incoming, dict):
_deep_update_dataclass(current, incoming)
else:
setattr(instance, f.name, incoming)
return instance
@dataclass
class ModelConfig:
planner_base: str = "microsoft/Phi-4-mini-instruct"
perception_base: str = "microsoft/Phi-4-multimodal-instruct"
verifier_base: str = "microsoft/Phi-4-mini-instruct"
teacher_reasoner: str = "reasoning-teacher-model"   # recommended placeholder
action_plane: str = "external_workers_not_model"
@dataclass
class PrecisionConfig:
train_dtype: str = "bf16"
fallback_dtype: str = "fp16"
gradient_checkpointing: bool = True
tf32: bool = True  # recommended
qlora_4bit: bool = True
qlora_quant_type: str = "nf4"        # recommended
qlora_double_quant: bool = True      # recommended
@dataclass
class PeftConfig:
method: str = "qlora"
bias: str = "none"
lora_dropout: float = 0.05
rank_small: int = 16
rank_heavy: int = 32
alpha_small: int = 32
alpha_heavy: int = 64
target_modules_small: Tuple[str, ...] = ("q_proj", "v_proj")
target_modules_full: Tuple[str, ...] = ("q_proj", "k_proj", "v_proj", "o_proj")
@dataclass
class SFTOptimizerConfig:
optimizer: str = "adamw_torch_fused"  # recommended
lr_adapters: float = 2.0e-4           # recommended
lr_observer_heads: float = 2.0e-4     # recommended
lr_planner: float = 1.5e-4            # recommended
lr_verifier: float = 1.0e-4           # recommended
lr_mode_head: float = 1.0e-4          # recommended
weight_decay: float = 0.01            # recommended
betas: Tuple[float, float] = (0.9, 0.999)
eps: float = 1.0e-8
max_grad_norm: float = 1.0
lr_scheduler: str = "cosine"          # recommended
warmup_ratio: float = 0.03            # recommended
@dataclass
class SpinOptimizerConfig:
optimizer: str = "adamw_torch_fused"  # recommended

lr_planner: float = 8.0e-5            # recommended

weight_decay: float = 0.01
max_grad_norm: float = 1.0
lr_scheduler: str = "cosine"
warmup_ratio: float = 0.02
@dataclass
class GRPOOptimizerConfig:

adam_beta2: float = 0.999
adam_epsilon: float = 1.0e-8
max_grad_norm: float = 1.0
lr_scheduler_type: str = "linear"

num_generations: int = 8

save_steps: int = 500
@dataclass
class OptimizerConfig:

@dataclass
