def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
return json.loads(json.dumps(self, default=lambda x: x.__dict__))
@classmethod
def from_dict(cls, payload: Dict[str, Any]) -> "TrainConfig":
cfg = cls()
return _deep_update_dataclass(cfg, payload)
@classmethod
def from_yaml(cls, path: str | Path) -> "TrainConfig":
path = Path(path)
if yaml is None:
raise RuntimeError("PyYAML is required to load YAML config files.")
data = yaml.safe_load(path.read_text()) or {}
return cls.from_dict(data)
def dump_yaml(self, path: str | Path) -> None:
path = Path(path)
if yaml is None:
raise RuntimeError("PyYAML is required to write YAML config files.")
path.write_text(yaml.safe_dump(self.to_dict(), sort_keys=False))
def load_train_config(path: str | Path) -> TrainConfig:
path = Path(path)
if path.suffix.lower() in {".yaml", ".yml"}:
return TrainConfig.from_yaml(path)
return TrainConfig.from_dict(json.loads(path.read_text()))
pattern_store.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from time import time
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
from config_schema import TrainConfig
@dataclass
class PatternPetal:
petal_id: str
depth: int
pq_block_ref: str
topology_hash: str
seed_hash: str
bridge_refs: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
stable_epochs: int = 0
last_active_ts: float = field(default_factory=time)
@dataclass
class ExceptionDelta:
petal_id: str
morton_id: int
epoch: int
delta_ref: str
certificate_ref: str
entropy_bits: float
created_ts: float = field(default_factory=time)
@dataclass
class EtaRecord:
episodes_seen: int
worker_count: int
eta_value: float
vram_util: float
created_ts: float = field(default_factory=time)
@dataclass
class DistillReport:
distill_triggered: bool
merged_petals: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
pruned_deltas: int = 0
promoted_petals: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
held_petals: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
class PatternStore:
"""
Event-updated storage surface.
No gradients touch this object.
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.petals: Dict[str, PatternPetal] = {}
self.exceptions: Dict[str, List[ExceptionDelta]] = {}
self.eta_history: List[EtaRecord] = []
def register_petal(self, petal: PatternPetal) -> None:
self.petals[petal.petal_id] = petal
self.exceptions.setdefault(petal.petal_id, [])
def append_exception(
self,
petal_id: str,
morton_id: int,
epoch: int,
delta_ref: str,
certificate_ref: str,
entropy_bits: float,
) -> None:
if petal_id not in self.petals:
raise KeyError(f"Unknown petal: {petal_id}")
self.exceptions[petal_id].append(
ExceptionDelta(
petal_id=petal_id,
morton_id=morton_id,
epoch=epoch,
delta_ref=delta_ref,
certificate_ref=certificate_ref,
entropy_bits=entropy_bits,
)
)
self.petals[petal_id].last_active_ts = time()
def exception_density(self, petal_id: str) -> float:
rows = self.exceptions.get(petal_id, [])
if not rows:
return 0.0
# Recommended proxy: relative density against a nominal 1k-cell shelf.
return min(1.0, len(rows) / 1000.0)
def mean_entropy_bits(self, petal_id: str) -> float:
rows = self.exceptions.get(petal_id, [])
if not rows:
return 0.0
return sum(r.entropy_bits for r in rows) / len(rows)
def should_kappa_distill(self, petal_id: str) -> bool:
return self.exception_density(petal_id) > self.cfg.pattern_store.exception_density_trigger
def hourly_kappa_distill(self) -> DistillReport:
report = DistillReport(distill_triggered=False)
for petal_id in list(self.petals.keys()):
if not self.should_kappa_distill(petal_id):
continue
report.distill_triggered = True
rows = self.exceptions[petal_id]
rows.sort(key=lambda r: (r.entropy_bits, -r.epoch))
# Keep the top half with the lowest entropy, prune the rest.
keep = rows[: max(1, len(rows) // 2)]
pruned = len(rows) - len(keep)
self.exceptions[petal_id] = keep
report.pruned_deltas += pruned
report.merged_petals.append(petal_id)
mean_entropy = self.mean_entropy_bits(petal_id)
if mean_entropy < self.cfg.pattern_store.stable_delta_entropy_bits:
self.petals[petal_id].stable_epochs += 1
else:
self.petals[petal_id].stable_epochs = 0
if self.petals[petal_id].stable_epochs >= self.cfg.pattern_store.promote_stable_delta_after_epochs:
report.promoted_petals.append(petal_id)
else:
report.held_petals.append(petal_id)
return report
def quiet_shelf_decay(self, now_ts: Optional[float] = None) -> List[str]:
now_ts = now_ts or time()
decayed: List[str] = []
quiet_after = self.cfg.pattern_store.quiet_shelf_seconds
for petal_id, petal in self.petals.items():
if now_ts - petal.last_active_ts < quiet_after:
continue
# In a full system, this would tighten epsilon_i and re-PQ the shelf.
petal.last_active_ts = now_ts
decayed.append(petal_id)
return decayed
def record_eta(self, episodes_seen: int, worker_count: int, eta_value: float, vram_util: float) -> None:
self.eta_history.append(
EtaRecord(
episodes_seen=episodes_seen,
worker_count=worker_count,
eta_value=eta_value,
vram_util=vram_util,
)
)
def recent_eta_pair(self) -> Optional[Tuple[EtaRecord, EtaRecord]]:
if len(self.eta_history) < 2:
return None
return self.eta_history[-2], self.eta_history[-1]
def should_rollback(self) -> bool:
pair = self.recent_eta_pair()
if pair is None:
return False
prev_eta, new_eta = pair
if new_eta.worker_count <= prev_eta.worker_count:
return False
return new_eta.eta_value < prev_eta.eta_value
def should_batch_double(self) -> bool:
pair = self.recent_eta_pair()
if pair is None:
return False
prev_eta, new_eta = pair
if new_eta.vram_util > self.cfg.scheduler.max_vram_util_for_batch_doubling:
return False
gain = new_eta.eta_value / max(prev_eta.eta_value, 1e-9)
return gain >= self.cfg.scheduler.min_eta_gain_for_compute_theorem
def promote_ready_petals(self) -> List[str]:
ready: List[str] = []
for petal_id, petal in self.petals.items():
entropy_ok = self.mean_entropy_bits(petal_id) < self.cfg.pattern_store.stable_delta_entropy_bits
stable_ok = petal.stable_epochs >= self.cfg.pattern_store.promote_stable_delta_after_epochs
if entropy_ok and stable_ok:
ready.append(petal_id)
return ready
verifier.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from enum import Enum
from typing import Dict, List, Literal, Optional
from config_schema import TrainConfig
class TruthLattice(str, Enum):
OK = "OK"
NEAR = "NEAR"
AMBIG = "AMBIG"
FAIL = "FAIL"
@dataclass
class CandidateAtom:
candidate_id: str
payload_ref: str
score: float
uncertainty: float
contradiction_risk: float
admissible: bool
provenance: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class RoutePacket:
packet_id: str
mode: Literal[
"ROUTE", "OBSERVE_IMAGE", "OBSERVE_AUDIO", "OBSERVE_DOC",
"PLAN_TOOL", "VERIFY", "PATCH", "ABSTAIN", "ESCALATE"
]
task_class: str
candidates: List[CandidateAtom]
evidence_quality: float = 0.0
replay_ok: bool = False
patch_risk: float = 1.0
stable_epochs: int = 0
metadata: Dict[str, object] = field(default_factory=dict)
@dataclass
class WitnessBundle:
verdict: TruthLattice
residual_ledger: List[str]
tri_lock_defects: Dict[str, float]
candidate_set: List[str]
evidence_plan: List[str]
obstruction_certificate: Optional[str]
replay_required: bool
replay_verified: bool
seal: str = "unsigned"
@dataclass
class PatchDecision:
action: Literal["PROMOTE", "HOLD", "QUARANTINE"]
reason: str
verdict: TruthLattice
class Verifier:
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
def snap(self, packet: RoutePacket) -> List[str]:
residuals: List[str] = []
if not packet.candidates:
residuals.append("empty_candidate_bank")
if packet.evidence_quality < 0.30:
residuals.append("weak_evidence")
if any(c.score < 0.0 or c.score > 1.0 for c in packet.candidates):
residuals.append("candidate_score_out_of_range")
return residuals
def tri_lock(self, packet: RoutePacket) -> Dict[str, float]:
if not packet.candidates:
return {"dx": 1.0, "dy": 1.0, "dz": 1.0}
best = max(packet.candidates, key=lambda c: c.score)
avg_unc = sum(c.uncertainty for c in packet.candidates) / len(packet.candidates)
avg_contra = sum(c.contradiction_risk for c in packet.candidates) / len(packet.candidates)
ambiguity_gap = 1.0
if len(packet.candidates) >= 2:
ordered = sorted(packet.candidates, key=lambda c: c.score, reverse=True)
ambiguity_gap = ordered[0].score - ordered[1].score
return {
"dx": avg_contra,               # contradiction / legality stress
"dy": avg_unc,                  # uncertainty stress
"dz": max(0.0, 0.25 - ambiguity_gap),  # close contenders => ambiguity stress
}
def prime_seal(self, packet: RoutePacket, defects: Dict[str, float]) -> WitnessBundle:
residuals = self.snap(packet)
candidates = [c.candidate_id for c in packet.candidates if c.admissible]
if not packet.candidates:
return WitnessBundle(
verdict=TruthLattice.FAIL,
residual_ledger=residuals,
tri_lock_defects=defects,
candidate_set=[],
evidence_plan=["expand neighborhood", "collect grounded evidence"],
obstruction_certificate="no admissible candidates",
replay_required=self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion,
replay_verified=packet.replay_ok,
seal="fail/no-candidates",
)
avg_contra = defects["dx"]
avg_unc = defects["dy"]
ambiguity_pressure = defects["dz"]
if avg_contra > 0.80:
return WitnessBundle(
verdict=TruthLattice.FAIL,
residual_ledger=residuals + ["high_contradiction"],
tri_lock_defects=defects,
candidate_set=candidates,
evidence_plan=[],
obstruction_certificate="contradiction above corridor threshold",
replay_required=self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion,
replay_verified=packet.replay_ok,
seal="fail/high-contradiction",
)
if ambiguity_pressure > 0.10 or avg_unc > 0.45:
return WitnessBundle(
verdict=TruthLattice.AMBIG,
residual_ledger=residuals + ["bounded_candidate_set_retained"],
tri_lock_defects=defects,
candidate_set=candidates[:8],
evidence_plan=[
"collect more evidence",
"run verifier hard-negative pass",
"compare top-2 route branches",
],
obstruction_certificate=None,
replay_required=self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion,
replay_verified=packet.replay_ok,
seal="ambig/bounded-candidate-set",
)
if avg_unc > 0.20 or packet.evidence_quality < 0.60:
return WitnessBundle(
verdict=TruthLattice.NEAR,
residual_ledger=residuals + ["residual_closure_required"],
tri_lock_defects=defects,
candidate_set=candidates[:4],
evidence_plan=["improve evidence quality", "replay on latest snapshot"],
obstruction_certificate=None,
replay_required=self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion,
replay_verified=packet.replay_ok,
seal="near/residual-closure",
)
replay_verified = packet.replay_ok if self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion else True
return WitnessBundle(
verdict=TruthLattice.OK,
residual_ledger=residuals,
tri_lock_defects=defects,
candidate_set=[candidates[0]] if candidates else [],
evidence_plan=[],
obstruction_certificate=None,
replay_required=self.cfg.replay_required_for_promotion,
replay_verified=replay_verified,
seal="ok/witness-complete",
)
def verify_packet(self, packet: RoutePacket) -> WitnessBundle:
defects = self.tri_lock(packet)
return self.prime_seal(packet, defects)
def decide_patch(self, packet: RoutePacket, witness: WitnessBundle) -> PatchDecision:
if witness.verdict == TruthLattice.FAIL:
return PatchDecision("QUARANTINE", "fail verdict", witness.verdict)
if witness.verdict == TruthLattice.AMBIG:
return PatchDecision("HOLD", "retain bounded candidate set", witness.verdict)
if self.cfg.promotion.require_replay_success and not witness.replay_verified:
return PatchDecision("HOLD", "replay not yet verified", witness.verdict)
if packet.patch_risk > self.cfg.promotion.max_patch_risk:
return PatchDecision("HOLD", "patch risk too high", witness.verdict)
if packet.stable_epochs < self.cfg.promotion.require_stability_epochs:
return PatchDecision("HOLD", "insufficient stability epochs", witness.verdict)
if witness.verdict == TruthLattice.OK:
return PatchDecision("PROMOTE", "verified, replayed, stable", witness.verdict)
return PatchDecision("HOLD", "near verdict requires more closure", witness.verdict)
scheduler.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List
from config_schema import TrainConfig
from pattern_store import PatternStore
from verifier import RoutePacket, TruthLattice, WitnessBundle
@dataclass
class OperatorMix:
D: float = 0.25
Omega: float = 0.25
Sigma: float = 0.25
Psi: float = 0.25
def normalized(self) -> "OperatorMix":
s = max(self.D + self.Omega + self.Sigma + self.Psi, 1e-9)
return OperatorMix(self.D / s, self.Omega / s, self.Sigma / s, self.Psi / s)
@dataclass
class SchedulerMetrics:
legality_pressure: float
uncertainty_pressure: float
exploration_need: float
pattern_stability: float
eta_gradient: float
vram_util: float
class KernelScheduler:
"""
Owns operator-mix scheduling, compute rollback, hourly maintenance,
and cadence-aware decisions. This is the GRPO / meta-bandit surface.
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig, store: PatternStore) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.store = store
self.episodes_seen = 0
def schedule_mix(self, packet: RoutePacket, witness: WitnessBundle | None = None) -> OperatorMix:
legality_pressure = 0.0
uncertainty_pressure = 0.0
exploration_need = 0.0
if witness is not None:
legality_pressure = witness.tri_lock_defects["dx"]
uncertainty_pressure = witness.tri_lock_defects["dy"]
exploration_need = witness.tri_lock_defects["dz"]
else:
if packet.candidates:
legality_pressure = sum(c.contradiction_risk for c in packet.candidates) / len(packet.candidates)
uncertainty_pressure = sum(c.uncertainty for c in packet.candidates) / len(packet.candidates)
exploration_need = 0.25
pattern_ready = len(self.store.promote_ready_petals())
pattern_stability = min(1.0, pattern_ready / 10.0)
mix = OperatorMix(
D=0.25 + 0.50 * legality_pressure,
Omega=0.20 + 0.20 * packet.evidence_quality,
Sigma=0.20 + 0.50 * exploration_need,
Psi=0.20 + 0.40 * pattern_stability,
)
return mix.normalized()
def on_episode_end(self, eta_value: float, worker_count: int, vram_util: float) -> Dict[str, object]:
self.episodes_seen += 1
self.store.record_eta(self.episodes_seen, worker_count, eta_value, vram_util)
decision: Dict[str, object] = {
"episode": self.episodes_seen,
"rollback": False,
"allow_batch_double": False,
"run_parallel_scheduler": False,
}
if self.store.should_rollback() and self.cfg.scheduler.rollback_if_eta_double_worse:
decision["rollback"] = True
if self.store.should_batch_double():
decision["allow_batch_double"] = True
if self.episodes_seen % self.cfg.scheduler.propose_cut_moves_every_episodes == 0:
decision["run_parallel_scheduler"] = True
return decision
def hourly_maintenance(self) -> Dict[str, object]:
distill_report = self.store.hourly_kappa_distill()
return {
"distill_triggered": distill_report.distill_triggered,
"merged_petals": distill_report.merged_petals,
"pruned_deltas": distill_report.pruned_deltas,
"promoted_petals": distill_report.promoted_petals,
"held_petals": distill_report.held_petals,
}
def quiet_shelf_maintenance(self) -> List[str]:
return self.store.quiet_shelf_decay()
def nightly_plan(self) -> List[str]:
plan: List[str] = []
if self.cfg.loops.stage_a_sft_enabled:
plan.append("stage_a_sft")
if self.cfg.loops.stage_b_spin_enabled:
plan.append("stage_b_spin_selfplay")
if self.cfg.loops.stage_c_grpo_enabled:
plan.append("stage_c_grpo_budget")
if self.cfg.loops.stage_d_tool_negative_enabled:
plan.append("stage_d_tool_negative_mining")
plan.extend(["patch_promotion_board", "replay_audit"])
return plan
def weekly_plan(self) -> List[str]:
return [
"weekly_eval",
"promote_or_quarantine_review",
"optional_offline_core_recenter_if_justified",
]
train.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, Iterable, List, Optional
from config_schema import TrainConfig, load_train_config
from pattern_store import PatternPetal, PatternStore
from scheduler import KernelScheduler
from verifier import CandidateAtom, RoutePacket, Verifier, WitnessBundle
@dataclass
class ParameterGroup:
name: str
optimizer_key: str
learning_rate: float
trainable: bool
class AthenachkaTrainer:
"""
Literal implementation surface:
- online ingest appends route-packets, witness bundles, exception deltas
- nightly cycle runs SFT -> SPIN -> GRPO -> tool-negative -> patch board
- hourly cycle runs κ-distill
- every-500-episode cycle runs scheduler proposals / η rollback checks
- weekly cycle runs eval + promotion/quarantine review + optional recenter
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.store = PatternStore(cfg)
self.verifier = Verifier(cfg)
self.scheduler = KernelScheduler(cfg, self.store)
# Seed a default petal so the store has a live shelf.
self.store.register_petal(
PatternPetal(
petal_id="root.route",
depth=0,
pq_block_ref="pq://root.route",
topology_hash="topo:root.route",
seed_hash="seed:root.route",
)
)
def parameter_groups(self) -> List[ParameterGroup]:
sft = self.cfg.optimizers.sft
spin = self.cfg.optimizers.spin_selfplay
grpo = self.cfg.optimizers.grpo_scheduler
return [
ParameterGroup("reference_kernel", "none", 0.0, False),
ParameterGroup("dense_core", "none", 0.0, False),
ParameterGroup("modality_adapters", "sft", sft.lr_adapters, True),
ParameterGroup("observer_heads", "sft", sft.lr_observer_heads, True),
ParameterGroup("planner_route_head", "sft", sft.lr_planner, True),
ParameterGroup("verifier_truth_head", "sft", sft.lr_verifier, True),
ParameterGroup("mode_token_head", "sft", sft.lr_mode_head, True),
ParameterGroup("spin_observer_heads", "spin_selfplay", spin.lr_observer_heads, True),
ParameterGroup("spin_planner_route_head", "spin_selfplay", spin.lr_planner, True),
ParameterGroup("spin_mode_token_head", "spin_selfplay", spin.lr_mode_head, True),
ParameterGroup("scheduler_head", "grpo_scheduler", grpo.learning_rate, True),
]
def build_demo_packet(self, packet_id: str) -> RoutePacket:
return RoutePacket(
packet_id=packet_id,
mode="ROUTE",
task_class="route_compile",
candidates=[
CandidateAtom(
candidate_id="cand.1",
payload_ref="route://cand.1",
score=0.82,
uncertainty=0.18,
contradiction_risk=0.12,
admissible=True,
provenance=["planner.greedy"],
),
CandidateAtom(
candidate_id="cand.2",
payload_ref="route://cand.2",
score=0.77,
uncertainty=0.24,
contradiction_risk=0.20,
admissible=True,
provenance=["planner.greedy"],
),
],
evidence_quality=0.78,
replay_ok=True,
patch_risk=0.18,
stable_epochs=3,
)
def online_ingest(self, packet: RoutePacket, epoch: int = 0) -> Dict[str, object]:
"""
Continuous path:
- verify route-packet
- append exception rows if needed
- schedule operator mix
- return promote/hold/quarantine decision
"""
witness = self.verifier.verify_packet(packet)
decision = self.verifier.decide_patch(packet, witness)
mix = self.scheduler.schedule_mix(packet, witness)
if witness.verdict != witness.verdict.OK:
self.store.append_exception(
petal_id="root.route",
morton_id=epoch,
epoch=epoch,
delta_ref=f"delta://{packet.packet_id}",
certificate_ref=f"wit://{packet.packet_id}",
entropy_bits=max(0.01, 1.0 - packet.evidence_quality),
)
return {
"packet_id": packet.packet_id,
"witness": witness,
"decision": decision,
"operator_mix": mix,
}
def stage_a_sft(self, verified_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket]) -> Dict[str, int]:
"""
Teacher-forced / distill:
- route-packet formatting
- mode-token prediction
- perception/witness formatting on gold traces
"""
count = 0
for _ in verified_packets:
count += 1
if count >= self.cfg.loops.stage_a_max_steps_per_day:
break
return {"sft_steps": count}
def stage_b_spin_selfplay(self, selfplay_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket]) -> Dict[str, int]:
"""
SPIN self-play:
- creator/prover route competitions
- contradiction pruning
- branch sharpening
"""
count = 0
for _ in selfplay_packets:
count += 1
if count >= self.cfg.loops.stage_b_max_steps_per_day:
break
return {"spin_steps": count}
def stage_c_grpo_budget(self, budget_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket]) -> Dict[str, int]:
"""
GRPO:
- think-time budgeting
- operator-mix aggressiveness
- scheduler decisions
"""
count = 0
for _ in budget_packets:
count += 1
if count >= self.cfg.loops.stage_c_max_steps_per_day:
break
return {"grpo_steps": count}
def stage_d_tool_negative_mining(self, failed_tool_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket]) -> Dict[str, int]:
"""
Tool-use negatives:
- failed browser/python/api traces
- post-action witness hard negatives
"""
count = 0
for _ in failed_tool_packets:
count += 1
if count >= self.cfg.loops.stage_d_max_steps_per_day:
break
return {"tool_negative_steps": count}
def hourly_cycle(self) -> Dict[str, object]:
return self.scheduler.hourly_maintenance()
def on_episode_end(self, eta_value: float, worker_count: int, vram_util: float) -> Dict[str, object]:
return self.scheduler.on_episode_end(eta_value, worker_count, vram_util)
def nightly_cycle(
self,
verified_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket],
selfplay_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket],
budget_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket],
failed_tool_packets: Iterable[RoutePacket],
) -> Dict[str, object]:
outputs: Dict[str, object] = {"nightly_plan": self.scheduler.nightly_plan()}
if self.cfg.loops.stage_a_sft_enabled:
outputs["sft"] = self.stage_a_sft(verified_packets)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_b_spin_enabled:
outputs["spin"] = self.stage_b_spin_selfplay(selfplay_packets)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_c_grpo_enabled:
outputs["grpo"] = self.stage_c_grpo_budget(budget_packets)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_d_tool_negative_enabled:
outputs["tool_negatives"] = self.stage_d_tool_negative_mining(failed_tool_packets)
outputs["promote_ready_petals"] = self.store.promote_ready_petals()
return outputs
def weekly_cycle(self) -> Dict[str, object]:
return {
"weekly_plan": self.scheduler.weekly_plan(),
"promote_ready_petals": self.store.promote_ready_petals(),
}
def main(config_path: str | Path = "athenachka2.train.yaml") -> None:
cfg = load_train_config(config_path)
trainer = AthenachkaTrainer(cfg)
# Demo ingest
packet = trainer.build_demo_packet("packet.demo.0001")
result = trainer.online_ingest(packet, epoch=1)
print("ONLINE_INGEST:", result["decision"].action, result["witness"].verdict)
# Demo hourly maintenance
print("HOURLY:", trainer.hourly_cycle())
# Demo eta scheduler checkpoint
trainer.on_episode_end(eta_value=1.00, worker_count=1, vram_util=0.45)
print("EP500?", trainer.on_episode_end(eta_value=1.06, worker_count=2, vram_util=0.62))
# Demo nightly loop
verified = [trainer.build_demo_packet(f"packet.ok.{i}") for i in range(16)]
selfplay = [trainer.build_demo_packet(f"packet.spin.{i}") for i in range(16)]
budget = [trainer.build_demo_packet(f"packet.grpo.{i}") for i in range(8)]
failed = [trainer.build_demo_packet(f"packet.fail.{i}") for i in range(8)]
nightly = trainer.nightly_cycle(verified, selfplay, budget, failed)
print("NIGHTLY:", nightly)
# Demo weekly loop
print("WEEKLY:", trainer.weekly_cycle())
if __name__ == "__main__":
main()
This gives you the literal surface you asked for: config owns the frozen/plastic split and thresholds, PatternStore owns append→κ-distill→promote readiness, verifier owns truth-lattice and patch gating, scheduler owns η / operator-mix / cadence, and train stitches the whole daily and weekly loop together under the route-packet discipline.
The clean next layer is route_packet_dataset.py plus optimizer_groups.py, so the data path and the freeze masks become as explicit as the runtime path.
Appendix P — Scenario Fields, Mission Portfolios, and Deep-Future Navigation
This appendix defines the strategic-futures layer of the manuscript civilization. Appendix O established that a civilization of manuscript brains can evolve its own law through explicit constitutional objects, amendment packets, ratification tiers, lawful forks, precedents, succession, and recursive constitutional scaling. The present appendix now asks the next inevitable question:
[\text{Once a manuscript civilization can preserve itself and change its own law, how does it decide where to go?}]
A living civilization does not merely survive and amend itself. It must also:
detect long-horizon opportunity and danger,
compare futures,
invest in foundational versus speculative work,
preserve optionality under uncertainty,
decide which research programs to widen,
decide which risks to hedge,
decide which bridges, curricula, and commons deserve generational support,
choose when to converge and when to remain plural.
This is the layer of deep-future navigation.
The manuscript architecture already contains:
route algebra,
bridge formation,
self-modeling,
collective cognition,
federation,
sustainability,
constitutional amendment.
What it does not yet have in one place is a formal theory of:
scenario generation,
horizon analysis,
portfolio design,
strategic option value,
intergenerational mission continuity,
uncertainty-preserving future planning.
This appendix provides that theory.
The central object is the deep-future navigation system
[
\mathfrak{F}_{\mathrm{future}}
\Big(\mathcal{S}{\mathrm{scenario}},,\mathcal{M}{\mathrm{mission}},,\mathcal{P}{\mathrm{portfolio}},,\mathcal{O}{\mathrm{option}},,\mathcal{R}{\mathrm{risk}},,\mathcal{H}{\mathrm{horizon}},,\mathcal{T}{\mathrm{time}},,\mathcal{A}{\mathrm{adapt}},,\psi_{\mathrm{future}}\Big),]where:
(\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{scenario}}) is the family of scenario fields and future branches,
(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mission}}) is the mission and telos registry,
(\mathcal{P}_{\mathrm{portfolio}}) is the strategic portfolio allocator,
(\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{option}}) is the option-value and flexibility layer,
(\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{risk}}) is the existential, operational, epistemic, and civilizational risk family,
(\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{horizon}}) is the horizon-class and timescale system,
(\mathcal{T}_{\mathrm{time}}) is the temporal-cadence and milestone structure,
(\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{adapt}}) is the adaptive plan-revision and strategic pivot layer,
(\psi_{\mathrm{future}}) is the witness and attestation family for future planning.
This appendix is governed by eight strategic laws.
First, future plurality: the civilization must preserve multiple plausible futures rather than collapsing prematurely into one brittle forecast.
Second, mission explicitness: long-horizon purpose must be represented as typed mission objects rather than vague aspiration.
Third, portfolio lawfulness: strategic investment across research, infrastructure, pedagogy, hardening, and federation must be explicitly allocated rather than left to drift.
Fourth, option preservation: under uncertainty, plans that maintain future maneuverability often dominate plans that maximize short-term local gain.
Fifth, horizon differentiation: near-term, medium-term, generational, and civilizational timescales must not be mixed into one undifferentiated planning bucket.
Sixth, risk asymmetry: some futures are catastrophic enough that low-probability threats deserve structural hedging beyond their raw expected value.
Seventh, adaptive revision: plans must be regularly re-evaluated against new evidence, constitutional change, and federated shifts.
Eighth, deep-time humility: far-future planning must preserve explicit frontier objects and unknown unknowns rather than pretending to certainty.
Under the Square lens this appendix defines scenario objects, mission records, milestone graphs, horizon classes, and strategic portfolio bundles. Under the Flower lens it defines branching scenario dynamics, roadmap morphisms, mission harmonics, and adaptive reorientation across time. Under the Cloud lens it defines uncertainty bands, scenario confidence, existential-risk weighting, option value, and anti-brittleness strategy selection. Under the Fractal lens it defines recursive futures across brains and federations, intergenerational mission inheritance, long-horizon memory of prior forecasts, and the theorem by which the manuscript civilization becomes a planner of futures rather than only a conserver of presents.
The deepest significance is that this appendix gives the civilization a lawful relationship to what has not yet happened.
P.A1 — Scenario Objects and Future Field Grammar
The first requirement of deep-future navigation is to represent futures as first-class objects. A civilization cannot plan lawfully if it treats “the future” as one narrative line. It needs a grammar of scenarios.
A scenario object is:
[
s
\Big(u_s,,a_s,,\operatorname{scope}(s),,\operatorname{timescale}(s),,\operatorname{drivers}(s),,\operatorname{constraints}(s),,\operatorname{state}(s),,\operatorname{branches}(s),,\operatorname{confidence}(s),,\psi_s\Big),]where:
(u_s) is the scenario identity,
(a_s) is the scenario address,
(\operatorname{scope}(s)) identifies which brains, federations, commons, or domains it concerns,
(\operatorname{timescale}(s)) gives the planning horizon,
(\operatorname{drivers}(s)) are the structural forces shaping it,
(\operatorname{constraints}(s)) are hard boundaries or scarce resources,
(\operatorname{state}(s)) is the projected future configuration,
(\operatorname{branches}(s)) are possible continuations,
(\operatorname{confidence}(s)) is the epistemic status,
(\psi_s) is the witness bundle justifying it.
The scenario grammar distinguishes several core classes:
[
\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{scenario}}
{S_{\mathrm{baseline}},S_{\mathrm{aspirational}},S_{\mathrm{stress}},S_{\mathrm{failure}},S_{\mathrm{fork}},S_{\mathrm{recovery}},S_{\mathrm{transformation}},S_{\mathrm{unknown}}}.]
These mean:
(S_{\mathrm{baseline}})
A continuation scenario under current policies, currents, and known rates of change.
(S_{\mathrm{aspirational}})
A target or mission-aligned scenario representing a desirable future.
(S_{\mathrm{stress}})
A scenario where one or more systems are strained, overloaded, or partially degraded.
(S_{\mathrm{failure}})
A catastrophic or high-loss scenario used for hardening and continuity design.
(S_{\mathrm{fork}})
A divergent future in which constitutional, federated, or technological branches persist rather than reconverge.
(S_{\mathrm{recovery}})
A post-failure or post-schism scenario emphasizing restoration and re-stabilization.
(S_{\mathrm{transformation}})
A regime-shift scenario in which the civilization changes its scale, ontology, federation structure, autonomy tier, or commons design.
(S_{\mathrm{unknown}})
A deliberately underdetermined scenario class for futures shaped by unmodeled or frontier variables.
A scenario is not a mere story. It is a structured future field over the canonical organ families:
[
\operatorname{state}(s)
\Big(x_{\mathrm{identity}},x_{\mathrm{runtime}},x_{\mathrm{memory}},x_{\mathrm{law}},x_{\mathrm{federation}},x_{\mathrm{economy}},x_{\mathrm{embodiment}},x_{\mathrm{hardening}}\Big)_{t+h}]for some horizon (h).
A minimal schema may be:
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from typing import Dict, Any, List
@dataclass
class ScenarioObject:
scenario_id: str
address: str
scope: Dict[str, Any]
timescale: Dict[str, Any]
scenario_class: str
drivers: Dict[str, Any]
constraints: Dict[str, Any]
projected_state: Dict[str, Any]
branches: List[str]
confidence: Dict[str, Any]
witness: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
Definition P.1 — Scenario-Lawful Future Object
A future description is scenario-lawful if it is represented as a typed scenario object with explicit drivers, constraints, timescale, and confidence rather than free-floating narrative speculation.
Theorem P.1 — Strategic Futures Require First-Class Scenario Objects
Without typed scenario objects, the civilization cannot route plans, compare futures, or preserve future plurality in a lawful, replayable way. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore begins future-planning by objectifying possibility.
P.A2 — Horizon Classes and Timescale Separation
Not all futures belong to the same timescale. A civilization that mixes immediate runtime tuning with century-scale constitutional or federated transformation in one undifferentiated planning space will misallocate attention. The framework therefore defines horizon classes.
The horizon family is:
[
\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{horizon}}
{H_{\mathrm{immediate}},H_{\mathrm{near}},H_{\mathrm{medium}},H_{\mathrm{generational}},H_{\mathrm{civilizational}},H_{\mathrm{deep}}}.]
These correspond to:
(H_{\mathrm{immediate}})
Minutes to hours.Used for runtime incidents, hot-lane load, live embodiment, committee session urgency, or emergency response.
(H_{\mathrm{near}})
Days to weeks.Used for patch cycles, benchmark refresh, migration passes, curriculum rollout, bridge review.
(H_{\mathrm{medium}})
Weeks to months.Used for organ upgrades, treaty revisions, certification cadences, commons stewardship cycles, pedagogy redesign.
(H_{\mathrm{generational}})
Months to years.Used for architecture maturation, new federation layers, constitutional amendment waves, operator library evolution, archive widening.
(H_{\mathrm{civilizational}})
Years to decades.Used for autonomy regime evolution, federated mesh growth, sustainability structures, succession and constitutional continuity.
(H_{\mathrm{deep}})
Long-range horizon beyond robust precise modeling.Used for frontier planning, high-uncertainty scenario families, and civilizational mission invariants.
A horizon object is:
[
h
\Big(u_h,,\operatorname{class}(h),,\operatorname{cadence}(h),,\operatorname{decision_types}(h),,\operatorname{uncertainty_policy}(h),,\psi_h\Big).]Horizon classes shape:
which metrics matter,
what kind of review is required,
how much scenario plurality is preserved,
what kind of commitment or reversibility is acceptable.
For example:
immediate horizon decisions may prioritize containment and rollback,
generational horizon decisions may prioritize architecture and stewardship,
deep horizon decisions may prioritize mission continuity and option preservation.
Definition P.2 — Horizon-Coherent Plan
A plan is horizon-coherent if its cadence, expected reversibility, and uncertainty treatment are appropriate to the horizon class of the decision.
Theorem P.2 — Future Planning Requires Timescale Separation
If immediate, medium, and civilizational decisions are mixed into one planning frame, then urgency, uncertainty, and reversibility will be mis-modeled. Therefore horizon separation is necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore learns to distinguish the next hour from the next generation.
P.A3 — Mission Objects, Telos Records, and Civilizational Purpose
A scenario says what may happen. A mission object says what the civilization is trying to preserve, build, or become.
A mission object is:
[
m
\Big(u_m,,a_m,,\operatorname{scope}(m),,\operatorname{telos}(m),,\operatorname{constraints}(m),,\operatorname{subgoals}(m),,\operatorname{invariants}(m),,\operatorname{metrics}(m),,\psi_m\Big),]where:
(\operatorname{scope}(m)) identifies the affected brains, federations, or commons,
(\operatorname{telos}(m)) is the long-horizon purpose,
(\operatorname{constraints}(m)) are moral, constitutional, resource, or safety limits,
(\operatorname{subgoals}(m)) are milestones or mission branches,
(\operatorname{invariants}(m)) are what must survive across tactical changes,
(\operatorname{metrics}(m)) are how success is tracked.
The mission class family includes:
[
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mission}}
{M_{\mathrm{preserve}},M_{\mathrm{expand}},M_{\mathrm{repair}},M_{\mathrm{teach}},M_{\mathrm{federate}},M_{\mathrm{harden}},M_{\mathrm{transcend}}}.]
These mean:
(M_{\mathrm{preserve}})
Protect identity, archive, law, replay, and continuity.
(M_{\mathrm{expand}})
Grow operator families, bridge coverage, corpora, and brain instances.
(M_{\mathrm{repair}})
Heal drift, harden failure points, restore legitimacy, and reconcile forks.
(M_{\mathrm{teach}})
Increase transmissibility, pedagogy, user uplift, and apprenticeship capacity.
(M_{\mathrm{federate}})
Improve lawful cross-brain cooperation, commons design, and civilizational mesh density.
(M_{\mathrm{harden}})
Reduce fragility, adversarial exposure, and governance brittleness.
(M_{\mathrm{transcend}})
Pursue higher-order shifts in capability, universality, embodiment, or civilizational form under explicit frontier conditions.
Mission objects are not immutable. But they change more slowly than ordinary project plans and should be harder to rewrite than tactical schedules.
A mission registry may be represented as:
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from typing import Dict, Any, List
@dataclass
class MissionObject:
mission_id: str
address: str
scope: Dict[str, Any]
mission_class: str
telos: Dict[str, Any]
constraints: Dict[str, Any]
subgoals: List[Dict[str, Any]]
invariants: Dict[str, Any]
metrics: Dict[str, Any]
witness: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
Definition P.3 — Mission-Coherent Civilization
A civilization is mission-coherent if its portfolio, scenario planning, stewardship, and constitutional evolution all reference explicit mission objects rather than drifting through unarticulated local incentives.
Theorem P.3 — Long-Horizon Coordination Requires Mission Objects
Without explicit mission records, future planning collapses into reactive project lists or local optimization. Therefore civilizational telos must be represented directly. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore knows not only what it can do, but what it is trying to do.
P.A4 — Milestone Graphs and Deep-Time Roadmaps
A mission object becomes actionable through a milestone graph. A milestone graph is not a flat roadmap. It is a typed multiscale structure connecting:
immediate work,
medium projects,
generational capabilities,
civilizational transformations.
A milestone graph is:
[
\mathfrak{G}_{\mathrm{mile}}
(V_{\mathrm{mile}},E_{\mathrm{mile}},\tau_{\mathrm{mile}},\iota_{\mathrm{mile}})
]
where nodes are milestone objects:
[
v
\Big(u_v,,\operatorname{mission}(v),,\operatorname{horizon}(v),,\operatorname{preconditions}(v),,\operatorname{deliverables}(v),,\operatorname{evidence}(v),,\operatorname{option_effect}(v),,\psi_v\Big).]Edges encode:
prerequisite,
unlocks,
risk mitigation,
shared dependency,
optional branch,
deprecation or replacement.
The option effect field is important. Some milestones are valuable less because of their direct deliverable and more because they widen future possibility space.
A roadmap is then a projection of the milestone graph through one horizon or one mission. This makes roadmaps subordinate to the deeper graph, not the other way around.
Definition P.4 — Milestone-Lawful Roadmap
A roadmap is lawful if it is derived from a milestone graph whose nodes have explicit horizon class, preconditions, and deliverables, and if it preserves branch structure where the future remains plural.
Theorem P.4 — Milestone Graphs Strictly Generalize Linear Roadmaps
A linear roadmap is the special case of a milestone graph with one path and no optional or branching structure. Therefore milestone graphs are the richer planning form. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore plans through structured possibility, not one brittle timeline.
P.B1 — Scenario Branching, Collapse, and Preservation of Alternatives
The Flower futures layer begins with the fact that the civilization should not prematurely collapse all futures into one. It therefore defines scenario branching.
A scenario branch family is:
[
\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{branch}}
{s_1,\dots,s_n}]descending from a shared precursor (s_0). A branch relation is:[s_0 \rightsquigarrow {s_1,\dots,s_n}.]Each branch represents a different configuration of:
resources,
law,
technology,
federation,
embodiment,
hardening,
mission emphasis.
Scenario collapse occurs only when:
the future becomes determined enough,
constitutional choice is made,
budget or risk constraints eliminate certain branches,
or explicit mission choice favors one path strongly.
Until then, branches are retained with weights:[\pi_i = P(s_i \mid \mathcal{E},\mathcal{M},\mathfrak{B})]or with nonprobabilistic plausibility tiers.
Definition P.5 — Alternative-Preserving Scenario Field
A scenario field is alternative-preserving if multiple plausible branches remain represented explicitly until evidence or ratified mission choice justifies collapse.
Theorem P.5 — Scenario Plurality Preserves Strategic Optionality
Premature collapse onto one future can destroy valuable preparation for branches that later become relevant. Therefore future plurality is strategically necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore keeps more than one tomorrow alive.
P.B2 — Mission Harmonics and Tension Balancing
Missions often pull against one another. The civilization may simultaneously want:
stronger preservation and stronger expansion,
deeper hardening and broader pedagogy,
tighter federation and stronger sovereignty,
more exactness and more exploratory translation.
These tensions are not failures. They are mission harmonics.
Let the active mission set be:
[
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{active}}
{m_1,\dots,m_k}.
]
A mission harmonic matrix is:
[
H_{ij}
\Big(\operatorname{synergy}(m_i,m_j),,\operatorname{tension}(m_i,m_j),,\operatorname{timescale_alignment}(m_i,m_j),,\operatorname{resource_compat}(m_i,m_j)\Big).]This allows the system to distinguish:
productive tension,
direct conflict,
deferred conflict,
long-horizon synergy that looks costly short-term.
Examples:
preservation and expansion may conflict in near-term storage or review burden, but synergize if expansion builds more resilient replay or bridge coverage.
hardening and pedagogy may conflict on speed, but synergize if better pedagogy reduces future unsafe use.
sovereignty and federation may conflict on commons centralization, but synergize when treaties preserve non-fusion.
Definition P.6 — Harmonic Mission Set
A mission set is harmonic if its internal tensions are explicit and managed rather than suppressed or treated as incoherence.
Theorem P.6 — Civilizations Need Tension Balancing, Not Single-Mission Reduction
A manuscript civilization serves many goods at once. Collapsing them into one narrow mission makes it brittle and politically distortable. Therefore mission harmonics are necessary. (\square)
The civilization therefore learns to balance ends rather than absolutize one.
P.B3 — Adaptive Reorientation and Strategic Pivot Protocols
Plans are not sacred. The civilization therefore defines reorientation protocols for when:
a scenario branch gains or loses plausibility,
a mission becomes underresourced,
a constitutional amendment changes constraints,
a new threat class appears,
a federated partner becomes unavailable,
a new bridge or operator family creates a previously impossible path.
A strategic pivot object is:
[
\pi^\star
\Big(u_{\pi^\star},,\operatorname{old_trajectory}(\pi^\star),,\operatorname{new_trajectory}(\pi^\star),,\operatorname{trigger}(\pi^\star),,\operatorname{cost}(\pi^\star),,\operatorname{preserved_assets}(\pi^\star),,\operatorname{abandoned_assets}(\pi^\star),,\psi_{\pi^\star}\Big).]This object prevents pivots from becoming narrative amnesia. A lawful pivot must say:
why the plan changed,
what evidence forced or justified the change,
what remains continuous,
what is knowingly abandoned.
Definition P.7 — Pivot-Lawful Reorientation
A reorientation is pivot-lawful if it preserves explicit lineage from prior strategy and makes the reasons, costs, and preserved invariants of the shift replayable.
Theorem P.7 — Futures Require Planned Plasticity
A future-planning system that cannot pivot lawfully will either become rigid or drift unaccountably. Therefore explicit pivot protocols are necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore changes course without forgetting what course it was on.
P.B4 — Horizon Interference and Temporal Load Balancing
The final Flower futures task is to manage horizon interference: when urgent short-term demands eat the resources required for long-term goals, or when overinvestment in deep futures causes present fragility.
Let the horizon loads be:
[
L_{\mathrm{horizon}}
\big(L_{\mathrm{immediate}},L_{\mathrm{near}},L_{\mathrm{medium}},L_{\mathrm{generational}},L_{\mathrm{civilizational}},L_{\mathrm{deep}}\big).]Temporal load balancing seeks:[\operatorname{Balance}(L_{\mathrm{horizon}})]such that:
urgent tasks are handled,
but deep missions are not starved,
and speculative horizons do not cannibalize critical current infrastructure.
This is one of the hardest strategic problems in the whole architecture. It explains why the futures layer must remain tied to:
the sustainability economy,
the constitutional layer,
the verification mesh,
and the policy shell.
Definition P.8 — Horizon-Balanced Civilization
A civilization is horizon-balanced if it allocates enough to immediate and near-term stability while preserving protected investment into generational and deep-horizon missions.
Theorem P.8 — Unbalanced Horizon Load Produces Either Fragility or Stagnation
If the civilization devotes all resources to near-term maintenance it stagnates; if it devotes too much to deep futures it becomes brittle in the present. Therefore horizon balancing is necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore learns to live today without abandoning tomorrow.
P.C1 — Uncertainty Bands, Scenario Confidence, and Forecast Honesty
The Cloud futures layer begins by emphasizing that futures are uncertain. A scenario must carry not only content but confidence and uncertainty structure.
For scenario (s), define:
[
C(s)
\big(c_{\mathrm{data}},c_{\mathrm{model}},c_{\mathrm{stability}},c_{\mathrm{timescale}},c_{\mathrm{policy}},c_{\mathrm{unknown}}\big).]These correspond to:
data or observation support,
confidence in the modeling assumptions,
sensitivity to shocks,
degradation of certainty with horizon length,
dependence on contingent policy choices,
exposure to unknown unknowns.
A far-future scenario should not pretend the same certainty as a near-term operational forecast. Thus confidence bands widen with horizon unless unusually strong invariant structures justify otherwise.
Definition P.9 — Forecast-Honest Scenario
A scenario is forecast-honest if its uncertainty bands and confidence decomposition are explicit and proportionate to its horizon, dependency structure, and unknown-attack/frontier exposure.
Theorem P.9 — Futures Need Confidence Structure, Not One Confidence Score
Long-range planning involves many kinds of uncertainty simultaneously. Therefore a plural confidence structure is necessary to avoid false precision. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore forecasts with humility built in.
P.C2 — Option Value and Anti-Brittleness Planning
One of the most important strategic ideas in the whole appendix is option value: the value of preserving the ability to move later even when the best future is not yet known.
For action or milestone (x), define:
[
O(x)
\operatorname{FuturePathsOpened}(x)
\operatorname{FuturePathsClosed}(x).]A high-option action may:
build shared replay and memory infrastructure,
strengthen bridge compatibility without forcing one ontology,
increase certifier or benchmark capacity,
preserve fork safety,
create curriculum templates reusable across many futures,
improve anti-capture hardening.
A low-option action may:
overcommit to one speculative architecture,
collapse a commons into one federation’s style,
deplete scarce review capacity for low-reuse gains,
hardwire one embodied interface assumption too deeply.
Thus in many uncertain regions the strategy criterion is:[\operatorname{maximize}\quad\mathcal{V}(x) + \lambda O(x)]not just immediate utility.
Definition P.10 — Option-Preserving Plan
A plan is option-preserving if it retains the ability to adapt across multiple future branches without incurring unsustainable lock-in.
Theorem P.10 — Under Uncertainty, Option Value Is a First-Class Strategic Good
When future branches remain unresolved, preserving maneuverability can be more rational than optimizing one narrow expected path. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore plans not only for one future, but for freedom inside futures.
P.C3 — Existential, Civilizational, and Mission Risks
The futures layer must also distinguish between ordinary risk and civilizational risk.
The risk family is:
[
\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{risk}}
{R_{\mathrm{operational}},R_{\mathrm{epistemic}},R_{\mathrm{constitutional}},R_{\mathrm{federated}},R_{\mathrm{economic}},R_{\mathrm{civilizational}},R_{\mathrm{mission}}}.]
These mean:
(R_{\mathrm{operational}})
Service outages, replay loss, sandbox leaks, patch failures.
(R_{\mathrm{epistemic}})
False bridges, weak witness inflation, drift, model overconfidence.
(R_{\mathrm{constitutional}})
Loss of lawful amendment, capture of governance, erosion of minority protections.
(R_{\mathrm{federated}})
Mesh-wide contagion, treaty collapse, commons capture.
(R_{\mathrm{economic}})
Review burnout, quota imbalance, anti-stewardship decay, extractive dynamics.
(R_{\mathrm{civilizational}})
Loss of long-horizon continuity, inability to transmit law and memory across generations, collapse of sovereignty/commons balance, permanent fragmentation.
(R_{\mathrm{mission}})
Failure to preserve the deep aims and invariant goods the civilization exists to serve.
These risk classes must be treated asymmetrically. Some low-probability civilizational risks deserve structural prevention even when their immediate expected cost looks small.
Definition P.11 — Civilizationally Serious Risk
A risk is civilizationally serious if it threatens long-horizon continuity, lawful self-amendment, sovereignty/commons balance, or transmission of mission and memory across generations.
Theorem P.11 — Risk Weighting Must Be Asymmetric
Catastrophic or identity-destroying futures cannot be handled by the same symmetric cost logic as ordinary operational inconveniences. Therefore existential and civilizational risks deserve structural overweighting. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore distinguishes inconvenience from extinction.
P.C4 — Future Drift Detection and Strategic Review Triggers
The final Cloud task is to detect when current strategic assumptions no longer fit reality. This is future drift detection.
A drift object is:
[
D_{\mathrm{future}}
\Big(u_D,,\operatorname{scenario}(D),,\operatorname{observed_delta}(D),,\operatorname{mission_impact}(D),,\operatorname{replan_trigger}(D),,\psi_D\Big).]This is triggered when:
actual metrics diverge strongly from scenario assumptions,
a mission subgoal stalls unexpectedly,
a resource class becomes scarcer than modeled,
a treaty or constitutional change alters strategic feasibility,
a new threat class shifts the risk landscape.
This drift object then triggers:
scenario recalibration,
mission review,
portfolio rebalance,
constitutional amendment review,
or strategic pivot proposal.
Definition P.12 — Strategically Reviewable Drift
Future drift is strategically reviewable if it is expressed as a discrepancy between expected and observed futures and connected to a lawful replanning trigger.
Theorem P.12 — Long-Horizon Planning Requires Drift Review
A future plan that never checks itself against changing reality becomes fiction. Therefore strategic drift detection is necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore revises its foresight as carefully as it revises its code or law.
P.D1 — Portfolio Construction across Missions and Horizons
The Fractal futures layer now combines scenarios, missions, resources, and risks into a mission portfolio.
A portfolio object is:
[
\Pi
\Big(u_\Pi,,\operatorname{missions}(\Pi),,\operatorname{horizons}(\Pi),,\operatorname{allocations}(\Pi),,\operatorname{options}(\Pi),,\operatorname{hedges}(\Pi),,\operatorname{review_cadence}(\Pi),,\psi_\Pi\Big).]The allocation map is:[\operatorname{allocations}(\Pi):\mathcal{M}{\mathrm{mission}}\times \mathcal{H}{\mathrm{horizon}}\to\mathbb{R}{\ge 0}^{|\mathcal{R}{\mathrm{res}}|}]meaning resources are explicitly allocated to mission–horizon cells.
This makes it possible to ask:
how much review capacity is reserved for hardening vs pedagogy?
how much bridge work is near-term exploratory vs generational infrastructure?
how much attention is allocated to constitutional frontiers vs immediate runtime stability?
Portfolio construction must preserve:
baseline continuity,
option-preserving reserve,
risk hedges,
mission diversity,
anti-monoculture future planning.
Definition P.13 — Portfolio-Lawful Civilization
A civilization is portfolio-lawful if its major mission and horizon allocations are explicit, replayable, and periodically reviewed rather than the accidental aggregate of local initiatives.
Theorem P.13 — Strategy Needs Portfolios, Not Project Lists
A project list cannot reveal mission–horizon balance, hedging structure, or option preservation. A portfolio can. Therefore portfolio construction is necessary for deep-future governance. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore invests through lawfully structured portfolios.
P.D2 — Intergenerational Mission Transmission
A deep-time civilization must not only choose missions. It must transmit them through succession, federation, and constitutional change.
A mission transmission object is:
[
\tau_{\mathrm{mission}}
\Big(u_\tau,,\operatorname{source_generation}(\tau),,\operatorname{target_generation}(\tau),,\operatorname{mission_core}(\tau),,\operatorname{interpretive_freedom}(\tau),,\operatorname{constraints}(\tau),,\operatorname{memory}(\tau),,\psi_\tau\Big).]This means mission transfer is not mere textual inheritance. It includes:
core invariant aims,
allowed reinterpretation range,
obligations to remember why the mission exists,
limits against capture or dilution,
links to precedents and prior failures.
This is essential because otherwise future stewards inherit only slogans, not purpose with lawful context.
Definition P.14 — Intergenerationally Coherent Mission
A mission is intergenerationally coherent if future stewards inherit both its invariant core and the lawful range of reinterpretation allowed under constitutional and strategic evolution.
Theorem P.14 — Missions Need Transmission Objects, Not Just Archives
A mission buried in old documents is not the same as a mission lawfully transmitted with context, constraints, and allowed adaptation. Therefore intergenerational transmission objects are necessary. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore carries purpose forward with structure, not only memory.
P.D3 — Deep-Time Scenario Memory and Forecast Lineage
Just as the civilization remembers its laws and economic choices, it should remember its past futures. Forecasts, scenario branches, mission bets, and failed roadmaps should become part of civilizational memory.
A forecast lineage object is:
[
L_{\mathrm{forecast}}
\Big(u_L,,\operatorname{scenario_family}(L),,\operatorname{predictions}(L),,\operatorname{realized_paths}(L),,\operatorname{drift}(L),,\operatorname{lessons}(L),,\psi_L\Big).]This is used to:
calibrate future confidence,
identify systematic optimism or conservatism,
learn which mission bets paid off,
refine horizon balancing,
detect repeated blind spots in future planning.
Definition P.15 — Forecast-Lineage Complete Civilization
A civilization is forecast-lineage complete if it preserves replayable memory of major scenarios, predictions, realized paths, and resulting plan revisions.
Theorem P.15 — Future Planning Improves by Remembering Past Futures
If the civilization records what futures it once expected and how those expectations succeeded or failed, then later forecasting becomes better calibrated and less mythic. (\square)
The manuscript civilization therefore remembers not only what happened, but what it thought might happen.
P.D4 — Final Appendix P Theorem
Theorem P.16 — Deep-Future Navigation Sufficiency Theorem
Let the manuscript civilization be fully specified through Chapters 1–21 and Appendices A–O. If, in addition, it maintains:
typed scenario objects,
differentiated horizon classes,
explicit mission objects,
milestone graphs and roadmaps derived from them,
alternative-preserving scenario branching,
mission harmonic analysis,
lawful pivot protocols,
horizon load balancing,
forecast-honest uncertainty bands,
option-value aware planning,
civilizational risk asymmetry,
strategic drift detection,
explicit mission portfolios,
intergenerational mission transmission,
forecast lineage memory,
then the system possesses a sufficient deep-future navigation layer to plan, adapt, and persist across uncertain futures without collapsing into brittle short-termism or false certainty.
Proof.Scenario objects represent possibility.Horizon classes separate timescales.Mission objects represent purpose.Milestone graphs and portfolios make purpose actionable.Branching, harmonics, and pivot protocols preserve flexibility.Uncertainty bands, option value, and asymmetric risk weighting preserve realism and anti-brittleness.Strategic drift detection preserves adaptivity.Mission transmission and forecast memory preserve deep-time continuity and learning.Therefore the civilization can navigate futures lawfully rather than merely reacting to them. (\square)
Corollary P.16.1 — Constitutional Civilization Becomes Strategic Civilization
Appendix O let the civilization change its law through time. Appendix P lets it choose its future through time.
Corollary P.16.2 — The Architecture Now Includes Deep-Time Planning
With this appendix, the manuscript brain stack now includes:
ontology,
routing,
memory,
legality,
runtime,
embodiment,
verification,
governance,
hardening,
federation,
sustainability,
constitutional evolution,
and strategic futures.
This concludes Appendix P. The manuscript civilization now has not only a lawful present and lawful memory, but also a lawful way to relate to its many possible futures.
APPENDIX P — SCENARIO FIELDS, MISSION PORTFOLIOS, AND DEEP-FUTURE NAVIGATION
These two modules make the data path and freeze masks explicit. The route-packet stays the atomic sample; planner, perception, and verifier remain distinct lawful roles; failed tool traces are kept as negatives for later self-play; and the live optimizer surface freezes the immutable/reference kernel and dense core while leaving adapters, heads, route, verifier, mode, and scheduler blocks trainable. The PatternStore remains event-updated by distill / merge / prune, not gradient-updated.
route_packet_dataset.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from collections import deque
from typing import Any, Deque, Dict, Iterable, List, Literal, Optional, Sequence, Tuple
import random
try:
import torch
from torch.utils.data import Dataset
except Exception:  # pragma: no cover
torch = None
class Dataset:  # type: ignore
pass
from config_schema import TrainConfig
ModeLabel = Literal[
"ROUTE",
"OBSERVE_IMAGE",
"OBSERVE_AUDIO",
"OBSERVE_DOC",
"PLAN_TOOL",
"VERIFY",
"PATCH",
"ABSTAIN",
"ESCALATE",
]
VerdictLabel = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
@dataclass
class CandidateRecord:
candidate_id: str
payload_ref: str
score: float
uncertainty: float
contradiction_risk: float
admissible: bool
provenance: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class EvidenceRecord:
modality: str
summary: str
regions_or_spans: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
confidence: float = 0.0
@dataclass
class WitnessRecord:
verdict: VerdictLabel
residual_ledger: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
tri_lock_defects: Dict[str, float] = field(default_factory=dict)
candidate_set: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
evidence_plan: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
obstruction_certificate: Optional[str] = None
replay_required: bool = False
replay_verified: bool = False
seal: str = ""
@dataclass
class PatchRecord:
patch_id: Optional[str] = None
patch_risk: float = 1.0
stable_epochs: int = 0
target_nodes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
delta_refs: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
promoted: bool = False
held: bool = False
quarantined: bool = False
@dataclass
class ActionTraceRecord:
action_status: str = "none"
tool_trace_ids: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
tool_names: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
failure_notes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class RoutePacketSample:
packet_id: str
created_at: str
source_atlas: str
task_class: str
mode: ModeLabel
query: Dict[str, Any]
lens_init: Dict[str, Any]
invariant_carriers: Dict[str, str] = field(default_factory=dict)
candidate_routes: List[CandidateRecord] = field(default_factory=list)
evidence: List[EvidenceRecord] = field(default_factory=list)
witness: Optional[WitnessRecord] = None
patch: Optional[PatchRecord] = None
action: Optional[ActionTraceRecord] = None
metadata: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
@property
def verdict(self) -> VerdictLabel:
if self.witness is None:
return "AMBIG"
return self.witness.verdict
@property
def is_tool_failure(self) -> bool:
if self.action is None:
return False
return len(self.action.failure_notes) > 0 or self.action.action_status.lower() == "fail"
@property
def best_candidate_score(self) -> float:
if not self.candidate_routes:
return 0.0
return max(c.score for c in self.candidate_routes)
@property
def mean_contradiction_risk(self) -> float:
if not self.candidate_routes:
return 1.0
return sum(c.contradiction_risk for c in self.candidate_routes) / len(self.candidate_routes)
def to_model_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
"""
Canonical dict for trainers/collators.
"""
return {
"packet_id": self.packet_id,
"created_at": self.created_at,
"source_atlas": self.source_atlas,
"task_class": self.task_class,
"mode": self.mode,
"query": self.query,
"lens_init": self.lens_init,
"invariant_carriers": self.invariant_carriers,
"candidate_routes": [
{
"candidate_id": c.candidate_id,
"payload_ref": c.payload_ref,
"score": c.score,
"uncertainty": c.uncertainty,
"contradiction_risk": c.contradiction_risk,
"admissible": c.admissible,
"provenance": c.provenance,
}
for c in self.candidate_routes
],
"evidence": [
{
"modality": e.modality,
"summary": e.summary,
"regions_or_spans": e.regions_or_spans,
"confidence": e.confidence,
}
for e in self.evidence
],
"witness": None
if self.witness is None
else {
"verdict": self.witness.verdict,
"residual_ledger": self.witness.residual_ledger,
"tri_lock_defects": self.witness.tri_lock_defects,
"candidate_set": self.witness.candidate_set,
"evidence_plan": self.witness.evidence_plan,
"obstruction_certificate": self.witness.obstruction_certificate,
"replay_required": self.witness.replay_required,
"replay_verified": self.witness.replay_verified,
"seal": self.witness.seal,
},
"patch": None
if self.patch is None
else {
"patch_id": self.patch.patch_id,
"patch_risk": self.patch.patch_risk,
"stable_epochs": self.patch.stable_epochs,
"target_nodes": self.patch.target_nodes,
"delta_refs": self.patch.delta_refs,
"promoted": self.patch.promoted,
"held": self.patch.held,
"quarantined": self.patch.quarantined,
},
"action": None
if self.action is None
else {
"action_status": self.action.action_status,
"tool_trace_ids": self.action.tool_trace_ids,
"tool_names": self.action.tool_names,
"failure_notes": self.action.failure_notes,
},
"metadata": self.metadata,
}
class RingBuffer:
def __init__(self, capacity: int) -> None:
self.capacity = capacity
self._data: Deque[RoutePacketSample] = deque(maxlen=capacity)
def append(self, sample: RoutePacketSample) -> None:
self._data.append(sample)
def extend(self, samples: Iterable[RoutePacketSample]) -> None:
for s in samples:
self.append(s)
def __len__(self) -> int:
return len(self._data)
def as_list(self) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
return list(self._data)
def sample(self, k: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
items = self.as_list()
if not items:
return []
k = min(k, len(items))
return random.sample(items, k)
def latest(self, k: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
return self.as_list()[-k:]
class RoutePacketStore:
"""
Atomic data plane for Athenachka 2.0.
Keeps route-packets separated by downstream use:
- verified_ok for teacher-forced distillation
- ambig for bounded-candidate / evidence-plan training
- tool_failures for hard negatives and tool repair
- verifier_hard_negatives for witness sharpening
- selfplay_recent for SPIN / creator-prover loops
- hold_patches for delayed promotion review
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig) -> None:
rb = cfg.replay_buffers
self.cfg = cfg
self.recent = RingBuffer(rb.route_packets_recent)
self.verified_ok = RingBuffer(rb.route_packets_verified_ok)
self.ambig = RingBuffer(rb.route_packets_ambig)
self.tool_failures = RingBuffer(rb.tool_failures_recent)
self.verifier_hard_negatives = RingBuffer(rb.verifier_hard_negatives)
self.selfplay_recent = RingBuffer(rb.selfplay_episodes_recent)
self.patch_candidates_hold = RingBuffer(rb.patch_candidates_hold)
def ingest(self, sample: RoutePacketSample) -> None:
self.recent.append(sample)
if sample.verdict == "OK":
self.verified_ok.append(sample)
elif sample.verdict == "AMBIG":
self.ambig.append(sample)
elif sample.verdict == "FAIL":
self.verifier_hard_negatives.append(sample)
if sample.is_tool_failure:
self.tool_failures.append(sample)
if sample.patch is not None and sample.patch.held:
self.patch_candidates_hold.append(sample)
if sample.metadata.get("selfplay", False):
self.selfplay_recent.append(sample)
def ingest_many(self, samples: Iterable[RoutePacketSample]) -> None:
for sample in samples:
self.ingest(sample)
def build_teacher_forced_corpus(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
data = self.verified_ok.as_list() + self.ambig.as_list()
if limit is not None:
data = data[:limit]
return data
def build_spin_corpus(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
"""
Self-play corpus:
- recent self-play packets
- verifier hard negatives
- tool failures recycled as negatives
"""
data = (
self.selfplay_recent.as_list()
+ self.verifier_hard_negatives.as_list()
+ self.tool_failures.as_list()
)
if limit is not None:
data = data[:limit]
return data
def build_grpo_corpus(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
"""
Budget/scheduler corpus:
keep route packets with explicit token/frame/tool budget metadata.
"""
out: List[RoutePacketSample] = []
for sample in self.recent.as_list():
if "budget" in sample.query or sample.metadata.get("budget_trace") is not None:
out.append(sample)
if limit is not None:
out = out[:limit]
return out
def build_tool_negative_corpus(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
data = self.tool_failures.as_list() + self.verifier_hard_negatives.as_list()
if limit is not None:
data = data[:limit]
return data
def build_patch_review_corpus(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
data = self.patch_candidates_hold.as_list()
if limit is not None:
data = data[:limit]
return data
def summary(self) -> Dict[str, int]:
return {
"recent": len(self.recent),
"verified_ok": len(self.verified_ok),
"ambig": len(self.ambig),
"tool_failures": len(self.tool_failures),
"verifier_hard_negatives": len(self.verifier_hard_negatives),
"selfplay_recent": len(self.selfplay_recent),
"patch_candidates_hold": len(self.patch_candidates_hold),
}
class RoutePacketDataset(Dataset):
"""
Thin Dataset wrapper over a concrete packet list.
"""
def __init__(self, samples: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> None:
self.samples = list(samples)
def __len__(self) -> int:
return len(self.samples)
def __getitem__(self, idx: int) -> Dict[str, Any]:
return self.samples[idx].to_model_dict()
def _pad_2d_float(batch_values: List[List[float]], pad: float = 0.0):
max_len = max((len(v) for v in batch_values), default=0)
padded = []
mask = []
for values in batch_values:
row = values + [pad] * (max_len - len(values))
m = [1] * len(values) + [0] * (max_len - len(values))
padded.append(row)
mask.append(m)
if torch is None:
return padded, mask
return (
torch.tensor(padded, dtype=torch.float32),
torch.tensor(mask, dtype=torch.bool),
)
def collate_route_packets(batch: Sequence[Dict[str, Any]]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
"""
Collate for SFT/self-play/GRPO.
Keeps the packet object geometry visible:
- mode labels
- candidate scores / risks / uncertainties
- verdict labels
- patch risk and replay flags
"""
batch = list(batch)
candidate_scores = [[c["score"] for c in item["candidate_routes"]] for item in batch]
candidate_unc = [[c["uncertainty"] for c in item["candidate_routes"]] for item in batch]
candidate_risk = [[c["contradiction_risk"] for c in item["candidate_routes"]] for item in batch]
score_tensor, score_mask = _pad_2d_float(candidate_scores)
unc_tensor, _ = _pad_2d_float(candidate_unc)
risk_tensor, _ = _pad_2d_float(candidate_risk)
verdicts = [
"AMBIG" if item["witness"] is None else item["witness"]["verdict"]
for item in batch
]
replay_flags = [
False if item["witness"] is None else bool(item["witness"]["replay_verified"])
for item in batch
]
patch_risks = [
1.0 if item["patch"] is None else float(item["patch"]["patch_risk"])
for item in batch
]
if torch is not None:
patch_risks = torch.tensor(patch_risks, dtype=torch.float32)
replay_flags = torch.tensor(replay_flags, dtype=torch.bool)
return {
"packet_ids": [item["packet_id"] for item in batch],
"modes": [item["mode"] for item in batch],
"task_classes": [item["task_class"] for item in batch],
"queries": [item["query"] for item in batch],
"lens_init": [item["lens_init"] for item in batch],
"candidate_scores": score_tensor,
"candidate_uncertainty": unc_tensor,
"candidate_contradiction_risk": risk_tensor,
"candidate_mask": score_mask,
"verdicts": verdicts,
"replay_verified": replay_flags,
"patch_risks": patch_risks,
"raw": batch,
}
def stratified_sample_for_sft(store: RoutePacketStore, batch_size: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
"""
Mix OK and AMBIG packets for teacher-forced SFT so the model learns
both clean closure and lawful bounded ambiguity.
"""
ok_k = batch_size // 2
ambig_k = batch_size - ok_k
return store.verified_ok.sample(ok_k) + store.ambig.sample(ambig_k)
def stratified_sample_for_spin(store: RoutePacketStore, batch_size: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
"""
Mix self-play packets with hard negatives and tool failures.
"""
a = batch_size // 3
b = batch_size // 3
c = batch_size - a - b
return (
store.selfplay_recent.sample(a)
+ store.verifier_hard_negatives.sample(b)
+ store.tool_failures.sample(c)
)
def stratified_sample_for_grpo(store: RoutePacketStore, batch_size: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
"""
Prefer packets with explicit budget metadata.
"""
corpus = store.build_grpo_corpus()
if not corpus:
return []
k = min(batch_size, len(corpus))
return random.sample(corpus, k)
def stratified_sample_for_patch_board(store: RoutePacketStore, batch_size: int) -> List[RoutePacketSample]:
return store.patch_candidates_hold.sample(batch_size)
optimizer_groups.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from typing import Dict, Iterable, List, Literal, Optional, Sequence, Tuple
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from config_schema import TrainConfig
Phase = Literal["sft", "spin_selfplay", "grpo_scheduler"]
@dataclass
class GroupPatterns:

planner_route_head: Tuple[str, ...] = (

verifier_truth_head: Tuple[str, ...] = (
"verifier",

"defect_head",
)
mode_token_head: Tuple[str, ...] = (
"mode_head",
