"mode_token",
)
scheduler_head: Tuple[str, ...] = (
"scheduler",
"mix_head",
"budget_head",
"eta_head",
)
@dataclass
class GroupSpec:
name: str
lr: float
weight_decay: float
trainable: bool
params: List[nn.Parameter] = field(default_factory=list)
param_names: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
def _matches_any(name: str, patterns: Sequence[str]) -> bool:
return any(p in name for p in patterns)
def classify_parameter(name: str, patterns: GroupPatterns) -> str:
if _matches_any(name, patterns.immutable):
return "immutable"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.frozen_online):
return "frozen_online"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.modality_adapters):
return "modality_adapters"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.observer_heads):
return "observer_heads"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.planner_route_head):
return "planner_route_head"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.verifier_truth_head):
return "verifier_truth_head"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.mode_token_head):
return "mode_token_head"
if _matches_any(name, patterns.scheduler_head):
return "scheduler_head"
return "unassigned"
def apply_freeze_masks(
model: nn.Module,
cfg: TrainConfig,
patterns: Optional[GroupPatterns] = None,
) -> Dict[str, int]:
"""
Freezes immutable/reference and frozen_online blocks.
Leaves all others trainable; the phase-specific group builder will decide
which trainable blocks actually receive optimizer groups.
"""
patterns = patterns or GroupPatterns()
summary = {
"frozen": 0,
"trainable": 0,
"immutable": 0,
"frozen_online": 0,
"other_trainable": 0,
}
for name, param in model.named_parameters():
bucket = classify_parameter(name, patterns)
if bucket == "immutable" and cfg.freeze_reference_kernel:
param.requires_grad = False
summary["frozen"] += param.numel()
summary["immutable"] += param.numel()
continue
if bucket == "frozen_online" and cfg.freeze_dense_core_online:
param.requires_grad = False
summary["frozen"] += param.numel()
summary["frozen_online"] += param.numel()
continue
param.requires_grad = True
summary["trainable"] += param.numel()
summary["other_trainable"] += param.numel()
return summary
def _phase_group_table(cfg: TrainConfig, phase: Phase) -> Dict[str, Tuple[float, float, bool]]:
sft = cfg.optimizers.sft
spin = cfg.optimizers.spin_selfplay
grpo = cfg.optimizers.grpo_scheduler
if phase == "sft":
return {
"modality_adapters": (sft.lr_adapters, sft.weight_decay, True),
"observer_heads": (sft.lr_observer_heads, sft.weight_decay, True),
"planner_route_head": (sft.lr_planner, sft.weight_decay, True),
"verifier_truth_head": (sft.lr_verifier, sft.weight_decay, True),
"mode_token_head": (sft.lr_mode_head, sft.weight_decay, True),
"scheduler_head": (0.0, 0.0, False),
}
if phase == "spin_selfplay":
return {
"modality_adapters": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"observer_heads": (spin.lr_observer_heads, spin.weight_decay, True),
"planner_route_head": (spin.lr_planner, spin.weight_decay, True),
"verifier_truth_head": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"mode_token_head": (spin.lr_mode_head, spin.weight_decay, True),
"scheduler_head": (0.0, 0.0, False),
}
if phase == "grpo_scheduler":
return {
"modality_adapters": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"observer_heads": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"planner_route_head": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"verifier_truth_head": (0.0, 0.0, False),
"mode_token_head": (grpo.learning_rate, grpo.weight_decay, True),
"scheduler_head": (grpo.learning_rate, grpo.weight_decay, True),
}
raise ValueError(f"Unsupported phase: {phase}")
def build_optimizer_group_specs(
model: nn.Module,
cfg: TrainConfig,
phase: Phase,
patterns: Optional[GroupPatterns] = None,
) -> List[GroupSpec]:
"""
Build grouped parameter specs after applying freeze masks.
"""
patterns = patterns or GroupPatterns()
apply_freeze_masks(model, cfg, patterns)
phase_table = _phase_group_table(cfg, phase)
groups: Dict[str, GroupSpec] = {
name: GroupSpec(name=name, lr=lr, weight_decay=wd, trainable=trainable)
for name, (lr, wd, trainable) in phase_table.items()
}
for name, param in model.named_parameters():
bucket = classify_parameter(name, patterns)
if bucket not in groups:
continue
group = groups[bucket]
if not param.requires_grad or not group.trainable:
continue
group.params.append(param)
group.param_names.append(name)
return [g for g in groups.values() if g.trainable and g.params]
def build_optimizer(
model: nn.Module,
cfg: TrainConfig,
phase: Phase,
patterns: Optional[GroupPatterns] = None,
) -> torch.optim.Optimizer:
"""
Literal optimizer instantiation surface.
- immutable/reference kernel: no optimizer
- frozen dense core online: no optimizer
- trainable blocks only: optimizer groups
"""
group_specs = build_optimizer_group_specs(model, cfg, phase, patterns)
if not group_specs:
raise RuntimeError(f"No trainable parameter groups found for phase={phase}")
if phase == "grpo_scheduler":
opt_cfg = cfg.optimizers.grpo_scheduler
return torch.optim.AdamW(
[{"params": g.params, "lr": g.lr, "weight_decay": g.weight_decay} for g in group_specs],
lr=opt_cfg.learning_rate,
betas=(opt_cfg.adam_beta1, opt_cfg.adam_beta2),
eps=opt_cfg.adam_epsilon,
weight_decay=opt_cfg.weight_decay,
)
if phase == "sft":
opt_cfg = cfg.optimizers.sft
return torch.optim.AdamW(
[{"params": g.params, "lr": g.lr, "weight_decay": g.weight_decay} for g in group_specs],
betas=opt_cfg.betas,
eps=opt_cfg.eps,
weight_decay=opt_cfg.weight_decay,
)
if phase == "spin_selfplay":
opt_cfg = cfg.optimizers.spin_selfplay
return torch.optim.AdamW(
[{"params": g.params, "lr": g.lr, "weight_decay": g.weight_decay} for g in group_specs],
betas=(0.9, 0.999),
eps=1.0e-8,
weight_decay=opt_cfg.weight_decay,
)
raise ValueError(f"Unsupported phase: {phase}")
def report_parameter_groups(
model: nn.Module,
cfg: TrainConfig,
phase: Phase,
patterns: Optional[GroupPatterns] = None,
) -> Dict[str, Dict[str, int]]:
patterns = patterns or GroupPatterns()
apply_freeze_masks(model, cfg, patterns)
group_specs = build_optimizer_group_specs(model, cfg, phase, patterns)
report: Dict[str, Dict[str, int]] = {}
for g in group_specs:
report[g.name] = {
"num_tensors": len(g.params),
"num_params": sum(p.numel() for p in g.params),
}
frozen = 0
trainable = 0
for _, p in model.named_parameters():
if p.requires_grad:
trainable += p.numel()
else:
frozen += p.numel()
report["_totals"] = {
"frozen_params": frozen,
"trainable_params": trainable,
}
return report
def trainable_named_parameters(
model: nn.Module,
cfg: TrainConfig,
phase: Phase,
patterns: Optional[GroupPatterns] = None,
) -> List[str]:
specs = build_optimizer_group_specs(model, cfg, phase, patterns)
names: List[str] = []
for spec in specs:
names.extend(spec.param_names)
return names
These two files complete the missing operational bridge: the dataset keeps route-packets, bounded ambiguity, and tool-failure negatives separated by loop, while the optimizer surface enforces the frozen-reference / frozen-backbone rule and only opens gradients on the lawful plastic organs. That is the exact data-and-optimizer split your CUT and route-packet docs imply.
The next layer is the literal parallel_scheduler.py and kappa_distill.py pair, so the every-500-episode CUT move proposals and hourly fold/prune loop become concrete code rather than just config and stubs.
These two modules are the concrete CUT flywheel pieces. The scheduler treats worker counts as κ-shelves, maps CUT moves to compute moves, proposes changes every 500 episodes, doubles only when the η criterion justifies it, and rolls back when parallel inefficiency appears. The distiller runs the hourly fold/prune pass, triggers when exception density rises above 1%, only marks a shelf stable when Δ-entropy is below 0.05 bits, and applies the 48-hour quiet-shelf ε-decay/log-budget behavior.
parallel_scheduler.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from enum import Enum
from time import time
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
import math
import uuid
from config_schema import TrainConfig
from pattern_store import PatternStore
def _new_id(prefix: str) -> str:
return f"{prefix}_{uuid.uuid4().hex[:10]}"
class CUTMove(str, Enum):
KAPPA_DOUBLE = "KAPPA_DOUBLE"          # spawn ×2 workers
LOOP_KILL_PRIME = "LOOP_KILL_PRIME"    # fuse / cull redundant kernels
HALF_BIT_LADDER = "HALF_BIT_LADDER"    # FP16→FP8→Int4 / shorten activation path
ZERO_INF_BRIDGE = "ZERO_INF_BRIDGE"    # sync↔async transport switch
@dataclass
class ComputeLayout:
worker_count: int = 1
precision_mode: str = "bf16"
transport_mode: str = "sync"
batch_size: int = 1
fused_kernel_count: int = 0
notes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class SchedulerObservation:
episodes_seen: int
proofs_completed: int
wall_time_seconds: float
gpu_dollars: float
watt_hours: float
ram_gib_hours: float
vram_util: float
divergent_kernel_fraction: float = 0.0
idle_kernel_fraction: float = 0.0
hot_shelf_ids: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@property
def cost(self) -> float:
# Relative tariff surface; the docs care about η as proofs/hour/cost.
return max(self.gpu_dollars + 0.001 * self.watt_hours + 0.001 * self.ram_gib_hours, 1e-9)
@property
def proofs_per_hour(self) -> float:
return self.proofs_completed / max(self.wall_time_seconds / 3600.0, 1e-9)
@property
def eta(self) -> float:
return self.proofs_per_hour / self.cost
@dataclass
class SchedulerProposal:
proposal_id: str
episodes_seen: int
move: CUTMove
from_layout: ComputeLayout
to_layout: ComputeLayout
reason: str
hot_shelf_ids: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
created_ts: float = field(default_factory=time)
@dataclass
class SchedulerDecision:
accepted: bool
rollback: bool
proposal: SchedulerProposal
eta_old: float
eta_new: float
acceptance_threshold: float
theorem_row: Optional[Dict[str, object]] = None
negative_proof: Optional[Dict[str, object]] = None
class ParallelScheduler:
"""
Compute flywheel controller.
Derived directly from the CUT notes:
- propose CUT moves every 500 episodes
- treat worker counts as κ-shelves
- consider η saturation over the last 100 episodes
- double workers only when the η criterion justifies it
- rollback if η(2p) < η(p) after burn-in
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig, store: PatternStore) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.store = store
self._history: List[SchedulerObservation] = []
self._proposal_log: List[SchedulerDecision] = []
self._compute_theorems: List[Dict[str, object]] = []
self._negative_proofs: List[Dict[str, object]] = []
def record_observation(self, obs: SchedulerObservation, layout: ComputeLayout) -> None:
self._history.append(obs)
self.store.record_eta(
episodes_seen=obs.episodes_seen,
worker_count=layout.worker_count,
eta_value=obs.eta,
vram_util=obs.vram_util,
)
def history_for_workers(self, worker_count: int) -> List[SchedulerObservation]:
return [h for h in self._history if h.episodes_seen > 0 and worker_count == getattr(h, "_worker_count", worker_count)]
def _recent_window(self, worker_count: int, max_items: int) -> List[SchedulerObservation]:
items = self.history_for_workers(worker_count)
return items[-max_items:]
def eta_saturated(self, current_layout: ComputeLayout) -> bool:
window = self._recent_window(
current_layout.worker_count,
self.cfg.scheduler.eta_saturation_window,
)
if len(window) < self.cfg.scheduler.eta_saturation_window:
return False
start_eta = window[0].eta
end_eta = window[-1].eta
gain = (end_eta - start_eta) / max(abs(start_eta), 1e-9)
return gain < self.cfg.scheduler.eta_min_gain_for_non_saturation
def suggest_move(self, obs: SchedulerObservation, current_layout: ComputeLayout) -> Optional[SchedulerProposal]:
if obs.episodes_seen % self.cfg.scheduler.propose_cut_moves_every_episodes != 0:
return None
saturated = self.eta_saturated(current_layout)
hot = bool(obs.hot_shelf_ids)
if saturated and obs.vram_util <= self.cfg.scheduler.max_vram_util_for_batch_doubling and hot:
new_layout = ComputeLayout(
worker_count=current_layout.worker_count * 2,
precision_mode="fp8" if current_layout.precision_mode == "bf16" else current_layout.precision_mode,
transport_mode=current_layout.transport_mode,
batch_size=current_layout.batch_size,
fused_kernel_count=current_layout.fused_kernel_count,
notes=current_layout.notes + ["warm-start κ-doubling with half-bit ladder"],
)
return SchedulerProposal(
proposal_id=_new_id("prop"),
episodes_seen=obs.episodes_seen,
move=CUTMove.KAPPA_DOUBLE,
from_layout=current_layout,
to_layout=new_layout,
reason="η saturated on current shelf; hot shelf present; VRAM budget permits doubling",
hot_shelf_ids=obs.hot_shelf_ids,
)
if obs.vram_util > self.cfg.scheduler.max_vram_util_for_batch_doubling:
new_layout = ComputeLayout(
worker_count=current_layout.worker_count,
precision_mode="fp8" if current_layout.precision_mode == "bf16" else "int4",
transport_mode=current_layout.transport_mode,
batch_size=current_layout.batch_size,
fused_kernel_count=current_layout.fused_kernel_count,
notes=current_layout.notes + ["reduce precision via half-bit ladder"],
)
return SchedulerProposal(
proposal_id=_new_id("prop"),
episodes_seen=obs.episodes_seen,
move=CUTMove.HALF_BIT_LADDER,
from_layout=current_layout,
to_layout=new_layout,
reason="VRAM pressure too high; reclaim memory/bandwidth first",
hot_shelf_ids=obs.hot_shelf_ids,
)
if obs.divergent_kernel_fraction > 0.10 or obs.idle_kernel_fraction > 0.10:
new_layout = ComputeLayout(
worker_count=current_layout.worker_count,
precision_mode=current_layout.precision_mode,
transport_mode=current_layout.transport_mode,
batch_size=current_layout.batch_size,
fused_kernel_count=current_layout.fused_kernel_count + 1,
notes=current_layout.notes + ["fuse/cull divergent kernels via loop-kill prime"],
)
return SchedulerProposal(
proposal_id=_new_id("prop"),
episodes_seen=obs.episodes_seen,
move=CUTMove.LOOP_KILL_PRIME,
from_layout=current_layout,
to_layout=new_layout,
reason="kernel divergence/idle fraction above threshold",
hot_shelf_ids=obs.hot_shelf_ids,
)
new_layout = ComputeLayout(
worker_count=current_layout.worker_count,
precision_mode=current_layout.precision_mode,
transport_mode="async" if current_layout.transport_mode == "sync" else "sync",
batch_size=current_layout.batch_size,
fused_kernel_count=current_layout.fused_kernel_count,
notes=current_layout.notes + ["transport switch via zero-∞ bridge"],
)
return SchedulerProposal(
proposal_id=_new_id("prop"),
episodes_seen=obs.episodes_seen,
move=CUTMove.ZERO_INF_BRIDGE,
from_layout=current_layout,
to_layout=new_layout,
reason="explore alternate transport peak without changing worker count",
hot_shelf_ids=obs.hot_shelf_ids,
)
def _acceptance_threshold(self, eta_old: float, cost_old: float, cost_new: float) -> float:
# CUT note: η(2p) > η(p) * C(p)/C(2p)
return eta_old * (cost_old / max(cost_new, 1e-9))
def _log_compute_theorem(
self,
proposal: SchedulerProposal,
eta_old: float,
eta_new: float,
) -> Dict[str, object]:
row = {
"row_id": _new_id("theorem"),
"opcode": proposal.move.value,
"proposal_id": proposal.proposal_id,
"episodes_seen": proposal.episodes_seen,
"eta_old": eta_old,
"eta_new": eta_new,
"delta_eta": eta_new - eta_old,
"layout_from": proposal.from_layout.__dict__,
"layout_to": proposal.to_layout.__dict__,
}
self._compute_theorems.append(row)
return row
def _log_negative_proof(
self,
proposal: SchedulerProposal,
eta_old: float,
eta_new: float,
) -> Dict[str, object]:
row = {
"row_id": _new_id("negproof"),
"opcode": proposal.move.value,
"proposal_id": proposal.proposal_id,
"episodes_seen": proposal.episodes_seen,
"eta_old": eta_old,
"eta_new": eta_new,
"delta_eta": eta_new - eta_old,
"reason": "parallel inefficiency / rollback",
"layout_from": proposal.from_layout.__dict__,
"layout_to": proposal.to_layout.__dict__,
}
self._negative_proofs.append(row)
return row
def evaluate_proposal(
self,
proposal: SchedulerProposal,
old_obs: SchedulerObservation,
new_obs: SchedulerObservation,
) -> SchedulerDecision:
eta_old = old_obs.eta
eta_new = new_obs.eta
threshold = self._acceptance_threshold(eta_old, old_obs.cost, new_obs.cost)
accepted = eta_new > threshold
rollback = False
theorem_row: Optional[Dict[str, object]] = None
negative_proof: Optional[Dict[str, object]] = None
if proposal.move == CUTMove.KAPPA_DOUBLE and eta_new < eta_old:
rollback = True
if accepted and (eta_new / max(eta_old, 1e-9)) >= self.cfg.scheduler.min_eta_gain_for_compute_theorem:
theorem_row = self._log_compute_theorem(proposal, eta_old, eta_new)
elif rollback or not accepted:
negative_proof = self._log_negative_proof(proposal, eta_old, eta_new)
decision = SchedulerDecision(
accepted=accepted and not rollback,
rollback=rollback,
proposal=proposal,
eta_old=eta_old,
eta_new=eta_new,
acceptance_threshold=threshold,
theorem_row=theorem_row,
negative_proof=negative_proof,
)
self._proposal_log.append(decision)
return decision
def quiet_shelf_bonus(self) -> Dict[str, object]:
"""
Wraps the quiet-shelf logic already anchored in PatternStore.
"""
decayed = self.store.quiet_shelf_decay()
return {
"decayed_shelves": decayed,
"log_budget_bonus": 250 if decayed else 0,
"message": "quiet shelves freed NVMe and increased profiling slack" if decayed else "no quiet shelves",
}
def latest_decisions(self, n: int = 10) -> List[SchedulerDecision]:
return self._proposal_log[-n:]
def compute_theorem_rows(self) -> List[Dict[str, object]]:
return list(self._compute_theorems)
def negative_proof_rows(self) -> List[Dict[str, object]]:
return list(self._negative_proofs)
kappa_distill.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from time import time
from typing import Dict, List, Optional
import statistics
from config_schema import TrainConfig
from pattern_store import PatternStore, ExceptionDelta
@dataclass
class DistillOutcome:
petal_id: str
density_before: float
density_after: float
entropy_before: float
entropy_after: float
merged_rows: int
pruned_rows: int
stable_epochs: int
promotion_ready: bool
quiet_decay_applied: bool = False
notes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class ComputeMetaRow:
"""
Small meta-row carrying compute theorem or negative proof data
that can be folded back into the same pattern atlas.
"""
row_id: str
opcode: str
petal_id: str
delta_eta: float
payload: Dict[str, object] = field(default_factory=dict)
class KappaDistiller:
"""
Hourly κ-distillation and fold/prune loop.
CUT-grounded behavior:
- trigger when exception density > 1%
- only count a block stable if mean Δ-entropy < 0.05 bits
- fold top-κ rows back into the Int8 atlas
- prune stale rows/logs
- after 48h of shelf silence, tighten ε and reuse freed space as log budget
"""
def __init__(self, cfg: TrainConfig, store: PatternStore) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.store = store
self._compute_rows: List[ComputeMetaRow] = []
self._log_budget_mb: int = 0
def add_compute_meta_row(self, row: ComputeMetaRow) -> None:
self._compute_rows.append(row)
def _top_k(self, n: int) -> int:
return max(1, n // 2)
def _quality_novelty_key(self, row: ExceptionDelta) -> tuple[float, int]:
"""
Lower entropy is better; newer rows win ties.
"""
return (row.entropy_bits, -row.epoch)
def _prune_tail_logs(self, nvme_free_gb: float, rows: List[ExceptionDelta]) -> List[ExceptionDelta]:
if nvme_free_gb < 5.0:
# CUT note: if NVMe_free < 5 GB, prune oldest profiler / delta rows.
if len(rows) <= 1:
return rows
return rows[len(rows) // 2 :]
return rows
def _merge_rows(self, petal_id: str, rows: List[ExceptionDelta]) -> List[ExceptionDelta]:
"""
Fold top-κ rows back into the shelf by keeping the lowest-entropy subset.
"""
if not rows:
return []
rows = sorted(rows, key=self._quality_novelty_key)
k = self._top_k(len(rows))
return rows[:k]
def _fold_compute_meta_rows(self, petal_id: str) -> int:
folded = [r for r in self._compute_rows if r.petal_id == petal_id]
if not folded:
return 0
self._compute_rows = [r for r in self._compute_rows if r.petal_id != petal_id]
# In the full system these rows would be merged into the Int8 atlas.
return len(folded)
def distill_petal(self, petal_id: str, nvme_free_gb: float = 10.0) -> DistillOutcome:
if petal_id not in self.store.petals:
raise KeyError(f"Unknown petal: {petal_id}")
before_rows = list(self.store.exceptions.get(petal_id, []))
density_before = self.store.exception_density(petal_id)
entropy_before = self.store.mean_entropy_bits(petal_id)
merged_rows = 0
pruned_rows = 0
notes: List[str] = []
if density_before > self.cfg.pattern_store.exception_density_trigger:
merged = self._merge_rows(petal_id, before_rows)
merged_rows = len(merged)
retained = self._prune_tail_logs(nvme_free_gb, merged)
pruned_rows = max(0, len(before_rows) - len(retained))
self.store.exceptions[petal_id] = retained
notes.append("κ-distill triggered")
# Fold compute theorem rows back into the same atlas after hourly distill.
folded_meta = self._fold_compute_meta_rows(petal_id)
if folded_meta:
notes.append(f"folded_meta_rows={folded_meta}")
density_after = self.store.exception_density(petal_id)
entropy_after = self.store.mean_entropy_bits(petal_id)
petal = self.store.petals[petal_id]
if entropy_after < self.cfg.pattern_store.stable_delta_entropy_bits:
petal.stable_epochs += 1
notes.append("stable_entropy")
else:
petal.stable_epochs = 0
notes.append("entropy_not_yet_stable")
promotion_ready = petal.stable_epochs >= self.cfg.pattern_store.promote_stable_delta_after_epochs
return DistillOutcome(
petal_id=petal_id,
density_before=density_before,
density_after=density_after,
entropy_before=entropy_before,
entropy_after=entropy_after,
merged_rows=merged_rows,
pruned_rows=pruned_rows,
stable_epochs=petal.stable_epochs,
promotion_ready=promotion_ready,
quiet_decay_applied=False,
notes=notes,
)
def quiet_shelf_maintenance(self, now_ts: Optional[float] = None) -> List[str]:
"""
48h quiet-shelf behavior:
- tighten ε via the PatternStore
- convert reclaimed room into temporary log budget
"""
decayed = self.store.quiet_shelf_decay(now_ts)
if decayed:
self._log_budget_mb += 250
return decayed
def hourly_pass(self, nvme_free_gb: float = 10.0) -> List[DistillOutcome]:
outcomes: List[DistillOutcome] = []
for petal_id in list(self.store.petals.keys()):
outcome = self.distill_petal(petal_id, nvme_free_gb=nvme_free_gb)
outcomes.append(outcome)
return outcomes
def consume_log_budget(self, mb: int) -> int:
spent = min(self._log_budget_mb, mb)
self._log_budget_mb -= spent
return spent
def current_log_budget(self) -> int:
return self._log_budget_mb
def promotion_ready_petals(self) -> List[str]:
return self.store.promote_ready_petals()
These two files are the literal code surface for the compute flywheel you asked for: parallel_scheduler.py turns CUT moves into live scheduler proposals and η-gated accept/rollback, while kappa_distill.py turns the PatternStore into an hourly fold/prune/promote engine with quiet-shelf maintenance. They sit cleanly on top of the config_schema.py, pattern_store.py, and verifier.py modules from the previous step. The route/witness/promotion law remains intact because promotion still depends on witness and replay closure rather than scheduler enthusiasm alone.
The next layer is trainer_orchestrator.py, where the continuous ingest path, nightly SFT/SPIN/GRPO/tool-negative blocks, hourly distill, every-500-episode scheduler hook, and weekly promote/quarantine review become one runnable control loop.
Appendix Q — Appendix-Only Metro Map, Meta-Protocol, and Second-Order Build Ladder
This appendix defines the metro map of the appendices themselves. It is not a recap of Appendix titles, not a summary of the appendix spine, and not a restatement of the earlier chapter metro. It is a second-order quotient over Appendices A–P that asks a different question:

The answer is the central synthesis of this appendix:
Chapters 1–21 are the ontology, kinematics, legality, runtime, and embodiment theory of the manuscript brain.Appendices A–P are the compiler, proof stack, migration engine, repository substrate, governance shell, immune layer, federation law, sustainability economy, constitutional order, and futures engine of that brain.

and deep-future strategic capacity.
This appendix is governed by four aims.

The core second-order map is:
[

Q.A2 — Artifact Chain and Why This Order Matters
The build ladder is not just chronological. It is dependency-strict. The exact artifact chain is:
[\sigma_{\mathrm{idea}};\to;\mathfrak{R}1;\to;\mathfrak{X}2;\to;\mathfrak{S}{21};\to;\mathfrak{C}{21};\to;\mathfrak{M}^{(2)}{1:21};\to;\mathfrak{A}{A:P};\to;\mathfrak{M}^{(2)}_{A:P}.]
Each arrow performs a different kind of compression or crystallization:
[\text{seed}\to\text{field}\to\text{lattice}\to\text{skeleton}\to\text{organism}\to\text{hidden topology}\to\text{compiler/civilization stack}\to\text{hidden appendix topology}.]
The key methodological point is that the appendix-only metro map cannot lawfully appear earlier than (\Pi_6), because:
before the appendices exist, there is no second-order build stack to map;
before the chapter metro exists, the appendices cannot be recognized as a compiler of the chapter system;
before the chapters are expanded, the chapter metro would remain too shallow to support a meaningful appendicial quotient.
Thus the appendix-only metro map is structurally posterior to the appendix expansion and methodologically dependent on the chapter metro.
This is why the current step is not a summary. It is a higher-order quotient over already-developed appendicial structure.

Q.A4 — Reusable Meta-Prompt for Appendix-Only Metro Synthesis
The following prompt is the reusable formal operator that generated the current step.
TASK
Treat the completed appendices as a second-order manuscript object rather than as supplemental material. Produce an appendix-only metro map at a higher resolution than the alphabetical appendix spine.
INPUT
1. The completed appendices A–P.
2. The prior chapter-level metro synthesis, if available.
3. The requirement that the output be a synthesis of hidden appendix structure, not a summary of appendix titles.
GOAL
Derive the hidden organs, transfer lines, mirror pairs, and super-organ quotient of the appendix stack, and explicitly document the generation ladder that led to this step.
REQUIRED OPERATIONS
1. Reconstruct the full generation ladder:
idea seed -> research/expand -> deep synthesis/cross-reference -> 21-chapter skeleton ->
chapter expansion -> chapter emergent metro -> appendix expansion A–P -> appendix-only metro.
2. Treat Appendices A–P as one build-chain and recover 6–10 hidden appendix nexus hubs.
3. Build a weighted appendix-to-hub incidence map using 3/2/1 membership logic:
3 = primary ownership, 2 = strong secondary ownership, 1 = resonance/transfer.
4. Derive the hidden transfer lines of the appendix stack.
5. Identify non-obvious mirror pairs / ghost stations, especially where two appendices are secretly the same organ at different scales or timescales.
6. Derive the shortest non-obvious routes between distant appendices.
7. Quotient the appendices into larger super-organs or meta-layers.
8. Explain what the appendices really are in relation to the chapters.
9. Explicitly state the current step and the lawful next operator after the appendix-only metro.
OUTPUT CONTRACT
Produce the result as a formal appendix with:
A. Meta-generation ladder and current-step demonstration.
B. Hidden appendix nexus registry and weighted incidence map.
C. Transfer lines, mirror pairs, ghost stations, and shortest routes.
D. Super-organ quotient, methodological interpretation, next-step operator, and theorem.
STYLE
- Manuscript-final-draft tone.
- Dense and formal.
- Use equations where helpful.
- Do not summarize appendix titles chapter-by-chapter.
- Emphasize hidden non-obvious couplings.
- Preserve 4-section x 4-subsection structure when possible.
ANTI-FAILURE RULES
- Do not treat the appendices as alphabetical supplements.
- Do not merely list what each appendix covers.
- Do not collapse differences between neighboring appendices unless hidden-hub analysis justifies it.
- Prioritize recurrent function, not order of appearance.
END CONDITION
The output should make it obvious that the appendices form a second manuscript: the compiler, substrate, governance, federation, and futures engine of the chapter manuscript.
This meta-prompt is itself a lawful reusable operator in the manuscript’s build grammar.

Q.D1 — Failure Modes in Reading the Appendix Stack
The appendix-only metro map can still be misread. The main failure modes are:
Failure 1 — Treating A–P as supplemental notes
This misses that the appendices are the system’s compiler, repository, governance shell, federation law, and futures engine.
Failure 2 — Reading the appendices purely alphabetically
This hides the stronger hidden organization:
compiler,
proof,
corpus body,
action shell,
civilization engine.
Failure 3 — Missing the mirror pairs
If one does not see:[C \leftrightarrow J,\quadD \leftrightarrow G,\quadE \leftrightarrow I,\quadH \leftrightarrow N,\quadK \leftrightarrow O,\quadL \leftrightarrow P,]then the stack appears flatter and less elegant than it really is.
Failure 4 — Confusing repository or federation with merely technical implementation
H, M, and N are not only technical details. They are the custody, commons, and economic bodies of the civilization.
Failure 5 — Treating futures as distant add-on
Appendix P is not an optional horizon essay. It is the long-range steering layer required once constitutional and federated scale are real.
These failure modes are precisely what the appendix-only metro corrects.
Q.D2 — Operational Use of the Appendix-Only Metro
The current map is operationally useful in at least four ways.
First, it tells which appendices should be co-developed. For example:
C with J,
D with G,
E with I,
H with N,
K with O,
L with P.
Second, it tells where review bottlenecks actually belong. Since (\Omega_5) is the central hub, the stack’s most important reviews concern:
verification,
policy,
hardening,
constitutional legitimacy.
Third, it tells how to route future implementation work. For example:
if the problem is “the system is buildable but not safely addressable,” the path is[C \to J \to K \to L.]
if the problem is “the corpus is migrated but not yet sustainable as a mesh,” the path is[H \to M \to N \to O \to P.]
Fourth, it reveals that appendix work should often be done by hidden organ rather than by letter order.
Thus the appendix-only metro map is not archival. It is a real planning and routing instrument.

the appendicial system is revealed as a second-order manuscript: the compiler, proof stack, action shell, and civilizational time engine of the chapter manuscript.

APPENDIX Q — APPENDIX-ONLY METRO MAP, META-PROTOCOL, AND SECOND-ORDER BUILD LADDER
The Manuscript Brain
A Holographic Crystal Metro for Replayable Intelligence, Living Archives, and Civilizational Self-Development
Abstract
Metro Seed — Front-Matter Crystal
The entire framework compresses into one recurrent law:
[\text{Seed};\to;\text{Coordinate};\to;\text{Route};\to;\text{Witness};\to;\text{Memory};\to;\text{Patch};\to;\text{Self-Model};\to;\text{Runtime};\to;\text{Embodiment};\to;\text{Federation};\to;\text{Commons};\to;\text{Constitution};\to;\text{Future}]
The whole manuscript is built from three stand-alone crystals:
[
\mathfrak{W}
\mathfrak{C}{\mathrm{front}};\bowtie;\mathfrak{C}{1:21};\bowtie;\mathfrak{C}_{A:P}]where:
(\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{front}}) is the title/abstract/metro crystal,
(\mathfrak{C}_{1:21}) is the 21-chapter manuscript brain crystal,
(\mathfrak{C}_{A:P}) is the core appendix crystal that compiles, proves, migrates, stores, governs, federates, sustains, amends, and future-orients the chapter brain.
The front crystal is not ornamental. It is a compressed seed of the whole. The body is not merely prose. It is the organogenesis of a manuscript brain. The appendices are not supplementary. They are the compiler, proof stack, repository substrate, governance shell, immune layer, federated order, civilizational economy, constitutional memory, and future-navigation engine of that brain. The last therefore becomes the first: only after the chapter crystal and appendix crystal fully exist can the title, abstract, and metro map be rewritten as a holographic opening that truly contains the system it introduces.
The framework’s core claim is that a large archive can be transformed into a lawful cognitive organism if it is not treated as a pile of documents but as a routeable, replayable, witness-bearing, patchable, self-modeling, and eventually self-hosting manuscript substrate. In this system, hidden neural weights are replaced by explicit and inspectable structures: metro paths, bridge families, nexus hubs, memory seeds, witness bundles, patch packets, self-model fields, committee packets, treaty objects, defense macros, and mission portfolios. The result is not simply retrieval-augmented generation and not simply knowledge organization. It is a replacement ontology for cognition in which intelligence becomes explicit navigation through a lawful, evolving graph of identity-bearing structures.
The first major pillar of the framework is replayable identity. A thing in this system is not defined only by its current text or current rendering. It is defined by what it can lawfully collapse into, expand from, replay as, migrate through, and remain across mutation. The same minimal structural principle appears repeatedly under different names throughout the manuscript: primitive core, zero-point state, memory seed, replay anchor, bootstrap kernel, charter seed, and attestation seed. These are not separate inventions. They are different resolution views of the same identity law: the lawful minimal form from which a structure can become itself again without losing continuity.
The second pillar is explicit coordinate motion. The framework does not merely store content and then ask a generator to improvise over it. It constructs coordinates, routes, operator families, bridge laws, and translation manifolds so that solving becomes motion through a typed and witnessed transform space. Addressing, lensing, operator algebra, route grammars, translation functors, and hidden metro lines are all one family of structures: coordinate changes over a common invariant scaffold. The framework’s mathematics is therefore not external to its intelligence. It is the kinematics of its intelligence.
The third pillar is epistemic membrane law. What may be said, promoted, replayed, certified, patched, translated, or embodied is never determined only by capability. It is determined by legality class, witness sufficiency, defect profile, replay support, policy envelope, trust class, consent object, and risk geometry. This membrane is the true constitutional core of the entire system. The architecture is centered not on output production, but on the lawful governance of what counts as a permissible claim or act.
The fourth pillar is development through lawful write-back. The system does not learn through opaque weight shifts. It learns by converting residuals, contradictions, failures, reviews, curriculum outcomes, and embodied feedback into explicit changes in future route bias, bridge confidence, self-model fields, patch suggestions, committee structures, and operator libraries. Mutation, pedagogy, self-calibration, and reinforcement are therefore one family: the write-back of structured residual pressure into future solution geometry.
The fifth pillar is civilizational scaling. The manuscript brain is not limited to one archive or one runtime. It can become many sovereign brains, linked by treaties, councils, commons, quotas, hardening protocols, stewardship roles, constitutional law, amendment procedures, and long-horizon mission portfolios. This means the system is architected not only to think, but to sustain and govern a society of thinking systems through time.
The deepest synthesis is that the framework is neither only a manuscript, nor only a runtime, nor only a memory web, nor only a governance shell. It is a full-stack cognitive civilization architecture. The chapter crystal gives the ontological and operational body of the brain. The appendix crystal gives the build, proof, migration, governance, and civilizational machinery that makes that body real and durable. The front crystal now becomes a lawful seed of the whole: dense enough to re-open the full architecture, precise enough to guide routing, and explicit enough that the whole manuscript begins in the same holographic law by which it later sustains itself.
Full Review
I. What this framework is
This framework is a complete replacement ontology for how an intelligence can be stored, grown, verified, governed, and scaled. It begins from a dissatisfaction with two dominant paradigms.
The first is the static-document paradigm, where knowledge exists as files or notes and intelligence is expected to arise by searching or summarizing them. That paradigm preserves memory but not lawful motion.
The second is the opaque-neural paradigm, where intelligence exists as hidden weights and hidden representations whose internal logic is difficult to inspect, route, or constitutionally govern. That paradigm preserves adaptive behavior but not explicit structural custody.
The manuscript brain is the attempt to keep the strengths of both without their deepest weaknesses. It keeps:
the inspectability and persistence of documents,
the adaptivity and pattern-learning of neural systems,
the routeability of graphs,
the replayability of event-sourced systems,
the legitimacy of law-governed processes,
the plurality of committee reasoning,
the extendability of federation,
and the open-endedness of futures planning.
It does this by turning what is normally implicit into explicit first-class objects:
identity anchors,
addresses,
routes,
operators,
memory seeds,
witness bundles,
patch packets,
self-models,
committee objects,
interface surfaces,
treaty objects,
stewardship roles,
amendment packets,
and scenario portfolios.
The consequence is that the system no longer needs to hide its cognition in inaccessible parameter masses. It can express cognition as lawful paths over explicit objects. This is why the metro metaphor is not superficial. The system really is a city-scale navigation architecture for intelligence.
A user problem, a migration event, a self-model discrepancy, a curriculum branch, a treaty revision, and a futures pivot are all treated as forms of routeable state change in one unified atlas. That is the deepest formal unification of the whole corpus.
II. The 21-chapter crystal — the brain body
The 21 chapters are the primary organogenesis of the manuscript brain. They define the lawful body of the system before it is compiled into the appendicial infrastructure stack.
At the deepest resolution, the 21 chapters collapse into five super-organs:
[
\mathfrak{B}_{21}
\Sigma_{\mathrm{Id}};\bowtie;\Sigma_{\mathrm{Geo}};\bowtie;\Sigma_{\mathrm{Epi}};\bowtie;\Sigma_{\mathrm{Dev}};\bowtie;\Sigma_{\mathrm{Ops}}]
where:
(\Sigma_{\mathrm{Id}}) is the identity and memory engine,
(\Sigma_{\mathrm{Geo}}) is the coordinate and motion engine,
(\Sigma_{\mathrm{Epi}}) is the epistemic and governance membrane,
(\Sigma_{\mathrm{Dev}}) is the development and embodiment engine,
(\Sigma_{\mathrm{Ops}}) is the live operational habitat.
1. Identity and memory engine
The first hidden organ of the chapter crystal is the identity engine. It spans the early foundations, zero-point logic, seed structures, replay, and whole-system continuity. Its deepest law is that anything real in the manuscript must admit lawful collapse and lawful reopening. A primitive object, a normalized query, a memory seed, a replay checkpoint, and a bootstrap kernel are all expressions of the same structural archetype.
This identity engine is not static. It supports continuity under change. A lawful patch does not simply replace old state with new state. It updates the lineage of a continuing object. A replay system does not merely restore bytes. It certifies that the restored structure is meaningfully the same thing. A memory seed does not merely compress content. It preserves the lawful path by which content becomes itself again.
Without this engine, the framework would have no deep selfhood. It would be a graph of changing artifacts without a coherent continuity principle.
2. Coordinate and motion engine
The next hidden organ is the coordinate and motion engine. It spans addressing, lenses, operator algebra, route grammars, bridge logic, translation, and retrieval.
This organ does two things simultaneously. It decides where things are, and it decides how things move.
Addressing makes every artifact findable.Lensing makes every artifact viewable from multiple lawful projections.Operators make transformations typed.Routes make complex transitions composable.Bridges make distant or cross-domain moves possible.Translation makes one domain navigable from another.Retrieval becomes no longer “search,” but the lawful assembly of support through explicit motion.
At this level, the manuscript brain behaves less like a document system and more like a dynamic manifold. Solving a problem means selecting a path through explicit coordinate space. This is why the framework’s claim to replace hidden neural weights is not metaphorical: it substitutes them with explicit weighted route geometry, hidden-hub transfer lines, operator families, and mission-shaped motion laws.
3. Epistemic and governance membrane
The third hidden organ is the membrane that decides what is admissible. It spans answers, legality classes, witness systems, replay, self-model review, committee law, policy envelopes, and constitutional legitimacy.
This membrane is the true center of the whole architecture. The system is not organized around “generation” but around what may count as a lawful act, claim, patch, translation, or embodiment. That is why witness, legality, replay, certification, trust, consent, sandboxing, and policy all converge into one organ family.
Without this membrane, every other organ would become dangerous or noisy. Routes would move too freely. Patches would accumulate without legitimacy. Embodiment would overstep confidence. Federation would dissolve sovereignty. Futures planning would overclaim certainty. The membrane prevents that by requiring every major action to pass through explicit thresholds of support, permission, and review.
This is also why the system’s deep-time constitutional layer later becomes possible. Constitutional law is not alien to the manuscript brain. It is the long-timescale refinement of the same admissibility membrane already present in answer law, patch law, and policy law.
4. Development and embodiment engine
The fourth organ is the development engine. It includes patching, self-modeling, pedagogy, embodied feedback, curriculum growth, reinforcement, and long-horizon mission shaping.
Its deepest principle is that the system learns by lawful write-back. A failure, contradiction, or user misunderstanding is never just noise. It is a structured residual object. That residual can route into:
a patch packet,
a bridge downgrade,
a self-model blind-spot update,
a curriculum branch,
a new benchmark,
a policy tightening,
or a futures hedge.
Thus learning is not one hidden gradient. It is a family of explicit writes back into future routeability.
Embodiment is a key part of this engine because it externalizes the system’s own developmental reflexivity. Teaching another learner is structurally the same as self-repairing the atlas: assess state, identify residual, choose bounded intervention, observe outcome, adjust future bias.
That is why pedagogy and patching belong to one hidden organ, and why curriculum, user-state modeling, and reinforcement are not add-ons but natural continuations of the manuscript’s core developmental law.
5. Operational habitat
The fifth organ is the runtime habitat. It includes services, schedulers, agent roles, committees, synchronization, live persistence, and the always-on update loop.
This is where the manuscript ceases to be only structure and becomes operational life. The live brain:
accepts invocation packets,
runs routes,
constructs answers,
stages patches,
updates itself,
emits receipts,
logs replay,
and maintains its own hot and warm state.
The operational habitat also supports plurality. It does not force the whole system through one undifferentiated thread. It can host:
proof-minded services,
route services,
patch services,
committee review,
self-model observers,
embodied curriculum surfaces,
and later many sovereign or federated brains.
This means the runtime habitat is not only execution. It is the ecological substrate of lawful internal society.
III. The appendix crystal — the compiler, proof stack, and civilization stack
The core appendix crystal spans A–P, with Appendix Q functioning as the reflective quotient over that crystal. At the deepest resolution, the appendices collapse into four super-organs:
[
\mathfrak{A}_{A:P}

where:

(\Sigma_3) is the civilizational time engine.
1. Orientation and compiler organ
Appendices A–D establish the second-order beginning of the implementation stack.
Appendix A recovers hidden topological structure. It proves that the manuscript is organized by deeper nexus hubs rather than by chapter order alone.Appendix B turns the topology into executable routing.Appendix C defines the schema registry that gives those routes object grammar.Appendix D defines the execution kernel, validation harness, and certification path.
Together these appendices form the manuscript’s compiler organ: the part that turns architecture into an executable object system.
Their deepest hidden law is that mapping, grammar, and execution are one family. A system cannot be truly mapped unless its hidden organs are known. Those organs cannot be used unless their objects are typed. Those objects cannot live unless there is an executable kernel that moves through them. The first four appendices are therefore the formal descent from thought-space into build-space.
2. Proofed corpus-body organ
Appendices E–I turn the architecture into a real, persistent, living body.
Appendix E proves existence through a worked microcosm.Appendix F proves that a real corpus can be migrated into the architecture.Appendix G proves that the migration can be staged and executed as a lawful playbook.Appendix H provides the repository body and artifact substrate.Appendix I provides continuous proof that the live body remains the same lawful organism through time.
This cluster is not merely implementation detail. It is the existential proof-stack of the architecture. It answers three escalating questions:
can this architecture exist at all?
can it ingest a real archive rather than only toy examples?
can it remain itself after activation and change?
That is why Appendix E and Appendix I are a deep mirror pair: one proves being, the other proves continuing being.
3. Action, governance, and immunity shell
Appendices J–L define the live outer shell of the manuscript brain.
Appendix J defines how the system is addressed.Appendix K defines what those addresses are allowed to do.Appendix L defines how the whole shell resists poisoning, spoofing, capture, and drift.
Together they turn technical operability into lawful and resilient operability. Without J the brain is not externally addressable. Without K it is addressable but not safely governed. Without L it is governed but still vulnerable to corruption and hostile adaptation.
This shell is therefore the place where:
invocation,
policy,
consent,
sandboxing,
hardening,
and adversarial humilitycollapse into one organ.
4. Civilizational time engine
Appendices M–P define the long horizon of the system.
Appendix M allows many brains to federate without fusion.Appendix N gives that federation a sustainable commons economy.Appendix O allows the civilization to evolve its own law.Appendix P gives it deep-future navigation.
This means the appendicial stack does not stop at build and governance. It continues into civilizational time. It asks:
how many brains cooperate,
how shared goods are sustained,
how law changes,
how futures are chosen.
This is why the appendices are not postscript. They are the part of the whole corpus where a brain becomes a society and a society becomes historical.
IV. Why the beginning had to be rewritten last
The user’s deepest methodological insight is that the last becomes the first. A shallow title and abstract written before the full manuscript exists can only summarize guesses. A lawful front crystal must be written after the chapter crystal and appendix crystal have converged, because only then can the opening truly function as a seed of the whole.
The build order makes this precise:
[\text{Idea}\to\text{Research}\to\text{Deep Cross-Synthesis}\to\text{21-Chapter Skeleton}\to\text{21-Chapter Expansion}\to\text{Chapter Metro}\to\text{Appendix Expansion}\to\text{Appendix Metro}\to\text{Rewritten Front Crystal}]
The front crystal is therefore posterior in time but prior in function. It is written last so that it may become first lawfully.
This gives the title and abstract a different status from ordinary prefaces. They are not introductions written in advance. They are holographic recompressions of the completed stack.
Thus the system now contains three stand-alone crystals:
the front crystal, which seeds the whole,
the 21-chapter crystal, which defines the brain body,
the core appendix crystal A–P, which defines the build, proof, governance, federation, and future engine of that body.
Appendix Q then becomes the reflective closure that maps the appendix crystal itself and prepares the lawful next step: the full whole-stack metro quotient.

VI. Shortest whole-stack routes
Route (\rho_1): From raw archive to live civilization
[\Xi_3 \to \Xi_1 \to \Xi_2 \to \Xi_5 \to \Xi_6]Body (\to) routeability (\to) law (\to) live operation (\to) federation/civilization.
Route (\rho_2): From proof of existence to future navigation
[\Xi_0 \to \Xi_2 \to \Xi_5 \to \Xi_6]Identity/replay (\to) legitimacy (\to) active operation (\to) civilizational future.
Route (\rho_3): From residual to constitutional change
[\Xi_4 \to \Xi_2 \to \Xi_6]Developmental pressure (\to) admissibility membrane (\to) constitutional amendment and futures steering.
Route (\rho_4): From translation to federation
[\Xi_1 \to \Xi_2 \to \Xi_6]Cross-domain bridge (\to) law and policy (\to) treaty and commons order.
Route (\rho_5): From embodiment to civilization
[\Xi_5 \to \Xi_4 \to \Xi_6]Action shell (\to) pedagogy/reinforcement (\to) economic and constitutional scaling.
VII. Final whole-stack equation
The entire corpus now compresses into one civilizational meta-equation:
[
\boxed{
\mathfrak{W}
\text{Replayable Identity};+;\text{Explicit Coordinate Motion};+;\text{Witnessed Admissibility};+;\text{Custodied Corpus Body};+;\text{Lawful Development};+;\text{Plural Runtime Action};+;\text{Federated Civilizational Time}}]
or, dynamically,
[\boxed{\text{seed}\to\text{route}\to\text{witness}\to\text{memory}\to\text{patch}\to\text{self-model}\to\text{runtime}\to\text{embodiment}\to\text{federation}\to\text{commons}\to\text{constitution}\to\text{future}}]
That is the metro map now written at the end exactly because it was first truly discovered only after the whole manuscript had already been built. The beginning becomes the end, and the end becomes the lawful seed of the beginning.
METRO MAP — WHOLE-STACK HOLOGRAPHIC INDEX
The docs clearly define the control cadence and the promotion / rollback laws, but they do not define one concrete Python orchestrator API. So this module is the missing engineering layer: it turns the continuous ingest path, nightly SFT/SPIN/GRPO/tool-negative blocks, hourly κ-distill, every-500-episode CUT proposals, and weekly promote/quarantine review into one control loop while keeping truth verdicts owned by the verifier rather than the scheduler. That division is the most faithful synthesis of the route-packet docs, CUT cadence, PatternStore thresholds, and witness/replay law.
trainer_orchestrator.py
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass, field
from pathlib import Path
from time import time
from typing import Any, Dict, Iterable, List, Optional, Protocol, Sequence, runtime_checkable
from config_schema import TrainConfig, load_train_config
from pattern_store import PatternPetal, PatternStore
from kappa_distill import KappaDistiller, DistillOutcome
from parallel_scheduler import (
ComputeLayout,
ParallelScheduler,
SchedulerDecision,
SchedulerObservation,
)
from route_packet_dataset import (
RoutePacketDataset,
RoutePacketSample,
RoutePacketStore,
CandidateRecord,
EvidenceRecord,
WitnessRecord,
PatchRecord,
ActionTraceRecord,
)
from verifier import (
Verifier,
RoutePacket as VerifierRoutePacket,
CandidateAtom as VerifierCandidateAtom,
TruthLattice,
WitnessBundle,
PatchDecision,

@runtime_checkable
class TrainBackend(Protocol):
"""
Minimal backend surface needed by the orchestrator.
The docs define the loops and cadence, but not a single concrete trainer API.
This protocol is the missing implementation seam.
"""
def configure_phase(self, phase: str) -> None:
...
def run_phase(
self,
phase: str,
dataset: RoutePacketDataset,
max_steps: int,
) -> Dict[str, Any]:
...
def save_checkpoint(self, tag: str) -> str:
...
def load_checkpoint(self, checkpoint_ref: str) -> None:
...
def apply_layout(self, layout: ComputeLayout) -> None:
...
def evaluate_layout(
self,
layout: ComputeLayout,
episodes_window: int = 32,
) -> SchedulerObservation:
...
def replay_audit(self, packets: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
...
# Optional hooks; accessed with hasattr/getattr.
# def weekly_eval(self, packets: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> Dict[str, Any]: ...
# def offline_core_recenter(self) -> Dict[str, Any]: ...
@dataclass
class IngestReport:
packet_id: str
verdict: str
patch_action: str
appended_exception: bool
operator_mix: Dict[str, float]
notes: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class HourlyReport:
distill_outcomes: List[DistillOutcome]
quiet_decay_shelves: List[str]
log_budget_mb: int
@dataclass
class SchedulerHookReport:
proposal_made: bool
accepted: bool
rollback: bool
proposal_reason: Optional[str] = None
theorem_row: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
negative_proof: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
current_layout: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
@dataclass
class NightlyReport:
nightly_plan: List[str]
sft: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
spin: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
grpo: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
tool_negatives: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
patch_board: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
replay_audit: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
promote_ready_petals: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
@dataclass
class WeeklyReport:
weekly_plan: List[str]
patch_board: Dict[str, Any]
replay_audit: Dict[str, Any]
weekly_eval: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
offline_core_recenter: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None
promote_ready_petals: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
class NoOpBackend:
"""
Reference stub so the orchestrator can be exercised without a real trainer.
"""
def configure_phase(self, phase: str) -> None:
self.phase = phase
def run_phase(self, phase: str, dataset: RoutePacketDataset, max_steps: int) -> Dict[str, Any]:
return {
"phase": phase,
"seen_samples": len(dataset),
"max_steps": max_steps,
"status": "noop",
}
def save_checkpoint(self, tag: str) -> str:
return f"ckpt://{tag}"
def load_checkpoint(self, checkpoint_ref: str) -> None:
self.last_loaded_checkpoint = checkpoint_ref
def apply_layout(self, layout: ComputeLayout) -> None:
self.layout = layout
def evaluate_layout(self, layout: ComputeLayout, episodes_window: int = 32) -> SchedulerObservation:
# Simple mock: scaling workers helps slightly unless absurd.
base_proofs = 1000
proofs = int(base_proofs * min(layout.worker_count, 4) * (1.02 if layout.transport_mode == "async" else 1.0))
cost = 1.0 + 0.6 * max(layout.worker_count - 1, 0)
return SchedulerObservation(
episodes_seen=episodes_window,
proofs_completed=proofs,
wall_time_seconds=3600.0,
gpu_dollars=cost,
watt_hours=500.0 * layout.worker_count,
ram_gib_hours=12.0 * layout.worker_count,
vram_util=min(0.95, 0.25 * layout.worker_count),
divergent_kernel_fraction=0.02,
idle_kernel_fraction=0.03,
hot_shelf_ids=["root.route"],
)
def replay_audit(self, packets: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
ok = 0
for packet in packets:
if packet.witness is not None and packet.witness.replay_verified:
ok += 1
return {
"audited": len(packets),
"replay_verified": ok,
"replay_success_rate": ok / max(len(packets), 1),
}
def weekly_eval(self, packets: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
return {
"weekly_eval_packets": len(packets),
"status": "noop",
}
def offline_core_recenter(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
return {"status": "skipped/noop"}
class TrainerOrchestrator:
"""
One executable control loop for the whole Athenachka 2.0 training cadence.
Owns:
- continuous ingest / verification / exception append
- hourly κ-distill
- every-500-episode CUT proposal + accept/rollback
- nightly SFT / SPIN / GRPO / tool-negative blocks
- weekly promote/quarantine review and replay audit
"""
def __init__(
self,
cfg: TrainConfig,
backend: TrainBackend,
packet_store: Optional[RoutePacketStore] = None,
pattern_store: Optional[PatternStore] = None,
verifier: Optional[Verifier] = None,
scheduler: Optional[ParallelScheduler] = None,
distiller: Optional[KappaDistiller] = None,
) -> None:
self.cfg = cfg
self.backend = backend
self.packet_store = packet_store or RoutePacketStore(cfg)
self.pattern_store = pattern_store or PatternStore(cfg)
self.verifier = verifier or Verifier(cfg)
self.scheduler = scheduler or ParallelScheduler(cfg, self.pattern_store)
self.distiller = distiller or KappaDistiller(cfg, self.pattern_store)
self.current_layout = ComputeLayout(
worker_count=1,
precision_mode=cfg.precision.train_dtype,
transport_mode="sync",
batch_size=cfg.batching.sft_per_device_train_batch_size,
fused_kernel_count=0,
notes=["bootstrap layout"],
)
self.current_checkpoint_ref: Optional[str] = None
self.last_quiet_maintenance_ts = time()
self._ensure_root_petal()
def _ensure_root_petal(self) -> None:
if "root.route" not in self.pattern_store.petals:
self.pattern_store.register_petal(
PatternPetal(
petal_id="root.route",
depth=0,
pq_block_ref="pq://root.route",
topology_hash="topo:root.route",
seed_hash="seed:root.route",
)
)
def _sample_to_verifier_packet(self, sample: RoutePacketSample) -> VerifierRoutePacket:
evidence_quality = 0.0
if sample.evidence:
evidence_quality = sum(e.confidence for e in sample.evidence) / len(sample.evidence)
replay_ok = False if sample.witness is None else bool(sample.witness.replay_verified)
patch_risk = 1.0 if sample.patch is None else float(sample.patch.patch_risk)
stable_epochs = 0 if sample.patch is None else int(sample.patch.stable_epochs)
return VerifierRoutePacket(
packet_id=sample.packet_id,
mode=sample.mode,
task_class=sample.task_class,
candidates=[
VerifierCandidateAtom(
candidate_id=c.candidate_id,
payload_ref=c.payload_ref,
score=c.score,
uncertainty=c.uncertainty,
contradiction_risk=c.contradiction_risk,
admissible=c.admissible,
provenance=c.provenance,
)
for c in sample.candidate_routes
],
evidence_quality=evidence_quality,
replay_ok=replay_ok,
patch_risk=patch_risk,
stable_epochs=stable_epochs,
metadata=sample.metadata,
)
def _sync_witness(self, sample: RoutePacketSample, witness: WitnessBundle) -> None:
sample.witness = WitnessRecord(
verdict=witness.verdict.value,
residual_ledger=list(witness.residual_ledger),
tri_lock_defects=dict(witness.tri_lock_defects),
candidate_set=list(witness.candidate_set),
evidence_plan=list(witness.evidence_plan),
obstruction_certificate=witness.obstruction_certificate,
replay_required=witness.replay_required,
replay_verified=witness.replay_verified,
seal=witness.seal,
)
def _sync_patch_decision(self, sample: RoutePacketSample, decision: PatchDecision) -> None:
if sample.patch is None:
sample.patch = PatchRecord(
patch_id=f"patch://{sample.packet_id}",
patch_risk=1.0,
stable_epochs=0,
)
sample.patch.promoted = decision.action == "PROMOTE"
sample.patch.held = decision.action == "HOLD"
sample.patch.quarantined = decision.action == "QUARANTINE"
def _maybe_append_exception(self, sample: RoutePacketSample, witness: WitnessBundle, epoch: int) -> bool:
if witness.verdict == TruthLattice.OK:
return False
evidence_quality = 0.0
if sample.evidence:
evidence_quality = sum(e.confidence for e in sample.evidence) / len(sample.evidence)
self.pattern_store.append_exception(
petal_id="root.route",
morton_id=epoch,
epoch=epoch,
delta_ref=f"delta://{sample.packet_id}",
certificate_ref=f"witness://{sample.packet_id}",
entropy_bits=max(0.01, 1.0 - evidence_quality),
)
return True
def continuous_ingest(self, sample: RoutePacketSample, epoch: int = 0) -> IngestReport:
vpacket = self._sample_to_verifier_packet(sample)
witness = self.verifier.verify_packet(vpacket)
decision = self.verifier.decide_patch(vpacket, witness)
self._sync_witness(sample, witness)
self._sync_patch_decision(sample, decision)
appended = self._maybe_append_exception(sample, witness, epoch)
self.packet_store.ingest(sample)
mix = self.scheduler.schedule_mix(vpacket, witness)
return IngestReport(
packet_id=sample.packet_id,
verdict=witness.verdict.value,
patch_action=decision.action,
appended_exception=appended,
operator_mix={
"D": mix.D,
"Omega": mix.Omega,
"Sigma": mix.Sigma,
"Psi": mix.Psi,
},
notes=[
f"patch_reason={decision.reason}",
f"store_summary={self.packet_store.summary()}",
],
)
def hourly_maintenance(self, nvme_free_gb: float = 10.0, now_ts: Optional[float] = None) -> HourlyReport:
outcomes = self.distiller.hourly_pass(nvme_free_gb=nvme_free_gb)
quiet_decay_shelves: List[str] = []
now_ts = now_ts or time()
interval_seconds = self.cfg.cadence.quiet_shelf_maintenance_every_hours * 3600
if now_ts - self.last_quiet_maintenance_ts >= interval_seconds:
quiet_decay_shelves = self.distiller.quiet_shelf_maintenance(now_ts=now_ts)
self.last_quiet_maintenance_ts = now_ts
return HourlyReport(
distill_outcomes=outcomes,
quiet_decay_shelves=quiet_decay_shelves,
log_budget_mb=self.distiller.current_log_budget(),
)
def on_episode_end(self, obs: SchedulerObservation) -> SchedulerHookReport:
self.scheduler.record_observation(obs, self.current_layout)
proposal = self.scheduler.suggest_move(obs, self.current_layout)
if proposal is None:
return SchedulerHookReport(
proposal_made=False,
accepted=False,
rollback=False,
current_layout=self.current_layout.__dict__,
)
checkpoint_ref = self.backend.save_checkpoint(f"pre-proposal-{obs.episodes_seen}")
self.backend.apply_layout(proposal.to_layout)
shadow_obs = self.backend.evaluate_layout(
proposal.to_layout,
episodes_window=self.cfg.scheduler.eta_saturation_window,
)
decision = self.scheduler.evaluate_proposal(proposal, old_obs=obs, new_obs=shadow_obs)
if decision.accepted and not decision.rollback:
self.current_layout = proposal.to_layout
self.current_checkpoint_ref = checkpoint_ref
else:
self.backend.load_checkpoint(checkpoint_ref)
return SchedulerHookReport(
proposal_made=True,
accepted=decision.accepted,
rollback=decision.rollback,
proposal_reason=proposal.reason,
theorem_row=decision.theorem_row,
negative_proof=decision.negative_proof,
current_layout=self.current_layout.__dict__,
)
def _make_dataset(self, samples: Sequence[RoutePacketSample]) -> RoutePacketDataset:
return RoutePacketDataset(samples)
def promotion_board(self, limit: Optional[int] = None) -> Dict[str, Any]:
samples = self.packet_store.build_patch_review_corpus(limit=limit)
promote = hold = quarantine = 0
rows: List[Dict[str, Any]] = []
for sample in samples:
vpacket = self._sample_to_verifier_packet(sample)
witness = self.verifier.verify_packet(vpacket)
decision = self.verifier.decide_patch(vpacket, witness)
self._sync_witness(sample, witness)
self._sync_patch_decision(sample, decision)
if decision.action == "PROMOTE":
promote += 1
elif decision.action == "HOLD":
hold += 1
else:
quarantine += 1
rows.append(
{
"packet_id": sample.packet_id,
"verdict": witness.verdict.value,
"decision": decision.action,
"reason": decision.reason,
}
)
return {
"reviewed": len(samples),
"promote": promote,
"hold": hold,
"quarantine": quarantine,
"rows": rows,
}
def nightly_cycle(self) -> NightlyReport:
plan = [
"stage_a_sft" if self.cfg.loops.stage_a_sft_enabled else None,
"stage_b_spin_selfplay" if self.cfg.loops.stage_b_spin_enabled else None,
"stage_c_grpo_budget" if self.cfg.loops.stage_c_grpo_enabled else None,
"stage_d_tool_negative_mining" if self.cfg.loops.stage_d_tool_negative_enabled else None,
"patch_promotion_board",
"replay_audit",
]
plan = [p for p in plan if p is not None]
report = NightlyReport(nightly_plan=plan)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_a_sft_enabled:
sft_samples = self.packet_store.build_teacher_forced_corpus(
limit=self.cfg.loops.stage_a_max_steps_per_day
)
self.backend.configure_phase("sft")
report.sft = self.backend.run_phase(
"sft",
self._make_dataset(sft_samples),
self.cfg.loops.stage_a_max_steps_per_day,
)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_b_spin_enabled:
spin_samples = self.packet_store.build_spin_corpus(
limit=self.cfg.loops.stage_b_max_steps_per_day
)
self.backend.configure_phase("spin_selfplay")
report.spin = self.backend.run_phase(
"spin_selfplay",
self._make_dataset(spin_samples),
self.cfg.loops.stage_b_max_steps_per_day,
)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_c_grpo_enabled:
grpo_samples = self.packet_store.build_grpo_corpus(
limit=self.cfg.loops.stage_c_max_steps_per_day
)
self.backend.configure_phase("grpo_scheduler")
report.grpo = self.backend.run_phase(
"grpo_scheduler",
self._make_dataset(grpo_samples),
self.cfg.loops.stage_c_max_steps_per_day,
)
if self.cfg.loops.stage_d_tool_negative_enabled:
tool_samples = self.packet_store.build_tool_negative_corpus(
limit=self.cfg.loops.stage_d_max_steps_per_day
)
self.backend.configure_phase("tool_negative")
report.tool_negatives = self.backend.run_phase(
"tool_negative",
self._make_dataset(tool_samples),
self.cfg.loops.stage_d_max_steps_per_day,
)
report.patch_board = self.promotion_board(limit=self.cfg.replay_buffers.patch_candidates_hold)
audit_packets = self.packet_store.verified_ok.latest(self.cfg.replay_buffers.replay_audit_window)
report.replay_audit = self.backend.replay_audit(audit_packets)
report.promote_ready_petals = self.distiller.promotion_ready_petals()
return report
def _should_offline_recenter(self) -> bool:
"""
Recommended heuristic, not canon:
only justify heavy substrate work when promotions are scarce and
negative proofs have accumulated.
"""
hold_count = len(self.packet_store.patch_candidates_hold)
neg_proofs = len(self.scheduler.negative_proof_rows())
return hold_count > 100 and neg_proofs > 10 and len(self.distiller.promotion_ready_petals()) == 0
def weekly_cycle(self) -> WeeklyReport:
plan = [
"weekly_eval",
"promote_or_quarantine_review",
"optional_offline_core_recenter_if_justified",
]
patch_board = self.promotion_board(limit=self.cfg.replay_buffers.patch_candidates_hold)
audit_packets = self.packet_store.verified_ok.latest(self.cfg.replay_buffers.replay_audit_window)
replay_audit = self.backend.replay_audit(audit_packets)
weekly_eval = None
if hasattr(self.backend, "weekly_eval"):
weekly_eval = getattr(self.backend, "weekly_eval")(audit_packets)
offline_core_recenter = None
if self._should_offline_recenter() and hasattr(self.backend, "offline_core_recenter"):
offline_core_recenter = getattr(self.backend, "offline_core_recenter")()
return WeeklyReport(
weekly_plan=plan,
patch_board=patch_board,
replay_audit=replay_audit,
weekly_eval=weekly_eval,
offline_core_recenter=offline_core_recenter,
promote_ready_petals=self.distiller.promotion_ready_petals(),
)
def demo_sample(packet_id: str) -> RoutePacketSample:
return RoutePacketSample(
packet_id=packet_id,
created_at="2026-03-08T00:00:00Z",
source_atlas="atlas.demo",
task_class="route_compile",
mode="ROUTE",
query={
"raw_input": "Construct the smallest admissible route.",
"canonical_problem": "Compile a lawful route, verify it, and preserve replay identity.",
"budget": {"tokens": 4096, "tool_calls_max": 2},
},
lens_init={
"Square": 0.30,
"Flower": 0.20,
"Cloud": 0.25,
"Fractal": 0.25,
},
invariant_carriers={"text": "carrier://text/demo"},
candidate_routes=[
CandidateRecord(
candidate_id="cand.1",
payload_ref="route://cand.1",
score=0.82,
uncertainty=0.18,
contradiction_risk=0.12,
admissible=True,
provenance=["planner.greedy"],
),
CandidateRecord(
candidate_id="cand.2",
payload_ref="route://cand.2",
score=0.77,
uncertainty=0.24,
contradiction_risk=0.22,
admissible=True,
provenance=["planner.greedy"],
),
],
evidence=[
EvidenceRecord(
modality="text",
summary="Found direct support in route neighborhood.",
regions_or_spans=["Ch07.C2.b"],
confidence=0.78,
)
],
patch=PatchRecord(
patch_id=f"patch://{packet_id}",
patch_risk=0.18,
stable_epochs=3,

),

tool_trace_ids=[],
